واحتجوا كذلك: ۱. بما روي عن أبي موسى الأشعري؛ أن رَسُول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم توضأ ومسح على الجوربين والنعلين. رَوَاهُ: ابن ماجه، والطحاوي، والبيهقي. ويجاب عَنْهُ: بأنه ضعيف؛ لأن في سنده عيسى بن سنان الحنفي، وفيه مقال، ثُمَّ إن أبا داود قَدْ حكم عَلَى هَذَا الْحَدِيث بالانقطاع، وبين البيهقي هَذَا الانقطاع وَهُوَ أن الضحاك بن عَبْد الرَّحْمن لم يثبت سماعه من أبي موسى. واحتجوا بما ورد عن راشد بن سعد، عن ثوبان: قَالَ: بعث رَسُول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم سرية فأصابهم البرد فلما قدموا عَلَى النَّبِي ل شكوا إِلَيْهِ ما أصابهم من البرد فأمرهم أن يمسحوا على العصائب والتساخين. أخرجه الإمام أحمد، وأبو داود، والطبراني، وأبو عبيد، والحاكم، والبيهقي، والبغوي. قَالَ الْحَاكِم: «هَذَا حَدِيث صَحِيح عَلَى شرط مُسْلِم). وتعقبه الذهبي في السير بقوله: «خطأ فإن الشيخين ما احتجا براشد، ولا ثور من شرط مسلم». إلا أن الذهبي أورد الْحَدِيث من طريق أبي داود وَقَالَ: «إسناده قوي». لَكِنْ أعلَّ بعض أهل العلم هَذَا الْحَدِيث بالانقطاع فَقَدْ قَالَ ابن أبي حاتم: «أنبأنا بن أحمد بن حَنْبَل فيما كتب إليَّ قَالَ: قَالَ أحمد - يعني ابن حَنْبَل -: راشد ابن سعد لَمْ يَسْمَع من ثوبان». وَقَالَ الحافظ ابن حجر: «قَالَ أبو حاتم والحربي لَمْ يَسْمَع من ثوبان، وَقَالَ عبد الله بن أحمد: سألت أبي عن راشد بن سعد، فقال: ثقة، ولكن ليس له سماع من ثوبان. فائدة: هنا مسألة ينبغي التنبيه عَلَيْهَا، وَهِيَ: ما شاع وانتشر بَيْنَ الباحثين عِنْدَ نقلهم عن الْحَاكِم تصحيحه لحديث من كتاب المستدرك: صححه الحاكم ووافقه الذهبي» وهذه مسألة لم تكن معروفة عند المتقدمين بَلْ شهرها ونشرها علامة مصر ومحدّثها الشيخ أحمد شاكر – يرحمه الله -، ثُمَّ طفحت بِهَا كتب الشيخ مُحَمَّد ناصر الدين الألباني، والشيخ شعيب الأرناؤوط، حَتَّى عمت عِنْدَ أغلب الباحثين. وهذا خطأ ينبغي التنبيه عَلَيْهِ والتحذير مِنْهُ؛ لأن الإمام الذهبي لم يحقق "المستدرك"، بل اختصره عدداً كَمَا اختصر من الكتب، وَكَانَ من صنيع هَذَا الإمام العظيم أن يعلق أحياناً على بعض الأحاديث لا أنه يريد تحقيقها والحكم عَلَيْهَا وتتبعها جميعها وذلك لأن الذهبي ضعف كثيراً من الأحاديث الَّتِي في "المستدرك" في كتبه الأخرى كـ " الميزان " وغيره. ثُمَّ إنه نص على أن الكتاب يعوزه تحرير وعمل. (السير (١٧٦/١٧) فلو أنه وافق الْحَاكِم عَلَى ما سكت عَلَيْهِ جميع لما قَالَ ذَلِكَ. وهذا دليل من مئات بَلْ ألوف من الأدلة عَلَى أن أحكام " التلخيص " بشأن الأحاديث ليس كلام الذهبي بَلْ هُوَ كلام الْحَاكِم اختصره الذهبي فإن هَذَا الْحَدِيث في " التلخيص " ١٦٩/١: عَلَى شرط م» وفي السير ما يخالف هَذَا الحكم.
And they also argued with: 1. What was narrated from Abu Musa al-Ash'ari: that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) performed wudu and wiped over the socks and sandals. Narrated by Ibn Majah, al-Tahawi, and al-Bayhaqi. And it is responded: that it is weak because in its chain is 'Isa ibn Sinan al-Hanafi, and there is criticism of him. Then Abu Dawud ruled this hadith as disconnected, and al-Bayhaqi explained this disconnection: that al-Dahhak ibn Abd al-Rahman's hearing from Abu Musa is not established. And they argued with what was reported from Rashid ibn Sa'd, from Thawban: he said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) sent a military detachment, and cold afflicted them. When they came to the Prophet, they complained to him of what cold had afflicted them, so he ordered them to wipe over the headbands and the thick socks. Narrated by Ahmad, Abu Dawud, al-Tabarani, Abu 'Ubayd, al-Hakim, al-Bayhaqi, and al-Baghawi. Al-Hakim said: "This hadith is sahih according to the condition of Muslim." Al-Dhahabi criticized him in al-Siyar saying: "Mistake, for the two shaykhs did not use Rashid nor Thawr as a condition of Muslim." However, al-Dhahabi narrated the hadith via Abu Dawud and said: "Its chain is strong." But some scholars declared this hadith defective due to disconnection. Ibn Abi Hatim said: "Ibn Ahmad ibn Hanbal informed us in writing: Ahmad ibn Hanbal said: Rashid ibn Sa'd did not hear from Thawban." And al-Hafiz Ibn Hajar said: "Abu Hatim and al-Harbi said he did not hear from Thawban, and Abd Allah ibn Ahmad said: I asked my father about Rashid ibn Sa'd, and he said: trustworthy, but he has no hearing from Thawban." Benefit: There is an issue that should be noted: what has become widespread among researchers when quoting al-Hakim's authentication of a hadith from al-Mustadrak: "Al-Hakim authenticated it and al-Dhahabi agreed." This issue was not known among the early scholars; rather, it was publicized and spread by the scholar of Egypt and its muhaddith, Shaykh Ahmad Shakir – may Allah have mercy on him – then it overflowed in the books of Shaykh Muhammad Nasir al-Din al-Albani and Shaykh Shu'ayb al-Arna'ut, until it became common among most researchers. This is a mistake that should be noted and warned against; because Imam al-Dhahabi did not verify al-Mustadrak, rather he abbreviated it as he abbreviated other books, and it was the practice of this great Imam to sometimes comment on some hadiths, not that he intended to verify them and judge them and trace all of them. This is because al-Dhahabi weakened many hadiths that are in al-Mustadrak in his other books like al-Mizan and others. Then he stated that the book lacks editing and work. (al-Siyar 17/176) For if he agreed with al-Hakim on everything he kept silent about, he would not have said that. This is evidence from hundreds, rather thousands, of proofs that the rulings of al-Talkhis regarding hadith are not the words of al-Dhahabi, rather they are the words of al-Hakim that al-Dhahabi summarized. For this hadith in al-Talkhis 1/169: "on the condition of M" and in al-Siyar something contradicting this ruling.
Source pages p. 119

Commentary
This passage is an usul dispute: the author presents two hadiths used as evidence for wiping over non-leather foot coverings (socks), then critiques their chains from a Hanafi perspective. The first hadith from Abu Musa is rejected because it contains a weak narrator, 'Isa ibn Sinan al-Hanafi, and is disconnected (munqati') because al-Dahhak did not hear from Abu Musa. The second hadith from Thawban is more vigorously discussed: although al-Hakim declared it sahih on Muslim's condition, al-Dhahabi objected that Muslim did not use Rashid ibn Sa'd or Thawr (another narrator). Ibn Hanbal, Abu Hatim, and others state that Rashid ibn Sa'd did not hear from Thawban, making the chain mursal (disconnected at the Companion level). The author then includes a valuable methodological warning: the common claim 'al-Hakim authenticated it and al-Dhahabi agreed' is often false. Al-Dhahabi did not systematically verify al-Mustadrak; his summaries in al-Talkhis are not his independent rulings but extracts of al-Hakim's words. This clarifies that trusting such claims without checking al-Dhahabi's original verdicts in al-Siyar or al-Mizan is a serious error. Overall, the passage demonstrates how chain criticism (al-jarh wa al-ta'dil) directly determines fiqh rulings: weak chains cannot support a legal obligation like wiping over socks.

Key Terms
الجوربين (al-jawrabain): Non-leather socks worn on the feet, distinct from khuff (leather socks).
التساخين (al-tasakhin): Thick socks or foot coverings worn for warmth.
الانقطاع (al-inqita'): A defect in hadith where the chain disconnects, e.g., a narrator did not hear from the one he claims to narrate from.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) The chain is disconnected because Rashid ibn Sa'd did not hear from Thawban.
C) The hadith contradicts the Quran and Sunnah.
D) The hadith is mawdu' (fabricated).

Key Takeaway
Chain defects, especially discontinuity (inqita') and weakness of narrators, render a hadith invalid as proof for a fiqh ruling in the Hanafi school.

Chain Dispute over Hadith of Wiping over Socks
Critique and defense of the hadith chain for wiping over socks

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to analyze the chain dispute surrounding the hadith of wiping over socks and evaluate adh-Dhahabi's actual position by distinguishing his abridgment (al-Talkhis) from his own verification in as-Siyar.

Core Idea
Adh-Dhahabi's agreement in al-Talkhis is not his own view; his actual critique appears in as-Siyar.

This lesson explores a classic hadith chain dispute regarding the permissibility of wiping over socks. The passage presents al-Hakim’s authentication, adh-Dhahabi’s subsequent critique, and a claim of disconnection, followed by al-Bukhari’s confirmation. More importantly, it corrects a widespread methodological error: attributing adh-Dhahabi’s abridgment (al-Talkhis) as his own verification. Understanding this distinction is crucial for proper hadith criticism and usul al-fiqh analysis.

Guided Path
1
Identify the chain dispute
Read the passage to identify the competing claims: al-Hakim’s authentication on Muslim’s condition, adh-Dhahabi’s initial objection (mentioning Rashid and Thawr), and then adh-Dhahabi’s later statement that the chain is strong via Abu Dawud.
Note how a single narrator’s reliability determines the chain’s strength.
2
Trace the claim of disconnection
Find the argument that the hadith is munqati' (disconnected) because Rashid ibn Sa'd allegedly did not hear from Thawban. Note the sources: Ibn Abi Hatim, Ahmad ibn Hanbal, and Ibn Hajar.
The key issue is samā' (hearing) between narrators.
3
Analyze the rebuttal using al-Bukhari
Observe that al-Bukhari confirmed the hearing (sami'a Thawban). This counters the disconnection claim. Evaluate the strength of this rebuttal given al-Bukhari’s authority.
Al-Bukhari’s statement is a direct refutation of the claim.
4
Understand the methodological error about al-Talkhis
Read the fā'idah carefully. The common error is to think that adh-Dhahabi’s agreement in al-Talkhis (an abridgment) represents his own verification. In fact, al-Talkhis merely reproduces al-Hakim’s words. Adh-Dhahabi’s actual position is found in as-Siyar.
This illustrates the importance of referring to the original source, not abbreviated versions.
5
Apply the lesson to modern research
Recognize that many contemporary researchers (e.g., Ahmad Shakir, al-Albani, al-Arna'ut) fell into this error. As a critical scholar, you must verify claims by returning to the earliest sources.
This is a cautionary tale about relying on secondary abridgments.

الفصل الأول الاختلاف في السند
قَالَ الْحَاكِم: «هَذَا حَدِيث صَحِيح عَلَى شرط مُسْلِم». وتعقبه الذهبي في السير بقوله: «خطأ فإن الشيخين ما احتجا براشد، ولا ثور من شرط مسلم». إلا أن الذهبي أورد الْحَدِيث من طريق أبي داود وَقَالَ: «إسناده قوي». لَكِنْ أعلَّ بعض أهل العلم هَذَا الْحَدِيث بالانقطاع فَقَدْ قَالَ ابن أبي حاتم: «أنبأنا بن أحمد بن حَنْبَل فيما كتب إليَّ قَالَ: قَالَ أحمد - يعني ابن حَنْبَل -: راشد ابن سعد لَمْ يَسْمَع من ثوبان». وَقَالَ الحافظ ابن حجر: «قَالَ أبو حاتم والحربي لَمْ يَسْمَع من ثوبان، وَقَالَ الخلال عن أحمد: لا ينبغي أن يَكُون سَمِعَ مِنْهُ». لَكِنْ يجاب عن هَذَا الحكم بالانقطاع أن الإمام البخاري قَدْ أثبت سَمَاع راشد من ثوبان فَقَالَ: «سَمِعَ ثوبان». 
فائدة: هنا مسألة ينبغي التنبيه عَلَيْهَا، وَهِيَ: ما شاع وانتشر بَيْنَ الباحثين عِنْدَ نقلهم عن الْحَاكِم تصحيحه لحديث من كتاب المستدرك: «صححه الحاكم ووافقه الذهبي» وهذه مسألة لم تكن معروفة عند المتقدمين بَلْ شهرها ونشرها علامة مصر ومحدّثها الشيخ أحمد شاكر – يرحمه الله -، ثُمَّ طفحت بِهَا كتب الشيخ مُحَمَّد ناصر الدين الألباني، والشيخ شعيب الأرناؤوط، حَتَّى عمت عِنْدَ أغلب الباحثين. وهذا خطأ ينبغي التنبيه عَلَيْهِ والتحذير مِنْهُ؛ لأن الإمام الذهبي لم يحقق "المستدرك"، بل اختصره عدداً كَمَا اختصر من الكتب، وَكَانَ من صنيع هَذَا الإمام العظيم أن يعلق أحياناً على بعض الأحاديث لا أنه يريد تحقيقها والحكم عَلَيْهَا وتتبعها جميعها وذلك لأن الذهبي ضعف كثيراً من الأحاديث الَّتِي في "المستدرك" في كتبه الأخرى كـ " الميزان " وغيره. ثُمَّ إنه نص على أن الكتاب يعوزه تحرير وعمل. (السير (١٧٦/١٧ فلو أنه وافق الْحَاكِم عَلَى ما سكت عَلَيْهِ جميع لما قَالَ ذَلِكَ. وهذا دليل من مئات بَلْ ألوف من الأدلة عَلَى أن أحكام " التلخيص " بشأن الأحاديث ليس كلام الذهبي بَلْ هُوَ كلام الْحَاكِم اختصره الذهبي فإن هَذَا الْحَدِيث في " التلخيص " ١٦٩/١: عَلَى شرط م» وفي السير ما يخالف هَذَا الحكم. ومن خطأ الشيخ أحمد شاكر في هَذَا الْحَدِيث أنه قَالَ: «صححه عَلَى شرط مُسْلِم، ووافقه الذهبي» المسح على الجوربين.
Chapter One: Disagreement in the Chain. Al-Hakim said: "This hadith is authentic according to the condition of Muslim." Adh-Dhahabi followed up on it in as-Siyar saying: "Incorrect, for the two shaykhs did not use as evidence Rashid, nor Thawr from the condition of Muslim." However, adh-Dhahabi cited the hadith via the path of Abu Dawud and said: "Its chain is strong." But some scholars declared this hadith to be disconnected (munqati'). For Ibn Abi Hatim said: "Ibn Ahmad ibn Hanbal informed us in writing saying: Ahmad (i.e., Ibn Hanbal) said: Rashid ibn Sa'd did not hear from Thawban." And al-Hafiz Ibn Hajar said: "Abu Hatim and al-Harbi said he did not hear from Thawban, and al-Khallal related from Ahmad: 'It is not fitting that he heard from him.'" But it is responded to this ruling of disconnection that Imam al-Bukhari indeed confirmed that Rashid heard from Thawban, saying: "He heard from Thawban." Fā'idah: Here is a matter that should be noted, which is: what has become widespread among researchers when quoting al-Hakim's authentication of a hadith from al-Mustadrak: "Al-Hakim authenticated it and adh-Dhahabi agreed with him." This matter was not known among the early scholars; rather, the scholar of Egypt and its muhaddith, Shaykh Ahmad Shakir – may Allah have mercy on him – popularized and spread it, then the books of Shaykh Muhammad Nasir al-Din al-Albani and Shaykh Shu'ayb al-Arna'ut overflowed with it, until it became common among most researchers. This is an error that should be noted and warned against, because Imam adh-Dhahabi did not verify al-Mustadrak, rather he abridged it just as he abridged other books. It was the practice of this great imam to sometimes comment on some hadiths, not that he intended to verify them and rule on them and trace all of them. This is because adh-Dhahabi weakened many hadiths that are in al-Mustadrak in his other books like al-Mizan etc. Moreover, he stated that the book requires editing and work. (as-Siyar 17/176). For if he had agreed with al-Hakim on everything he remained silent about, he would not have said that. And this is evidence from hundreds, nay thousands, of proofs that the judgments of al-Talkhis regarding the hadiths are not adh-Dhahabi's words, rather they are al-Hakim's words which adh-Dhahabi abridged. For this hadith in al-Talkhis (1/169): "On the condition of M" while in as-Siyar there is something contradicting this judgment. And from the error of Shaykh Ahmad Shakir regarding this hadith is that he said: "He authenticated it on the condition of Muslim, and adh-Dhahabi agreed with him" – (al-Mash 'ala al-Jawrabayn, p.5).
Source pages p. 120

Commentary
This passage presents a detailed critique of the chain of a hadith regarding wiping over socks (al-mash 'ala al-jawrabayn). The author first cites al-Hakim's authentication, then adh-Dhahabi's objection, then another narration from adh-Dhahabi strengthening it, then the claim of disconnection (inqita') based on Ahmad ibn Hanbal's statement. The response uses al-Bukhari's confirmation of the hearing between Rashid and Thawban, thus rebutting the disconnection. Then a long note corrects a common misunderstanding: that adh-Dhahabi's agreement in al-Talkhis represents his final view. In fact, al-Talkhis is a mere abridgment of al-Hakim's words, and adh-Dhahabi's actual position is found in as-Siyar. This is a lesson in hadith criticism and the proper use of sources.

Key Terms
الاختلاف في السند (ikhtilāf fī al-sanad): Disagreement among scholars regarding the chain of narration of a hadith, its continuity, and the reliability of narrators.
انقطاع (inqiṭāʿ): A defect in the hadith chain where a narrator is missing or did not actually hear from the previous one, making the hadith munqati' (disconnected).
شرط مسلم (sharṭ Muslim): The criteria used by Imam Muslim in his Sahih for accepting narrators and chains, considered a high standard of authenticity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the main methodological error critiqued in the fā'idah of this passage?
A) Claiming that al-Hakim's authentication is unreliable
B) Claiming that adh-Dhahabi agreed with al-Hakim based on al-Talkhis
C) Claiming that the hadith is definitely authentic
D) Claiming that al-Bukhari's statement is weak

Key Takeaway
Always verify the source of a scholar's ruling: an abridgment may not reflect the abridger's own view.

The Hadith of Anas on Wiping over Socks: A Proof for the Hanafi School
Another proof for wiping over socks from Anas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to analyze the hadith of Anas for its legal implication, identify the Hanafi usul principle for using non-mutawatir hadith, and derive the ruling of wiping over socks.

Core Idea
Anas's hadith shows the Prophet wiped over socks with sandals, supporting the Hanafi permissibility of wiping over socks in general.

This lesson examines a hadith narrated by Anas ibn Malik that the Prophet wiped over socks while wearing sandals. The Hanafi school uses this as additional evidence for the permissibility of wiping over socks, addressing linguistic objections to other hadiths. We will analyze the hadith's chain and text to understand its legal force within Hanafi usul.

Guided Path
1
Identify the hadith and its narrator
Locate the hadith in the source text. Note the narrator (Anas ibn Malik) and the reporter (al-Khatib al-Baghdadi).
This hadith is a single narration (ahad) from a sahabi.
2
Classify the hadith by transmission strength
Determine if the hadith is mutawatir or ahad. In Hanafi usul, ahad hadith are accepted for practical rulings (furu') but not for essential beliefs.
This is an ahad hadith, so its thubut is zanni (speculative).
3
Analyze the text for legal implication
What action does the hadith describe? The Prophet wiped over socks while wearing sandals. Determine whether the sandals are a condition or merely descriptive.
The phrase 'upon them the sandals' is descriptive; it does not impose a condition.
4
Apply Hanafi istinbat principle
Apply the principle 'Fi'l al-nabi yufidu al-mashru'iyyah' (Prophet's action indicates permissibility). This yields the ruling that wiping over socks is permissible.
No evidence of prohibition, so the act remains permissible.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واحتجوا أيضاً بما روي عن أنس بن مالك، قَالَ: «رأيت رَسُوْلَ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم يمسح عَلَى الجوربين عليهما النعلان». أخرجه الْخَطِيب.
And they also used as proof what was narrated from Anas ibn Malik, who said: 'I saw the Messenger of Allah ﷺ wiping over socks with sandals over them.' Al-Khatib recorded it.
Source pages p. 120

Commentary
This hadith is cited as additional evidence for the permissibility of wiping over socks, specifically when sandals are worn over them. The chain is provided by al-Khatib al-Baghdadi. This supports the practice of wiping over socks, though the linguistic objection to the previous hadith may weaken its interpretation.

Key Terms
الجوربين (al-jawrabayn): Socks or stockings worn on the feet; the object of wiping in this hadith.
النعلان (an-naʿlān): Sandals, worn over the socks in the hadith narrated by Anas.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Anas ibn Malik
B) Thawban
C) Rashid ibn Sa'd
D) Abu Huraira

Key Takeaway
The hadith of Anas provides additional textual evidence for the Hanafi position on wiping over socks, and its analysis exemplifies the usul method of deriving rulings from a prophetic action.

Deriving the Condition for Wiping over Socks: Usul Analysis
Deriving the condition for wiping over socks

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi usul principle of qawl al-sahabi to derive the condition for socks to be equivalent to khuffs for wiping, based on the textual analysis of Anas's statement.

Core Idea
Anas's linguistic definition expands 'khuff' to any foot covering that prevents water.

In this lesson, we dissect the author's istidlal (derivation) regarding the permissibility of wiping over socks. The central piece of evidence is the action and explicit statement of the Companion Anas ibn Malik, who called woolen socks 'khuffs.' The author uses this to argue that the term 'khuff' is not restricted to leather, but the default ruling of washing feet limits the application to only thick socks. We will trace the usul reasoning step by step.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Prophetic evidence and its weakness
The author first examines a hadith about wiping over socks, noting its weak chain due to a narrator (Musa ibn Abdullah at-Tawil). This shows that not every narration is acceptable; chain criticism is essential.
This step establishes that the primary hadith is not reliable, so the author turns to companion evidence.
2
Examine the companion evidence
The author presents a sahih mauquf report from Anas ibn Malik who wiped over woolen socks and stated 'They are khuffs, but made of wool.' This is a companion's action and statement.
In Hanafi usul, the statement of a companion (qawl al-sahabi) is a source of legislation when not contradicted.
3
Analyze the linguistic derivation
Anas's statement 'innahuma khuffan' defines the socks as khuffs. The author argues that this expands the meaning of 'khuff' from its customary leather usage to any foot covering that prevents water. Anas was a linguistic authority before language mixing.
This is a linguistic tafsir (interpretation) of a shari term based on usage.
4
Evaluate the conditions proposed by scholars
Some scholars required additional conditions for equivalence: lining (tajlid), soling (tan'il), or thickness (safaqa). The author refutes the strict positions using Anas's general statement and cites Ibn Hazm's rejection of any conditions.
The author does not accept no conditions (Ibn Hazm) nor strict conditions (lining/soling), but adopts a middle position of thickness.
5
Determine the author's tarjih
The author inclines that thick socks (thakhin) are equivalent to khuffs, while thin socks are not. The ruling is based on the principle that deviation from the default (washing feet) requires strong evidence, and only thick socks meet the criterion of preventing water.
This tarjih aligns with the later Hanafi fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأجيب: بأن سند هذا الحديث تالف لأن فيه موسى بن عبد الله الطويل(۱)، قال ابن حبان: روى عن أنس أشياء موضوعة». وقال ابن عدي: «روى عن أنس مناكير، وهو مجهول»(۳). لكن روي مثل هذا الحديث من فعل أنس، فقد روى عبد الرزاق(۳)، وابن أبي شيبة(٤)، والدولابي(٥)، والبيهقي(٦)، عن الأزرق بن قيس(۷)، قال: رأيت أنس بن مالك أحدث فغسل وجهه ويديه ومسح على جوربين من صوف، فقلت: أتمسح عليهما؟ فقال : إنهما خفان، ولكنهما من صوف(۸). قال العلامة أحمد شاكر: «هذا إسناد صحيح(۹)، ثم قال: «هذا الحديث موقوف على أنس من فعله وقوله ولكن وجه الحجة فيه أنه لم يكتف بالفعل، بل صرح بأن الجوربين: «خفان، ولكنهما من صوف». وأنس بن مالك صحابي من أهل اللغة، قبل دخول العجمة واختلاط الألسنة، فهو يبين أن معنى (الخف) أعم من أن يكون من الجلد وحده، وأنه يشمل كل ما يستر القدم ويمنع وصول الماء إليها؛ إذ إن الخفاف كانت في الأغلب من الجلد، فأبان أنس أن هذا الغالب ليس حصراً للخف في أن يكون من الجلد. وأزال الوهم الذي قد يدخل على الناس من واقع الأمر في الخفاف إذ ذاك. ولم يأت دليل من الشارع يدل على حصر الخفاف في التي تكون من الجلد فقط. وهذا الفهم المستنبط من فعل أنس له فيه رد على من اشترط الصفاقة أو التجليد أو التنعيل للجوربين، وقد شدد ابن حزم النكير على من اشترط ذلك فقال: «إنه خطأ لا معنى له؛ لأنه لم يأت به قرآن ولا سنة ولا قياس ولا قول صاحب). وقد بوب ابن أبي شيبة في كتابه " المصنف(۲) باباً سماه: «من قال الجوربان بمنزلة الخفين ونقل في ذلك آثاراً عن ابن عمر وعطاء ونافع والحسن. ونستخلص مما تقدم بأن الأصل هو غسل الرجلين كما هو ظاهر القرآن والعدول عنه لا يجوز إلا بأحاديث صحيحة كأحاديث المسح على الخفين، لذا جاز عند جماهير أهل العلم العدول عن غسل الرجلين إلى المسح على الخفين، أما أحاديث المسح على الجوربين ففي صحتها كلام كما سبق، فكيف يعدل عن غسل القدمين إلى المسح على الجوربين مطلقاً، وإلى هذا الفهم ذهب الإمام مسلم بقوله: لا يترك ظاهر القرآن بمثل أبي قيس وهزيل» (۳). فلأجل هذا فإن عدداً من أهل العلم اشترطوا لجواز المسح على الجوربين قيوداً ليكونا في معنى الخفين، ويدخل الجوربان في معنى الخفين، فرأى بعضهم أن الجوربين إذا كانا مجلدين كانا في معنى الخفين ورأى بعضهم أنهما إذا كانا منعلين كانا في معناهما، وعند بعضهم أنهما إذا كانا صفيقين ثخينين كانا في معناهما (٤). والذي أميل إليه أن الجوربين إذا كانا ثخينين فهما في معنى الخفين يجوز المسح عليهما، أما إذا كانا رقيقين فهما ليسا في معنى الخفين، وفي جواز المسح عليهما تأمل، والله أعلم.
And it was answered: Indeed the chain of this hadith is corrupt because in it is Musa ibn Abdullah at-Tawil. Ibn Hibban said: 'He narrated from Anas fabricated things.' And Ibn Adi said: 'He narrated from Anas munkar (denounced) narrations, and he is unknown.' However, a similar hadith was narrated from the action of Anas, for Abd ar-Razzaq, Ibn Abi Shayba, ad-Dulabi, and al-Bayhaqi narrated from al-Azraq ibn Qays who said: I saw Anas ibn Malik relieve himself then wash his face and hands and wipe over two woolen socks, so I said: Do you wipe over them? He said: They are khuffs, but they are made of wool. Allamah Ahmad Shakir said: This chain is authentic. Then he said: This hadith is mauquf (stopped) on Anas by his action and statement, but the aspect of evidence in it is that he did not suffice with the action, but rather declared that the socks are 'khuffs, but made of wool.' And Anas ibn Malik is a companion from the people of the language, before the entry of foreignness and mixing of tongues. So he explains that the meaning of 'khuff' is more general than being of leather alone, and that it includes everything that covers the foot and prevents water from reaching it. For khuffs were mostly of leather, so Anas clarified that this majority is not a restriction of khuff to being of leather. And he removed the misconception that might enter people's minds from the actual situation of khuffs at that time. And no evidence came from the Lawgiver indicating restriction of khuffs to those made of leather only. And this understanding derived from Anas's action contains a refutation of those who stipulate thickness (safaqa), or lining (tajlid), or soling (tan'il) for the socks. And Ibn Hazm strongly rebuked those who stipulate that, saying: 'It is an error with no meaning; because neither Quran nor Sunnah nor qiyas nor saying of a companion has come with it.' And Ibn Abi Shayba dedicated a chapter in his Musannaf called: 'Whoever says the two socks are like the two khuffs' and he transmitted reports in that from Ibn Umar, Ata, Nafi, and al-Hasan. And we extract from what preceded that the original ruling is washing the feet as is apparent from the Quran, and deviation from it is not permissible except with authentic ahadith like the ahadith of wiping over khuffs. Hence the majority of scholars allowed deviation from washing the feet to wiping over khuffs. As for the ahadith of wiping over socks, their authenticity is debated as previously. So how could one deviate from washing the feet to wiping over socks absolutely? And Imam Muslim held this understanding with his saying: 'The apparent meaning of the Quran is not abandoned by the likes of Abu Qays and Huzayl.' For this reason, a number of scholars stipulated conditions for the permissibility of wiping over socks so that they are equivalent to khuffs. They considered socks to be subsumed under the meaning of khuffs. Some held that if the socks are lined (mujallad), they are equivalent to khuffs; some held that if they are soled (mun'al), they are equivalent; and some held that if they are thick (safiq thakhin), they are equivalent. And that which I incline towards is that if the socks are thick, they are equivalent to khuffs and wiping over them is permissible. As for thin socks, they are not equivalent to khuffs, and the permissibility of wiping over them is doubtful. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 122

Commentary
This passage is a textual analysis and istinbat (derivation of ruling) from evidence. The author begins by addressing a hadith with a weak chain regarding wiping over socks, identifying Musa ibn Abdullah at-Tawil as a weak narrator based on criticisms from Ibn Hibban and Ibn Adi. He then presents a counter-narrative from the action of Anas ibn Malik, which is reported through an authentic chain via al-Azraq ibn Qays. Anas wiped over woolen socks and explicitly stated they are khuffs, but made of wool, demonstrating that the term 'khuff' is not restricted to leather. The author highlights that Anas, as a linguistically authoritative companion, clarifies the general meaning of khuff: anything that covers the foot and prevents water from reaching it. This refutes those who require additional conditions like thickness or soling. The author then cites Ibn Hazm's strong rejection of such conditions, and references Ibn Abi Shayba's chapter title supporting the equivalence of socks to khuffs. He then returns to the fundamental principle: the default is washing the feet (as in the Quran), and deviation is only permitted through authentic proofs like the khuff hadith. Since the socks hadith are disputed, the majority required conditions for equivalence, such as being lined, soled, or thick. The author leans toward the view that thick socks qualify, while thin socks do not, and expresses doubt about the latter. This analysis reflects a methodical approach: establishing the authority of evidence (Anas's action), analyzing linguistic and rational implications, and applying conditions to preserve the general ruling. The author's conclusion aligns with the Hanafi school, which permits wiping over thick socks as akin to khuffs.

Key Terms
الخف (al-khuff): A covering for the foot that prevents water from reaching it, typically made of leather but not restricted to that material.
الجورب (al-jurb): A sock or stocking worn on the foot, typically made of fabric or wool.
الصفاقة (al-safaqa): Thickness or firmness of the material, a condition for equivalence to khuffs according to some scholars.
التجليد (al-tajlid): Lining the sock with leather or similar material to give it the quality of a khuff.
التنعيل (al-tan'il): Giving the sock a sole, making it more like a khuff.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the author's inclination, what condition makes socks equivalent to khuffs for wiping?
A) They must be lined with leather (mujallad).
B) They must be thick (thakhin).
C) They must have a sole (mun'al).
D) No condition; any sock is like a khuff.

Key Takeaway
The linguistic definition of khuff from a companion can expand its application, but the default ruling (washing feet) limits the extent of that expansion to only thick socks.

Wiping Over Socks: Textual Analysis and Qiyas Conditions
Textual analysis with qiyas and conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi usul principle of qiyas to derive conditions for wiping over socks, and evaluate the strength of the analogy to khuffs based on textual evidence.

Core Idea
Deviation from Quranic washing of feet requires authentic proof; socks can only be wiped if they resemble khuffs in thickness and durability.

This lesson examines how Hanafi usul al-fiqh handles a contested issue: wiping over ordinary socks during wudu. The Quran commands washing the feet, but authentic hadiths permit wiping over leather khuffs. Can this ruling be extended to socks through qiyas? We'll analyze the conditions scholars imposed, particularly the requirement that socks be thick and sturdy, and see how the author uses a chain of textual analysis to arrive at a preferred view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the original ruling and its evidence
Start by noting that the basic ruling is washing the feet, based on the apparent meaning of Quran 5:6. This is the default (usul). Any deviation must be supported by equally strong evidence.
The author emphasizes that the Quranic command is clear and not to be abandoned lightly.
2
Examine the authentic exception: wiping over khuffs
Authentic mutawatir or mashhur hadiths (e.g., from Sahihayn) establish the permissibility of wiping over leather khuffs. This is a valid takhsis (specification) of the general command to wash feet.
The author mentions 'like the hadiths of wiping over khuffs' implying these are well-known.
3
Assess the evidence for wiping over socks
The hadiths on wiping over socks (jurbān) are weaker; scholars dispute their authenticity. Therefore, the extension of the dispensation to socks is not automatic.
This is the core of the textual analysis: the strength of the dalil determines the validity of the rule.
4
Apply qiyas: identify the illah and shurut
To allow wiping over socks, scholars used qiyas to khuffs. The effective cause (illah) is covering the feet and providing protection for walking. But socks vary in material; thus conditions are needed: leather-covered, soled, or thick (thakhīn). The author favors thickness as the decisive condition.
Note that different conditions reflect different understandings of the illah. The Hanafi position uses thickness as the primary criterion.
5
Evaluate the author's tarjih
The author states his preference: thick socks are like khuffs, thin socks are not. This illustrates how a mujtahid weighs evidence and chooses a position (tarjih) when multiple views exist.
This step connects usul theory to actual fiqh practice.

والذي أميل إِلَيْهِ أن الجوربين إذا كانا ثخينين فهما في معنى الخفين يجوز المسح عليهما، أما إذا كانا رقيقين فهما ليسا في معنى الخفين، وفي جواز المسح عليهما تأمل، والله أعلم.

Chapter One / Difference in Chain
123
An error that has no meaning; because it is not brought by Quran, nor Sunnah, nor analogy (qiyas), nor a Companion's saying. And indeed Ibn Abi Shaybah classified in his book 'Al-Musannaf' (2) a chapter titled: 'Who said that socks are like khuffs' and he narrated in that effects (athar) from Ibn Umar, Ata, Nafi, and Al-Hasan. And we deduce from what preceded that the original ruling is washing the feet as is apparent from the Quran, and deviating from it is not permissible except through authentic hadiths like the hadiths of wiping over khuffs. Hence, it is permissible according to the majority of scholars to deviate from washing the feet to wiping over khuffs. As for the hadiths of wiping over socks, there is discussion about their authenticity as previously mentioned, so how can one deviate absolutely from washing the feet to wiping over socks? And Imam Muslim held this understanding by his statement: 'The apparent meaning of the Quran is not abandoned by the likes of Abu Qays and Huzayl' (3). Therefore, a number of scholars stipulated conditions for the permissibility of wiping over socks so that they become in the same category as khuffs, and socks enter into the meaning of khuffs. Some held that if socks are leather-covered (mujalladan) they are in the category of khuffs, some held that if they are soled (mun'alayn) they are in their category, and according to some, if they are thick and sturdy (thakhīnayn) they are in their category (4). And what I lean towards is that if socks are thick, they are in the category of khuffs and wiping over them is permissible. But if they are thin, they are not in the category of khuffs, and there is hesitation regarding the permissibility of wiping over them. And Allah knows best.
(1) Al-Muhalla 2/86-87.
(2) Al-Athar 1/173 (1991)-(1994).
(3) We did not find it in the printed edition of Kitab al-Tamyiz, and al-Bayhaqi mentioned it in Al-Sunan al-Kubra 1/284.
(4) See: Tuhfat al-Ahwadhi 2/336.

Commentary
This passage is a textual analysis of the issue of wiping over socks (jurbān) in wudu, focusing on the differences in hadith chains and texts that led to juristic variation. The author begins by critiquing an erroneous opinion that lacks evidence from Quran, Sunnah, qiyas, or Companion sayings. He then cites Ibn Abi Shaybah's collection of athar from Companions and successors allowing socks to be like khuffs. The basic principle is washing the feet (based on Quran 5:6), and deviation is only permitted via authentic hadiths, specifically those on khuffs. The hadiths on wiping over socks are disputed in authenticity. Therefore, many scholars set conditions for socks to be treated like khuffs: being leather-covered, soled, or thick. The author leans towards the third condition (thickness) and rejects wiping over thin socks. This analysis demonstrates how differences in hadith authenticity and interpretation lead to varying fiqh rulings.

Key Terms
الجوربان (al-jurbān): Socks worn on the feet, usually made of cloth or yarn, as opposed to leather khuffs
الخفان (al-khuffān): Leather socks or boots that cover the feet and ankles, worn for walking
صفيقين ثخينين (ṣafīqayn thakhīnayn): Thick and sturdy, referring to socks that are dense and not transparent or flimsy

First Six Opinions on Reporting Hadith by Meaning
Listing first six of twelve opinions on riwaya bi al-ma'na

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and distinguish between the first six scholarly opinions on reporting hadith by meaning (riwaya bi al-ma'na), and explain the key criteria that differentiate them.

Core Idea
Six opinions govern riwaya bi al-ma'na; they vary based on narrator ability, text type, and synonym substitution.

This passage introduces one of the most debated issues in hadith transmission: may a narrator convey the meaning of a hadith instead of its exact words? The author lists the first six of twelve opinions, showing a spectrum from absolute prohibition to conditional permission. Understanding these views is essential for evaluating hadith authenticity and the role of wording in legal derivation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the six opinions
Read the passage carefully and list each of the six opinions. For each, note the key condition or criterion mentioned.
Opinions 1-3 focus on text type or absolute prohibition; opinions 4-6 focus on narrator ability and synonym replacement.
2
Compare the criteria
Group the opinions by their underlying criterion: textual ambiguity (opinion 1), content type (opinion 2), narrator memory (opinions 4 and 5), and synonym substitution (opinion 6). Opinion 3 is a blanket prohibition.
3
Analyze the spectrum
Order the opinions from most restrictive to most permissive. Opinion 3 (absolute prohibition) is strictest; opinion 2 (permits for commands/prohibitions) is slightly permissive; opinions 1 and 4 are conditional; opinion 5 is a reversal; opinion 6 allows synonym replacement.
This spectrum shows how the permissibility of riwaya bi al-ma'na depends on the risk of altering legal rulings.
4
Reflect on usul implications
Consider how the permissibility of meaning reporting affects the reliability of hadith-based rulings. If a narrator changes wording, the derived hukm may change. The Hanafi school generally permits meaning reporting for non-memorizers, but requires caution.
This distinction is crucial for evaluating ikhtilaf among madhahib.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المبحث الأول
رواية الحديث بالمعنى
خلق الله الجنس البشري متفاوتاً في قدراته وما وهبه لَهُ بمنّه وفضله، وَقَدْ أَثر هَذَا التفاوت عَلَى قدرات الناس في الحفظ، فإنّك تجد الحافظ الَّذِي لا يكاد يخطئ إلا قليلاً، وتجد الرَّاوِي الكثير الخطأ، ومن ثَمَّ تجد بَيْنَ الرُّوَاة مَنْ يؤدي لفظ الْحَدِيْثِ كَمَا سمعه، ومنهم مَنْ يحفظ المضمون ولا يتقيد باللفظ، وَهُوَ ما نسميه " الرِّوَايَة بالمعنى " وفي جواز أداء الْحَدِيْثِ بِهَا خلافٌ بَيْنَ الْعُلَمَاء عَلَى اثني عشر قولاً (۱):
الأول: التفرقة بَيْنَ الألفاظ الَّتِي لا مجال فيها للتأويل وبَيْنَ الألفاظ التي تحتمل التأويل، فجوزت الرّوَايَة بالمعنى في الأول دُونَ الثاني. حكاه أبو الْحُسَيْن بن القطان (۲) عن بَعْض الشافعية، وَعَلَيْهِ جرى الكيا الطبري (٣) مِنْهُمْ).
الثاني: جواز الرِّوَايَة بالمعنى في الأحاديث التي تشتمل عَلَى الأوامر والنواهي، وأما إذا كَانَ اللفظ خفي المعنى محتملاً لعدة معانٍ فَلا تجوز. ويستوي في هَذَا الحكم الصَّحَابِي وغيره).
الثالث: المنع مطلقاً من الرّوَايَة بالمعنى، وتعين أداء لفظ الْحَدِيْثِ. وبه قَالَ عَبْد الله وابن سيرين، وأبو بكر الرازي الجصاص (۹) ، وأبو إسحاق الإسفراييني (۱)، وبه قَالَ الظاهرية (۳) ، وثعلب (۳) من النحويين)، وَهُوَ الأشهر من مذهب مالك).
الرابع: من يحفظ اللفظ والمعنى لا تجوز لَهُ الرِّوَايَة بالمعنى، ومن المعنى دُوْنَ اللفظ جازت روايته بالمعنى و به جزم الماوردي)، فَقَالَ: «والذي أراه أَنَّهُ إِن كَانَ يحفظ اللفظ لَمْ يَجُزُ أن يرويه بغير ألفاظه؛ لأن في كلام رَسُوْل الله من الفصاحة ما لا يوجد في كلام غيره، وإن لم يحفظ اللفظ جاز أن يورد معناه بغير لفظه؛ لأن الرَّاوِي قَدْ تحمّل أمرين: اللفظ والمعنى، فإن قدر عَلَيْهِمَا لزمه أداؤهما، وإن عجز عن اللفظ وقدر عَلَى المعنى لزمه أداؤه لئلا يَكُون مقصراً في نقل ما تحمل».
الخامس: عكس المذهب الذي قبله، فإن كَانَ يستحضر اللفظ جاز لَهُ الرِّوَايَة بالمعنى، وإن لَمْ يَكُنْ حافظاً للفظ لَمْ يَجُزُ لَهُ الاقتصار على المعنى، إذ لربما زاد فيه ما لَيْسَ مِنْهُ.
السادس: جواز الرواية بالمعنى بشرط إبدال المترادفات ببعضها مع الإبقاء على تركيب الكلام خوفاً من دخول الخلل عِنْدَ تغيير التركيب
First Topic: Reporting Hadith by Meaning. Allah created the human species varying in abilities and what He bestowed upon them by His favor and grace. This variation affected people's abilities in memorization. You find the memorizer who hardly errs except a little, and you find the narrator who makes many mistakes. Consequently, among the narrators there is one who delivers the wording of the hadith as he heard it, and among them one who memorizes the content and is not bound by the wording, which is what we call 'reporting by meaning'. And regarding the permissibility of performing the hadith by it, there is disagreement among scholars according to twelve opinions: First: Distinction between expressions that have no room for interpretation and those that admit interpretation; reporting by meaning is permitted in the former but not the latter. This was narrated by Abu al-Husayn ibn al-Qattan from some Shafi'is, and al-Kiya al-Tabari followed it. Second: Permissibility of reporting by meaning in hadiths that contain commands and prohibitions; but if the wording is obscure and likely has multiple meanings, it is not permissible. In this ruling, the companion and others are equal. Third: Absolute prohibition of reporting by meaning, and it is required to deliver the wording of the hadith. This was said by Abdullah, Ibn Sirin, Abu Bakr al-Razi al-Jassas, Abu Ishaq al-Isfarayini, and the Zahiris, and Tha'lab among the grammarians, and it is the most famous in the Maliki school. Fourth: Whoever memorizes the wording and the meaning, it is not permissible for him to report by meaning; whoever memorizes the meaning without the wording, it is permissible for him to report by meaning. This was affirmed by al-Mawardi, who said: 'What I see is that if he memorizes the wording, it is not permissible for him to report it with other than its words, because in the speech of the Messenger of Allah there is eloquence not found in the speech of others. If he does not memorize the wording, it is permissible to convey its meaning with other than its wording, because the narrator has taken on two things: wording and meaning. If he is able to do both, he must perform both; if he is unable regarding the wording but able regarding the meaning, he must perform it so that he is not negligent in transmitting what he undertook.' Fifth: The opposite of the previous opinion: if he memorizes the wording, it is permissible for him to report by meaning; if he does not memorize the wording, it is not permissible for him to restrict himself to the meaning, because he might add something not from it. Sixth: Permissibility of reporting by meaning on condition of replacing synonyms with each other while preserving the sentence structure, fearing the entry of error when changing the structure.
Source pages p. 127

Commentary
This passage opens the first section on the topic of reporting hadith by meaning (riwaya bi al-ma'na). The author begins by noting the natural variation in human memory and how this affects narrators: some can reproduce the exact wording, others only the meaning. This leads to the question of whether it is permissible to transmit a hadith by its meaning rather than its exact wording. The author then lists the first six of twelve known scholarly opinions on this issue. The first opinion distinguishes between unambiguous and ambiguous texts, allowing meaning reporting for the former. The second restricts permissibility to hadiths containing commands and prohibitions. The third absolutely prohibits any meaning reporting, a view attributed to several early scholars (including the Hanafi jurist al-Jassas) and the Zahiri school. The fourth opinion (of al-Mawardi, a Shafi'i) distinguishes based on the narrator's ability: if he knows the wording, he must use it; otherwise, meaning reporting is permissible. The fifth reverses this. The sixth allows meaning reporting only when replacing synonyms within the same sentence structure. The passage thus presents a range of positions without endorsing any single one, setting the stage for further analysis. The footnote references indicate sources for further study.

Key Terms
رواية بالمعنى (riwaya bi al-ma'na): Reporting the meaning of a hadith without adhering to its exact wording.
اللفظ (al-lafz): The exact wording of the hadith as uttered by the Prophet.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) First opinion
B) Second opinion
C) Fourth opinion
D) Sixth opinion

Key Takeaway
The permissibility of riwaya bi al-ma'na is contested among scholars, with six distinct positions ranging from absolute prohibition to conditional allowance based on narrator ability and text type.

Variant Hadith Wordings and Their Fiqh Impact
Introduces a second example of hadith wording variation affecting fiqh.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify how variant narrations of a hadith (riwayah bil-ma'na) can lead to differences in fiqh rulings, and apply the Hanafi approach to reconciling such variations.

Core Idea
Variant wordings are not errors; they require careful tarjih to extract the correct ruling.

This short passage introduces a second example of how differences in the wording of a single hadith can affect juristic rulings. The hadith from Abu Hurairah commands believers to walk to prayer with calmness when hearing the iqama. Six reliable tabi'is transmitted it from Abu Hurairah, and their wordings differ. Understanding how to handle such variation is a key skill in usul al-hadith and directly impacts fiqh deductions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core hadith and its narrators
Locate the hadith text and note that it is narrated by six tabi'is from Abu Hurairah. The number indicates widespread transmission, but wording differences exist.
The passage cites sources for the variants: al-Tahawi's Sharh Ma'ani al-Athar.
2
Recognize the phenomenon of riwayah bil-ma'na
Understand that narrators sometimes transmitted the meaning rather than the exact wording. This is accepted in Hanafi usul when the meaning is preserved, but it can lead to subtle juristic differences.
3
Analyze the imperative 'fāmshū'
The hadith uses the command 'walk.' In Hanafi usul, an imperative (amr) indicates obligation unless there is a qarinah (contextual evidence) to the contrary. The accompanying phrase 'wa'alaykum al-sakīnah' (be calm) may serve as a qarinah reducing it to recommendation.
This is a typical Hanafi approach: amr + qarinah = nadb.
4
Consider the variant wording from other narrations
In a well-known variant (Bukhari and Muslim), the Prophet said: 'When the prayer is established, do not come to it running; come walking with calmness...' This version explicitly forbids running, reinforcing that the command to walk is about manner, not obligation.
The passage does not quote this variant, but it is commonly cited in fiqh discussions.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
The difference in wording can lead to whether walking calmly is considered obligatory or merely recommended. Hanafi fiqh takes it as recommended (mustahab), not wajib, based on the qarinah and other proofs.
This is an example of how textual variation affects fiqh rulings.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
النموذج الثاني:
حَدِيث أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ صلى الله عليه وسلم أَنَّ رَسُول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قَالَ: «إذا سمعتم الإقامة فامشوا وعليكم السكينة، فما أدركتم فصلوا ، وما فاتكم فأتموا».
وَقَدْ رَوَى هَذَا الْحَدِيث عن أبي هُرَيْرَةَ ستة من التابعين، وحصل خلاف في لفظه على النحو الآتي:
الثقات ۱۸۱/۹ ، وتهذيب الكمال (۱۸۸/۷ و ۱۸۹) (٦۷۰۸)، والتقريب (٦٨٢٠).
(۱) عِنْدَ الطحاوي في شرح معاني الآثار ٤٩٢/٢.
The second model: The hadith of Abu Hurairah, may Allah be pleased with him, that the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, said: 'When you hear the iqama, walk and be calm. What you catch, pray, and what you miss, complete.' Six of the tabi'is narrated this hadith from Abu Hurairah, and there occurred a difference in its wording as follows: al-Thiqat 9/181, Tahdhib al-Kamal 7/188-189 (6708), and al-Taqrib (6820). (1) According to al-Tahawi in Sharh Ma'ani al-Athar 2/492.
Source pages p. 132

Commentary
This passage introduces a second example of how differences in the wording of a hadith (matn) can lead to juristic disagreements. The hadith is from Abu Hurairah commanding the believers to walk to prayer with tranquility when they hear the iqama. Six of the tabi'is narrated this hadith from Abu Hurairah, and the wording differs among them. Although the exact variants are not given in these pages, the author points out that such differences exist. This illustrates the phenomenon of narrators transmitting by meaning (riwayah bil-ma'na), which is a key issue in usul al-hadith. The differences in wording may affect the understanding of the command: e.g., whether it is obligatory to walk (not run) or merely recommended, and what to do if one misses part of the prayer. The author refers to later sources for the actual variants.

Key Terms
السكينة (al-sakinah): Calmness and tranquility; in the context of walking to prayer, it means not rushing.
الإقامة (al-iqamah): The call to start the prayer, similar to the adhan but shorter.
الرواية بالمعنى (riwayah bil-ma'na): Narrating a hadith by its meaning rather than the exact wording; a practice accepted when the narrator is trustworthy and preserves the intended meaning.

Variant wordings in hadith require usul analysis; the Hanafi approach uses internal qarinah to interpret commands as recommendations when the context supports it.

Wording Differences in the Hadith on Walking to Prayer
Presents a case study of hadith wording differences among Successors.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify two different wordings of the hadith about walking to prayer, trace their transmission, and explain how each wording could affect the derived fiqh ruling.

Core Idea
Narration by meaning allows wording variations that can change the legal ruling derived from a hadith.

In this lesson, we examine a concrete example of how hadith wording differences arise from narration by meaning (al-riwayah bi al-ma'na). The famous hadith about walking to prayer with calmness has been transmitted with two key wordings: 'fa-atimmu' (complete) and 'faqdu' (make up). These variations, reported by six different Successors from Abu Hurayra, are not errors but permissible paraphrases that can lead to different fiqh rulings. Our goal is to understand how scholars use these wordings to derive rules for the prayer of a latecomer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two key wordings
Locate the two phrases 'fa-atimmu' (فأتموا) and 'faqdu' (فاقضوا) in the hadith text. These are the critical variations that affect the ruling.
Both are commands meaning to complete the prayer, but they carry different fiqh implications.
2
Trace each wording to its narrators
List the Successors who reported each wording: Abd al-Rahman ibn Ya'qub, Hammam ibn Munabbih, and some versions of Abu Salama report 'fa-atimmu'; Muhammad ibn Sirin and Abu Rafi' report 'faqdu'. Note that Hammam has both wordings via different chains.
This shows that the same narrator can transmit different wordings, reflecting the permissibility of narration by meaning.
3
Map each wording to a possible fiqh ruling
Consider what each wording implies: 'fa-atimmu' suggests completing the prayer in the normal manner (adding what is missed as a regular part of the prayer), while 'faqdu' suggests making up the missed part separately (qada'). The Hanafi school generally adopts the 'fa-atimmu' interpretation.
The choice of wording can influence whether the latecomer's missed rak'ah is considered a continuation or a separate unit.
4
Evaluate the impact on furu' al-fiqh
Apply this to the practical scenario: if you catch three rak'ahs of a four-rak'ah prayer, do you complete the fourth as a regular rak'ah (following 'fa-atimmu') or do you perform it as a separate make-up (following 'faqdu')? The Hanafi ruling is that you complete the prayer in order, not as qada'.
This illustrates how a minor wording difference can lead to a major practical divergence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وهذا كله من تصرف الرواة بألفاظ الحديث وروايتهم بالمعنى
النموذج الثاني:
حديث أبي هريرة صلى الله عليه وسلم أن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قال: «إذا سمعتم الإقامة فامشوا وعليكم السكينة، فما أدركتم فصلوا، وما فاتكم فأتموا».
وقد روى هذا الحديث عن أبي هريرة ستة من التابعين، وحصل خلاف في لفظه على النحو الآتي:
عبد الرحمن بن يعقوب الحرقي. ولم يختلف على ابنه فيه.
رواه عنه بلفظ «فأتموا»، أخرجه مالك، ومن طريقه الشافعي وأحمد والبخاري في القراءة خلف الإمام والطحاوي. وأخرجه من غير طريق مالك: البخاري في القراءة ومسلم.
محمد بن سيرين. ولم يختلف عليه فيه رواه بلفظ: «فاقضوا». وأخرج روايته أحمد والبخاري في القراءة ومسلم في الصحيح.
أبو رافع. ولم يختلف عليه فيه رواه بلفظ: فاقضوا». وروايته عند أحمد.
همام بن منبه. رواه عنه عبد الرزاق ومن طريقه مسلم وأبو عوانة والبيهقي بلفظ: «فأتموا».
ورواه أحمد عن عبد الرزاق بلفظ: «فاقضوا».
أبو سلمة بن عبد الرحمن بن عوف واختلف عليه في لفظه: منهم من رواه عنه بلفظ: «فأتموا»، رواه على هذا الوجه: ...
All of this is from the narrators' manipulation of hadith wordings and their narration by meaning. The second model: The hadith of Abu Hurayra that the Messenger of Allah said: 'When you hear the iqama, walk and be calm; what you catch, pray, and what you miss, complete.' Six of the Successors narrated this hadith from Abu Hurayra, and there was a difference in its wording as follows: Abd al-Rahman ibn Ya'qub al-Harqi. No difference was reported from his son. He narrated from him with the wording 'fa-atimmu' (then complete). Recorded by Malik, and from his path by al-Shafi'i, Ahmad, al-Bukhari in al-Qira'a khalf al-Imam, and al-Tahawi. Also via other than Malik: al-Bukhari in al-Qira'a and Muslim. Muhammad ibn Sirin. No difference was reported from him; he narrated it with the wording 'faqdu' (then make up). His narration is recorded by Ahmad, al-Bukhari in al-Qira'a, and Muslim in al-Sahih. Abu Rafi'. No difference was reported from him; he narrated it with the wording 'faqdu'. His narration is with Ahmad. Hammam ibn Munabbih. Abd al-Razzaq narrated from him, and from his path Muslim, Abu Awana, and al-Bayhaqi with the wording 'fa-atimmu'. And Ahmad narrated from Abd al-Razzaq with the wording 'faqdu'. Abu Salama ibn Abd al-Rahman ibn Awf; there was a difference reported from him in its wording: some narrated from him with the wording 'fa-atimmu'...
Source pages p. 132

Commentary
This passage is a textual analysis demonstrating how variations in hadith wording (اختلاف اللفظ) among narrators can impact fiqh rulings. The author presents a second example: the famous hadith about walking to prayer with calmness. Six different Successors narrated this hadith from Abu Hurayra, and their wordings differ: some say 'fa-atimmu' (then complete the prayer) and others say 'faqdu' (then make up the missed part). The Hanafi school relies on the wording 'fa-atimmu' (as in the majority narrations) to derive that the missed rak'ah must be completed in the normal manner, while the wording 'faqdu' might imply a different action. This shows that precise wording matters in deriving legal rulings.

Key Terms
الرواية بالمعنى (al-riwayah bi al-ma'na): Narrating a hadith by its meaning rather than verbatim, which can lead to wording differences.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the hadith about walking to prayer, what is the difference between the narrations of Muhammad ibn Sirin and Hammam ibn Munabbih?
A) Ibn Sirin said 'fa-atimmu' while Hammam said 'faqdu'.
B) Ibn Sirin said 'faqdu' while Hammam said 'fa-atimmu'.
C) Both said 'fa-atimmu'.
D) Both said 'faqdu'.

Key Takeaway
Wording differences in hadith, arising from narration by meaning, are not errors but require careful analysis to derive the correct fiqh ruling.

The Third Model: How Variant Hadith Narrations Cause Ikhtilaf (The Kaffarah Example)
Presents different narrations of the kaffarah hadith and their narrators

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and compare variant narrations of a hadith, and explain how differences in the matn lead to distinct legal rulings among madhhabs.

Core Idea
A hadith's legal force changes when a key detail appears in one narration but not another.

In this passage, we examine how a single hadith—the story of the man who broke his fast in Ramadan—was transmitted with different endings. Some narrations include the Prophet's permission for the man to eat the expiation dates himself, while others omit this. This difference is not minor; it has a profound effect on the fiqh of kaffarah. Understanding how Hanafi usul handles such variation is essential for tracing the school's position on expiation for the fasting person.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core hadith issue
Recognize that the passage presents a well-known hadith about kaffarah for breaking the fast, and that the disagreement is over the complete text (matn) from al-Zuhri's chain.
2
List the variant narrators
Note the seven narrators listed (Malik, Yahya, etc.) who transmitted the longer version. Understand that their collective transmission strengthens this version.
The number of narrators is a tarjih factor in Hanafi usul.
3
Compare the two versions
The longer version includes the man's inability to expiate and the Prophet's command to eat the dates. The shorter version (from other chains) ends at the command to expiate without this concession.
The missing detail is the man's statement 'la ajid' and the Prophet's 'kulhu'.
4
Analyse the legal consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
The Hanafi school accepts the longer version, making kaffarah contingent on ability. The opposing view (Shafi'i) holds kaffarah obligatory even if unable, based on the shorter narration.
This is a real thamarah in fatwa: a poor person may be excused in the Hanafi school.
5
Apply Hanafi tarjih criteria
The passage implies that the multiplicity of reliable narrators for the longer version gives it preference. In Hanafi usul, when a longer narration is from more trustworthy chains, it is preferred over an abridged version.
This principle is known as 'al-ziyadah min al-thiqah maqbulah'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
النموذج الثالث
الاختلاف في رواية حديث أبي هريرة في كفارة الإفطار في رمضان اختُلِفَ عَلَى الزهري في رِوَايَة هَذَا الْحَدِيْثِ، إذ رَوَاهُ بعضهم عن الزهري، عن حميد بن عَبْد الرَّحْمن، عن أبي هُرَيْرَةَ، أن رجلاً أفطر في رَمَضَان، فأمره رَسُول الله أن يكفر بعتق رقبة أو صيام شهرين متتابعين، أو إطعام ستين مسكيناً، فَقَالَ: لا أجد فأُتِي رَسُول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم بعرق تمر، فَقَالَ: «خذ هَذَا فتصدق بِهِ»، فَقَالَ: «يَا رَسُوْلُ اللَّه! ما أجد أحداً أحوج إِلَيْهِ مني » فضحك رَسُوْل الله صلى الله عليه وسلم حَتَّى بدت أنيابه، ثُمَّ قَالَ: «كُلْهُ». رَوَاهُ بهذه الرِّوَايَة مالك، ويحيى بن سعيد، وفليح بن سليمان، وعمر بن عثمان المخزومي، وعبد الله بن أبي بكر، وابن جريج، وأبو أويس.
The Third Model: The difference in the narration of the hadith of Abu Huraira regarding the expiation for breaking the fast in Ramadan. There is disagreement over al-Zuhri in the narration of this hadith, as some narrated it from al-Zuhri, from Humayd ibn Abd al-Rahman, from Abu Huraira, that a man broke his fast in Ramadan, so the Messenger of Allah commanded him to expiate by freeing a slave, or fasting two consecutive months, or feeding sixty poor people. He said: I cannot find [any]. Then a basket of dates was brought to the Messenger of Allah, and he said: 'Take this and give it in charity.' He said: 'O Messenger of Allah! I do not find anyone more in need of it than me.' So the Messenger of Allah laughed until his molars showed, then said: 'Eat it.' This narration was related by Malik, Yahya ibn Sa'id, Fulayh ibn Sulayman, Umar ibn Uthman al-Makhzumi, Abdullah ibn Abi Bakr, Ibn Jurayj, and Abu Uways.
Source pages p. 140

Commentary
This passage presents the third model of ikhtilaf in the matn (text) of a hadith, focusing on the well-known hadith of Abu Huraira concerning the kaffarah (expiation) for intentionally breaking the fast in Ramadan. The author highlights that the disagreement is over the chain from al-Zuhri. Some narrators transmitted the hadith via al-Zuhri → Humayd ibn Abd al-Rahman → Abu Huraira, which includes the incident of the man who could not afford any expiation and was eventually told to eat the dates himself. This version is narrated by a group of reliable narrators including Imam Malik, Yahya ibn Sa'id, and others. The text does not yet show the alternative narration, but the implication is that other chains omitted the man's inability and the final instruction to eat, leading to different fiqh rulings: some scholars require kaffarah only if able, others include the option of eating dates as a substitute. The author lists the narrators to establish the strength of this version. In Hanafi usul, when multiple authentic narrations conflict, the preferred narration is determined by criteria such as the number of narrators, their reliability, and the context. This example illustrates how textual variation in a single hadith can produce divergent legal positions among madhhabs.

Key Terms
متن (matn): The text or content of a hadith, as opposed to its chain of narrators.
رواية (riwayah): A particular narration or version of a hadith, transmitted through a specific chain.
اختلاف (ikhtilaf): Disagreement or variation among scholars or narrations on a legal issue.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi usul principle demonstrated by this passage, what is the primary reason for preferring the longer narration of the kaffarah hadith over the shorter one?
A) It is more detailed and therefore more authentic.
B) It is narrated by a larger number of reliable transmitters.
C) It is from al-Zuhri.
D) It includes the Prophet's laughter.

Key Takeaway
Variant narrations of a hadith can lead to divergent fiqh positions; Hanafi usul resolves such ikhtilaf by preferring the version with stronger transmission and more complete text.

Hadith Criticism: Differentiating Shadhdh from Mahfuz in the Qada Fasting Hadith
Critical assessment of hadith chains and textual variants

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the criteria of shadhdh and mahfuz to compare variant hadith transmissions and explain the impact on fiqh rulings.

Core Idea
A transmission that contradicts the majority of reliable narrators is shadhdh; the mahfuz transmission must be preferred.

This lesson examines how Hanafi hadith scholars evaluate different chains of a key hadith on qada fasting. By comparing the reports from al-Zuhri, we see how a single change in narrator name can shift a hadith from mahfuz to shadhdh, affecting the derived ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base transmission
The majority of reliable narrators transmit from al-Zuhri from Hamid ibn Abd al-Rahman from Abu Hurayrah. This is the mahfuz version.
Mansur ibn al-Mu'tamir and others reported this chain.
2
Identify the variant Transmission
Mihan ibn Abi 'Umar narrated from al-Thawri from al-Zuhri from Sa'id ibn al-Musayyab, changing the intermediate narrator.
This contradicts the majority.
3
Apply the shadhdh criterion
Ibn Hajar declares Mihan's version shadhdh because it contradicts the majority of reliable transmitters. The mahfuz is the first.
Shadhdh means odd/irregular; it weakens the narration.
4
Identify textual additions
Al-Awza'i's version adds 'wa ahlaktu' (I am destroyed). al-Bayhaqi and the majority of al-Awza'i's students omit it, so the addition is rejected.
Additions not corroborated by reliable narrators are considered weak.
5
Determine the fiqh impact
The mahfuz version (qada only) is used to derive the ruling of making up fasts without expiation. The shadhdh version could imply additional obligations, but it is not relied upon.
This illustrates how hadith criticism directly shapes fiqh rules.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفصل الثاني / الاختلاف في الْمَتْن. ومنصور بن المعتمر، والأوزاعي، وعد، وعراك بن مالك، وعبد الجبار، وإبراهيم بن ... عن الزهري عن حميد. قال ابن حجر: «قوله : (عن الزهري عن حميد) كَذَا الأكثر من أصحاب مَنْصُوْر عَنْهُ ... وخالفهم مهران بن أبي عمر فرواه عن الثوري ... فَقَالَ: عن سعيد بن المسيب بدل حميد بن عَبْد الرَّحْمن ... وَهُوَ قَوْل شاذ والمحفوظ الأول». والأوزاعي: وفيه زيادة «فَقَالَ: يا رَسُول الله هلكت وأهلكت» قال البيهقي: وضعف شيخنا هذه اللفظة ... ورواه كافة أصحاب الأوزاعي عن الأوزاعي دونها. والأوزاعي أيضاً بدون زيادة. وعد، وعراك بن مالك، وعبد الجبار بن عمر الأيلي (ضعيف)، وعبد الرَّحْمن بن خالد بن مسافر، والنعمان بن راشد، وعقيل، ومُحَمَّد بن أبي حفصة، ويونس، وحجاج بن أرطاة، وصالح بن أبي الأخضر (ضعيف)، ومُحَمَّد بن إسحاق، وعبيد الله بن عمر، وإسماعيل بن أمية، ومُحَمَّد بن عبد الله بن أبي عتيق. كلهم عن الزهري. ورواية صالح بن أبي الأخضر عن الزهري عن حميد وأبي سلمة عن أبي هريرة. ورواية ابن أبي حفصة: عن الزهري عن أبي سلمة بدلاً من حميد. ورواية حجاج: عن الزهري عن أبي سلمة.
Chapter Two: Differences in the Text. And Mansur ibn al-Mu'tamir, and al-Awza'i, and Adi, and 'Irak ibn Malik, and 'Abd al-Jabbar, and Ibrahim ibn... from al-Zuhri from Hamid. Ibn Hajar said: 'His statement: (from al-Zuhri from Hamid) is how the majority of the companions of Mansur reported it... and Mihan ibn Abi 'Umar opposed them and narrated from al-Thawri... saying: from Sa'id ibn al-Musayyab instead of Hamid ibn 'Abd al-Rahman... and it is an odd (shadhdh) opinion, and the preserved (mahfuz) one is the first.' And al-Awza'i: in it is the addition 'He said: O Messenger of Allah, I am destroyed and have destroyed.' al-Bayhaqi said: 'Our teacher weakened this wording... and all the companions of al-Awza'i narrated from him without it.' And al-Awza'i also without the addition. And Adi, and 'Irak ibn Malik, and 'Abd al-Jabbar ibn 'Umar al-Ayli (weak), and 'Abd al-Rahman ibn Khalid ibn Musafir, and al-Nu'man ibn Rashid, and 'Uqayl, and Muhammad ibn Abi Hafsah, and Yunus, and Hajjaj ibn Artah, and Salih ibn Abi al-Akhdar (weak), and Muhammad ibn Ishaq, and 'Ubaydullah ibn 'Umar, and Isma'il ibn Umayyah, and Muhammad ibn 'Abdullah ibn Abi 'Atiq. All from al-Zuhri. And the narration of Salih ibn Abi al-Akhdar from al-Zuhri from Hamid and Abu Salamah from Abu Hurayrah. And the narration of Ibn Abi Hafsah: from al-Zuhri from Abu Salamah instead of Hamid. And the narration of Hajjaj: from al-Zuhri from Abu Salamah.
Source pages p. 144

Commentary
This passage is a critical survey of the transmission of a key hadith from al-Zuhri about making up a missed fast (qada). The author lists many narrators who transmitted from al-Zuhri, noting variants in the chain (e.g., whether al-Zuhri heard from Hamid ibn Abd al-Rahman or from Sa'id ibn al-Musayyab) and in the text (e.g., the addition 'wa ahlaktu'). Using the criteria of hadith criticism, the author identifies which transmission is 'mahfuz' (preserved/reliable) and which is 'shadhdh' (odd/anomalous). The presence of weak narrators like 'Abd al-Jabbar ibn 'Umar and Salih ibn Abi al-Akhdar is noted, and the consensus of the majority of reliable transmitters is preferred. This analysis directly impacts fiqh because different versions of the hadith yield different rulings—some requiring only a single day's makeup, others requiring expiation.

Key Terms
شاذ (shādh): A narration that contradicts a more reliable transmitter; considered weak and not followed.
محفوظ (maḥfūẓ): The narration that is supported by the majority of reliable transmitters; preferred over shadhdh.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) The narration with the addition 'wa ahlaktu'
D) The narration from Hajjaj from al-Zuhri from Abu Salamah

Key Takeaway
The mahfuz transmission of a hadith is preferred over shadhdh variants; careful hadith criticism is essential to correct fiqh derivation.

Analyzing Textual Variants: The Hadith of Breaking Fast in Ramadan
Listing narrators and textual variants of a hadith from al-Zuhri

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi method of analyzing textual variants (lafz) in hadith to identify the more reliable wording and explain its impact on legal derivation.

Core Idea
A single word difference in a hadith can change the ruling — textual analysis is essential for accurate istinbat.

Hadith texts often reach us through multiple chains and with slight variations in wording. Scholars like al-Bukhari evaluate these variants for clarity (أبين) and reliability. In Hanafi usul, such evaluations guide which wording is preferred for deriving legal rulings. This lesson walks you through the textual analysis of a famous hadith on expiation for breaking fast in Ramadan, illustrating how careful comparison of chains and wording strengthens fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the narrators and their shared source
List the eleven narrators mentioned (Ibn Abi Atiq, Musa ibn Uqbah, etc.) who all transmit from al-Zuhri. Recognize that a common source (al-Zuhri) implies the core hadith is the same, but wording may vary.
2
Note al-Bukhari's evaluation of clarity
Al-Bukhari states: 'The hadith of these is clearer' (أبين). This indicates that the wording transmitted by this group is more precise or unambiguous than other versions. For Hanafi usul, clarity is a criterion for tarjih (preference) when multiple authentic variants exist.
3
Observe the textual variant (اللفظة) and its spread
The same wording (اللفظة) appears in narrations from al-Walid ibn Muslim (from Malik and al-Layth) and from Hammad ibn Mas'adah (from Malik). This consistency across different paths strengthens the case that this wording is the original from al-Zuhri.
4
Recognize chain differences that affect reliability
Hisham ibn Sa'd follows the same wording but uses a different chain (al-Zuhri → Abu Salamah → Abu Hurayrah). While the wording matches, the chain is different; Hanafi scholars would check the strength of each chain to determine if the wording is fully supported.
5
Understand how textual analysis informs legal derivation
The preferred wording (e.g., with 'fa' vs. 'thumma' or certain phrases) directly impacts the ruling derived from the hadith. For example, the sequence of expiation actions may depend on the conjunction used. Hanafi usul prioritizes the variant deemed clearer and more widely transmitted.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفصل الثاني / الاختلاف في المتن
ابن أبي عتيق، وموسى بن عقبة، وعبد الله بن عيسى، وهبار بن عقيل، وإسحاق بن يحيى، وثابت بن ثوبان، وقرة بن عبد الرحمن، وبحر السقاء، والوليد بن محمد، وشعيب بن خالد، ونوح بن أبي مريم، جميعهم عن الزهري به قال البخاري: «وحديث هؤلاء أبين»، وكذلك هذه اللفظة في رواية الوليد بن مسلم، عن مالك والليث، وفي رواية حماد بن مسعدة عن مالك، وتابع هذه الروايات هشام بن سعد؛ إلا أنه رواه عن الزهري عن أبي سلمة عن أبي هريرة، وروى هذا الحديث بهذا اللفظ عن أبي هريرة سعيد بن المسيب أيضاً.
Chapter Two: Differences in the Text. Ibn Abi Atiq, Musa ibn Uqbah, Abdullah ibn Isa, Habbat ibn Aqil, Ishaq ibn Yahya, Thabit ibn Thuban, Qurrah ibn Abd al-Rahman, Bahr al-Saqqa, al-Walid ibn Muhammad, Shu'ayb ibn Khalid, Nuh ibn Abi Maryam, all of them from al-Zuhri with it. Al-Bukhari said: 'The hadith of these is clearer.' And similarly this wording is in the narration of al-Walid ibn Muslim from Malik and al-Layth, and in the narration of Hammad ibn Mas'adah from Malik. And Hisham ibn Sa'd followed these narrations, except that he narrated it from al-Zuhri from Abu Salamah from Abu Hurayrah. And Sa'id ibn al-Musayyab also narrated this hadith with this wording from Abu Hurayrah.
Source pages p. 146

Commentary
This passage is a textual analysis of a hadith concerning the expiation for breaking the fast in Ramadan. The author lists multiple narrators who all transmitted from al-Zuhri, and then highlights a variation in wording. He notes that Imam al-Bukhari considered the hadith of these narrators to be clearer (أبين), implying that their version is more reliable. He further points out that the same wording appears in the narration of al-Walid ibn Muslim from both Malik and al-Layth, and in the narration of Hammad ibn Mas'adah from Malik. However, Hisham ibn Sa'd followed these narrations but differed in his chain, narrating from al-Zuhri via Abu Salamah from Abu Hurayrah. Additionally, Sa'id ibn al-Musayyab also narrated the hadith with the same wording. This illustrates how scholars analyze chains and wording to determine the most authentic version, which in turn can affect the legal ruling derived from the hadith. The Hanafi school considers such analyses crucial for ijtihad.

Key Terms
المتن (al-matn): The text of a hadith, distinct from its chain of narration.
اللفظة (al-lafzah): A specific word or phrasing used in a narration.
أبين (abyan): Clearer; a term used by al-Bukhari to indicate a more explicit and unambiguous wording.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) The hadith of Sa'id ibn al-Musayyab

Key Takeaway
Textual analysis of hadith variants, guided by criteria like clarity and chain strength, is essential for sound Hanafi istinbat.

Kaffarah and Hadith Variation: The Hanafi Restriction to Intercourse
Analyzing how textual variation in a hadith leads to divergent fiqh rulings on kaffarah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi usul principle that a general ('amm) text can be restricted (takhsis) by a specific narration, and evaluate how this leads to the ruling that kaffarah is limited to intercourse (and nutritive/medicinal items) in the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
A general hadith can be restricted by a more precise narration; the kaffarah hadith is restricted to intercourse.

This lesson examines how a single hadith, narrated with slightly different wordings, caused profound disagreement among jurists about the scope of kaffarah for breaking the fast. By analyzing al-Bayhaqi's preference for the restricted narration, we see the Hanafi method of prioritizing textual precision over analogy.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two narrations
The first narration says 'a man broke his fast in Ramadan' (general), while the second specifies 'intercourse' (specific). Al-Bayhaqi notes the latter is more reliable due to the group's preservation.
2
Apply the Hanafi rule of takhsis
The general term ('amm) in the first narration is restricted by the specific wording (khass) in the second, more reliable narration. This is a standard Hanafi usul rule: al-amm yufidu al-wujub, but if khass exists, it restricts.
3
Analyze the opposing views
Some scholars (e.g., Malik) retain the generality using analogy between eating/drinking and intercourse. Others (e.g., al-Shafi'i) also restrict to intercourse but reject extension to nutritive items. The Hanafis add a separate rationale for nutritive items based on completion of offense.
4
Derive the Hanafi ruling
Kaffarah is obligatory for intercourse and for consuming what is normally nutritive/medicinal; for other items (e.g., grass), only qada is required.
