⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفصل الثاني / الاختلاف في المتن
وَقَالَ البيهقي: «ورواية الجماعة، عن الزهري مقيدة بالوطء ناقلة للفظ صاحب الشرع أولى بالقبول لزيادة حفظهم ، وأدائهم الْحَدِيث عَلَى وجهه».
أثر حديث أبي هريرة في اختلاف الفقهاء
اختلف الفقهاء في وجوب الكفارة عَلَى مَن أفطر عامداً بغير الجماع.
جمهور الفقهاء يرون وجوب الكفارة عَلَى مَن جامع عامداً في نهار رَمَضَان؛
وَلَكِنْ حكى العبدري وغيره: أن سعيد بن جبير، والشعبي، ومُحَمَّد بن سيرين، وقتادة، والنخعي، قالوا: لا كفارة عَلَيْهِ في الوطء أو غيره، وذهب الزيدية إلى أنّ الكفارة مندوبة.
وَلَكِنَّ الفقهاء اختلفوا في الإفطار عامداً في رَمَضَان بغير الجماع، هَلْ يوجِب الكفارة أم لا؟
فذهب أبو حَنِيْفَةَ إِلَى أنّ الكفارة تجب عَلَى مَن جامع في نهار رَمَضَان وَهُوَ صائم وعلى من أفسد صومه بأكل أو شرب ما يتغذى أو يتداوى به، بمعنى أنه : متى ما حصل الفطر بما لا يتغذى أو يتداوى بهِ عادة فعليه القضاء دُونَ الكفارة؛ وذلك لأنّ وجوب الكفارة يوجب اكتمال الجناية والجناية تكتمل بتناول ما يتغذى أو يتداوى به.
في حين ذهب الحسن، وعطاء، والزهري، والأوزاعي، والثوري، ومالك، وعبد الله بن المبارك، وإسحاق، وأبو ثور، أن من أفطر عامداً في رَمَضَان بأكل أو شرب أو جماع، فإنّ عَلَيْهِ القضاء والكفارة؛ وذلك لأنهم استدلوا بظاهر لفظ الْحَدِيث أنّ رجلاً أفطر في رَمَضَان فليس فِيْهِ تخصيص فطر بشيء دُوْنَ الآخر كَما يمكن قياس الأكل أو الشرب على الجماع بجامع ما بَيْنَهُما من انتهاك لحرمة الصوم.
وذهب سعيد بن المسيب، والشافعي، والصحيح من مذهب أحمد، والظاهرية، إلى عدم وجوب الكفارة عَلَى مَن أفطر عامداً في رَمَضَان إلا عَلَى المجامع، وحملوا الإفطار في الرّوَايَة الأولى للحديث عَلَى تقييد الرواية الثانية بالجماع فَقَطْ أما القياس فَقَدْ قَالَ البغوي: يختص ذَلِكَ بالجماع؛ لورود الشرع بِهِ، فَلا يقاس عَلَيْهِ سائر أنواع الفطر كَمَا لا يقاس عَلَيْهِ سائر أنواع الفطر؛ كَمَا لا يقاس عَلَيْهِ القيء.
Chapter Two / Variation in the Text. And al-Bayhaqi said: 'The narration of the group, from al-Zuhri, restricted to intercourse, transmitting the exact wording of the Lawgiver, is more deserving of acceptance due to the increase in their preservation and their performance of the hadith as it is.' The impact of the hadith of Abu Hurayra on the disagreement of the jurists. The jurists disagreed about the obligation of expiation on one who intentionally breaks the fast without intercourse. The majority of jurists hold the obligation of expiation on one who has intercourse intentionally during the day in Ramadan. But al-ʿAbdari and others narrated that Saʿid ibn Jubayr, al-Shaʿbi, Muhammad ibn Sirin, Qatada, and al-Nakhaʿi said: No expiation is due on him for intercourse or anything else, and the Zaydiyya held that expiation is recommended. But the jurists disagreed about intentionally breaking the fast in Ramadan without intercourse: does it obligate expiation or not? Abu Hanifa went to the view that expiation is obligatory on one who has intercourse during the day in Ramadan while fasting, and on one who spoils his fast by eating or drinking what is nutritive or medicinal, meaning that whenever breaking the fast occurs by what is not normally nutritive or medicinal, then only qada is due without expiation; because the obligation of expiation requires completion of the offense, and the offense is completed by consuming what is nutritive or medicinal. Meanwhile, al-Hasan, ʿAta, al-Zuhri, al-Awzaʿi, al-Thawri, Malik, ʿAbdullah ibn al-Mubarak, Ishaq, and Abu Thawr went to the view that one who intentionally breaks the fast in Ramadan by eating, drinking, or intercourse owes both qada and expiation; because they inferred from the apparent wording of the hadith that a man broke the fast in Ramadan, and there is no specification of breaking by one thing rather than another, as it is possible to analogize eating or drinking to intercourse due to the common factor of violating the sanctity of fasting. And Saʿid ibn al-Musayyib, al-Shafiʿi, the correct view of Ahmad’s school, and the Zahiris went to the view that expiation is not obligatory on one who intentionally breaks the fast in Ramadan except on the one who engages in intercourse; they interpreted the breaking of the fast in the first narration of the hadith as restricted by the second narration to intercourse only. As for analogy, al-Baghawi said: That is specific to intercourse because the Law has come with it, so other types of breaking the fast cannot be analogized to it, just as vomiting cannot be analogized to it.
Source pages p. 148

Commentary
This passage is a textual analysis of how the wording of Abu Hurayra's hadith regarding kaffarah for breaking the fast in Ramadan led to disagreement among jurists. The author begins by quoting al-Bayhaqi, who argues that the version narrated by a group from al-Zuhri—restricted to intercourse—is more reliable because the group's preservation and transmission are superior. Then the author presents the dispute. The majority of jurists (including the Hanafis) hold that kaffarah is only obligatory for intentional sexual intercourse during a Ramadan fast. However, some early scholars (Saʿid ibn Jubayr, al-Shaʿbi, etc.) held that no kaffarah is due even for intercourse, while the Zaydiyya consider it recommended. The main point of disagreement is whether breaking the fast by eating or drinking intentionally also requires kaffarah. Abu Hanifa distinguishes between nutritive/medicinal items and others: if one consumes what is normally eaten or drunk for sustenance or medicine, kaffarah is due; if not, only qada. His reasoning is that the offense (jinaya) is only complete with such consumption. Another group (al-Hasan, Malik, etc.) extends kaffarah to all intentional eating and drinking based on the apparent generality of the hadith and analogy to intercourse, since both violate the sanctity of fasting. A third group (Saʿid ibn al-Musayyib, al-Shafiʿi, etc.) restricts kaffarah to intercourse alone, interpreting the first narration as qualified by the second (which specifies intercourse). They reject analogy because the ruling is textually specific to intercourse, like vomiting, which is not subject to analogy. Thus, the textual variation in the hadith—whether the word 'iftara' (broke his fast) is general or restricted—directly affects the fiqh ruling.

Key Terms
الكفارة (al-kaffārah): Expiation required for violating the fast, specifically mentioned in the hadith for intercourse; its obligation is disputed for other acts.
الجماع (al-jimāʿ): Sexual intercourse, the act that triggers kaffarah according to most scholars, and the only act agreed upon for kaffarah.
الفطر (al-fiṭr): Breaking the fast; in this context, intentional breaking of the Ramadan fast, whether by eating, drinking, or intercourse.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa as stated in this passage, what is the ruling for a person who intentionally eats a non-nutritive substance (like a pebble) during Ramadan?
A) He must perform qada (make up the fast) only.
B) He must pay kaffarah only.
C) He must perform both qada and kaffarah.
D) He is exempt from any penalty.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school restricts kaffarah to intercourse and nutritive/medicinal consumption due to textual specificity and the concept of complete offense.

Al-Sunnah as Source
advanced
8 min
Khabar al-Wahid and the Quran: Hanafi vs. Majority
Dispute over khabar al-wahid vs. Quran with examples

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the Hanafi principle that a speculative report cannot override a definitive text, and evaluate the contrasting positions on specification (takhsis) using the hadith of Fatima bint Qais.

Core Idea
A speculative report cannot override a definitive text; Hanafis reject or reinterpret conflicting khabar al-wahid.

This lesson examines a fundamental usul dispute: when a solitary hadith appears to contradict a clear Quranic ruling, should the hadith be rejected or can it specify the Quran? The Hanafi school holds the former view, while the majority accepts specification. We will explore the reasoning, the key principle, and a concrete example.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the epistemological difference
The Quran is qat'i al-thubut (definitive in transmission) while khabar al-wahid is zanni (speculative). This asymmetry is the foundation of the Hanafi position.
Recall that even a trustworthy narrator can err, as Imam Ahmad said: 'Who is free from distortion and error?'
2
State the Hanafi principle
The Hanafis apply the maxim: 'ما فيه شبهة لا يعارض ما ليس فيه شبهة' (what contains suspicion does not oppose what has no suspicion). Thus, a speculative report cannot challenge a definitive text.
This principle is cited directly in the passage.
3
Understand the Hanafi view on ziyada 'ala al-nass
Hanafis consider an addition to the text (ziyada 'ala al-nass) as naskh (abrogation), which requires equally strong evidence. Since khabar al-wahid is weaker, it cannot abrogate.
The majority, however, see additions as bayan or takhsis, not necessarily naskh.
4
Contrast with the majority view
The Jumhur (Shafi'is, Malikis, Hanbalis) allow khabar al-wahid to specify (takhsis) or restrict (taqyid) the Quran, considering it an explanation rather than abrogation.
They do not require equivalence in the number of transmitters for bayan.
5
Apply to the example of Fatima bint Qais
Her hadith denies maintenance to a triple-divorced woman, contradicting the general Quranic maintenance rule (65:6). Hanafis reinterpret the hadith (e.g., restricting it to non-pregnant women) or reject it; the majority accept it as a specification.
This thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence) shows how the dispute impacts fiqh rulings.

الفصل الثاني / الاختلاف في الْمَتْن (1), بعتق رقبة أو صيام شهرين متتابعين أو إطعام ستين مسكيناً)، و(أو) هنا تقتضي التخيير، واختار مالك الإطعام؛ لأنَّه يشبه البدل من الصيام، فَقَالَ مالك: «الإطعام أحب إليَّ في العتق وغيره ) ، وَعَنْهُ في رِوَايَة أخرى - جواباً لسائله : «الطعام، لا نعرف غَيْر الطعام لا يأخذ مالك بالعتق ولا بالصيام». وذهب الحسن البصري (۳) إلى التخيير بَيْنَ العتق ونحر بدنة، واستدل بحديث ذلك من أرسله هُوَ أَن النَّبِيَّ صلى الله عليه وسلم قَالَ في الذي وطئ امرأته في رَمَضَان: رقبة ثُمَّ بدنة»(4). وروي عن الشعبي)، والزهري (٦) أن مَن أفطر في رَمَضَان عامداً فإِنْ عَلَيْهِ عتق قَالَ ابن رقبة، أو إطعام ستين مسكيناً، أو صيام شهرين متتابعيـن مـع قـضاء اليوم. عبد البر: وفي قَوْل الشعبي والزهري ما يقضي لرواية مالك بالتخيير في الْحَدِيث). المبحث الثاني مخالفة الحديث للقرآن الكريم هَذَا في من المتفق عَلَيْهِ بَيْنَ المُسْلِمِيْنَ أنّ القرآن الكريم من حَيْثُ الثبوت قطعي لا مراء فِيْهِ، في حين أنّ خبر الآحاد لا يعدو كونه ظني الثبوت، إذ إنّ احتمال وجود الخطأ رِوَايَة الحفاظ الثقات أمر وارد وَقَدْ قَالَ الإمام أحمد: «ومن ذا الذي يعـرى مـن التصحيف والخطأ» (۸). ومع توافر هَذِهِ الشبهة في خبر الآحاد فإنه لا مجال للقول بقطعية ثبوته؛ لأنّ (۱) انظر: الاستذكار ١٩٥/٣. (۲) انظر: المدونة الكبرى ،۲۱۸/۱ ، والاستذكار ١٩٥/٣. (۳) انظر: المحلى ۱۸۹/٦ - ١٩۰، والمجموع ٣٤٥/٣. (٤) أخرجه عبد الرزاق (٧٤٦٣) وللحديث طريق آخر مرسل أيضاً ذكره ابن حزم في المحلى ٦/ ۱۹۰، وَقَالَ النووي: حَدِيث الحسن ضعيف جداً». المجموع ٣٤٥/٦. (٥) انظر: الاستذكار ١٩٤/٣ ، وهذه الرِّوَايَة معارضة لما سبق ذكره عن الشعبي أن لا كفارة في الوطء وغيره. (٦) انظر: الاستذكار ١٩٥/٣. (۷) كَذَلِكَ. وذكر النووي روايات أخرى عن بغض الصَّحَابَة والتابعين والفقهاء في ما عَلَى من أفطر في رَمَضَان عامداً بغير جماع المجموع ٣٢٩/٦ - ٣٣٠، وانظر: المحلى ١٨٩/٦ – ١٩١. (۸) مَعْرِفَة أنواع علم الْحَدِيث: ٣٨٣، وطبعة نور الدين: ٢٥٢.  الفصل الثاني / الاختلاف في المتن (۲) «ما فِيْهِ شبهة لا يعارض ما لَيْسَ فِيْهِ شبهة ) . ومن ثَمَّ فإنه لا وجه للقول باستوائهما من ناحية الاستدلال، فضلاً عن تعارضهما؛ لذا نجد فقهاء الحنفية (٢) وبعض فقهاء المالكية (۳) عند معارضة خبر الآحاد للقرآن الكريم يوجبون ردّه، أو تأويله على وجه يجمع بَيْنَهُمَا. ويُعلّلون هَذَا الاشتراط بأنّ «خبر الواحد يحتمل الصدق والكذب، والسهو والغلط والكتاب دليل قاطع، فلا يقبل المحتمل بمعارضة القاطع، بَلْ يخرج عَلَى موافقته بنوع تأويل». وبالمقابل فإننا نجد الجُمْهُور يلغون هَذَا الاشتراط، ويجوزون تخصيص عموم نصوص الكتاب بخبر الواحد عِنْدَ التعارض، كَمَا يجوز تقييد ما أطلق من نصوصه بِهَا)، وذلك أنّ الحنفية ومن وافقهم يرون الزيادة على النص نسخاً)، وكيف يصح رفع المقطوع بالمظنون؟ والجمهور يقولون: إن الزيادة عَلَى النص ليست من باب النسخ دائماً)، وإنما قَدْ تَكون بياناً، أو تخصيصاً، أو تقييداً. وفي مسألة البيان لا يشترط تكافؤ الأدلة من حَيْثُ عدد ناقليها. ونستطيع أن نتلمس أثر هَذَا الخلاف في اختلاف الفقهاء من خلال الأمثلة الآتية: النموذج الأول: حَدِيث فاطمة بنت قيس قالت: طلقني زوجي ثلاثاً لم يجعل لي سكنى ولا نفقة، فأتيت رَسُوْلَ الله فذكرت لَهُ ذَلِكَ، فقلت لَهُ إِنَّهُ لَمْ يجعل لي سكنى ولا نفقة، قَالَ: صدق» (۸).
Chapter Two: Difference in the Text (Matn). (1), 'by freeing a slave, or fasting two consecutive months, or feeding sixty poor persons,' and 'or' here implies choice. Malik chose feeding because it resembles a substitute for fasting. So Malik said: 'Feeding is more beloved to me regarding freeing and other than it.' And from him in another narration – answering a questioner: 'Food, we do not know other than food. Malik does not adopt freeing nor fasting.' Al-Hasan al-Basri (3) held the view of choice between freeing and sacrificing a camel, and he adduced the hadith which he sent (mursal) that the Prophet (peace be upon him) said concerning the one who had intercourse with his wife in Ramadan: 'Free a slave, then sacrifice a camel.' (4) And it is narrated from al-Sha'bi (5) and al-Zuhri (6) that whoever intentionally breaks the fast in Ramadan must free a slave, or feed sixty poor persons, or fast two consecutive months along with making up the day. Ibn Abd al-Barr said: In the statement of al-Sha'bi and al-Zuhri, there is a judgment for Malik's narration of choice in the hadith. The Second Section: Contradiction of the Hadith to the Noble Qur'an. This is from what is agreed upon among Muslims that the Noble Qur'an, in terms of transmission (thubut), is definitive (qat'i) with no doubt about it, while khabar al-ahad (solitary report) is no more than speculative (zanni) in transmission, because the possibility of error in the narration of trustworthy preservers is existent. Indeed, Imam Ahmad said: 'And who is free from distortion and error?' (8). And with the availability of this suspicion in khabar al-ahad, there is no room for declaring its transmission definitive; because 'what includes suspicion does not oppose what has no suspicion.' Hence, there is no basis for saying they are equal in terms of deduction, let alone their contradiction; therefore we find the Hanafi jurists (2) and some Maliki jurists (3), when a khabar al-ahad contradicts the Noble Qur'an, require its rejection or its interpretation in a manner that reconciles between them. They justify this condition by saying: 'Khabar al-wahid (single report) admits truth and falsehood, forgetfulness and error, while the Book is a definitive proof, so that which admits possibility cannot be accepted in opposition to the definitive; rather it is interpreted in accordance with it by a type of interpretation.' On the other hand, we find the majority (Jumhur) abolish this condition and permit the specification of general Qur'anic texts by khabar al-wahid when there is contradiction, as they permit restricting what is absolute from its texts by them. This is because the Hanafis and those who agree with them consider an addition to the text as abrogation (naskh), and how can the definitive be raised by the speculative? The majority say: Addition to the text is not always of the category of abrogation, but it may be explanation (bayan), specification (takhsis), or restriction (taqyid). And in the matter of explanation, equivalence of evidences in terms of number of transmitters is not required. We can trace the effect of this difference in the differences of jurists through the following examples: The first example: The hadith of Fatima bint Qais who said: 'My husband divorced me three times and did not provide me with residence or maintenance. So I came to the Messenger of Allah and mentioned that to him, and I said to him: He did not provide me with residence or maintenance. He said: He spoke the truth.' (8).
Source pages p. 151

Commentary
This passage presents a fundamental usul dispute between the Hanafis and the majority (Jumhur) over the authority of khabar al-wahid (solitary reports) when they appear to contradict the Qur'an. The author begins with an example of textual variation (ikhtilaf in matn) concerning the kaffara (expiation) for intentionally breaking the fast in Ramadan. Various opinions are cited: Malik chose feeding, al-Hasan al-Basri allowed choice between freeing and sacrificing a camel, al-Sha'bi and al-Zuhri included freeing, feeding, or fasting. This illustrates how differences in hadith texts lead to fiqh differences. Then the passage moves to the core usul issue: the Qur'an is qat'i al-thubut (definitive in transmission), whereas khabar al-ahad is zanni al-thubut (speculative). The Hanafis and some Malikis argue that because the khabar al-wahid carries the possibility of error, it cannot oppose the definitive Qur'an. Therefore, when there is an apparent contradiction, the khabar must be either rejected or interpreted to harmonize with the Qur'an. The majority, however, allow specification (takhsis) and restriction (taqyid) of Qur'anic texts by khabar al-wahid, considering such additions not as abrogation but as explanation (bayan) or specification. The key difference stems from the Hanafi view that an addition to the text (ziyada 'ala al-nass) is considered naskh (abrogation), which is impermissible with a speculative source. The majority reject this equation. The passage concludes with an example: the hadith of Fatima bint Qais, where she was denied maintenance after triple divorce. This hadith was used by some to argue against the general maintenance rule, but the Hanafis reinterpret it to maintain consistency with the Qur'an. The commentary follows the author's order: first the kaffara example as a preliminary, then the principle, then the example of Fatima.

Key Terms
خبر الآحاد (khabar al-ahad): A solitary report that does not reach the level of tawatur; its transmission is speculative (zanni).
قطعي الثبوت (qat'i al-thubut): Definitive in transmission; the Qur'an is qat'i while khabar al-ahad is not.
ظني الثبوت (zanni al-thubut): Speculative in transmission; possible error or forgetfulness.
زيادة على النص (ziyada 'ala al-nass): An addition to the text of the Qur'an or a mutawatir hadith; Hanafis consider this as naskh (abrogation).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafis, what is the status of a khabar al-wahid that contradicts a clear Qur'anic verse?
A) It is accepted and specifies the Qur'an.
B) It is rejected or reinterpreted to harmonize with the Qur'an.
C) The Qur'an is considered abrogated by the hadith.
D) Both are considered equally authoritative and a new ijtihad is made.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafis uphold the definitive priority of the Quran over solitary reports, insisting on harmony or rejection when conflict arises.

Al-Sunnah as Source
intermediate
8 min
Hanafi Principle: Khabar al-Wahid Cannot Contradict the Qur'an
Stating Hanafi condition that khabar al-wahid must not oppose Qur'an

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi condition that a khabar al-wahid must not oppose the Qur'an, and apply it to evaluate the dispute over the hadith of Fatimah bint Qays.

Core Idea
A probabilistic solitary hadith cannot override the certain Qur'an; therefore it must be reconciled or rejected.

This passage introduces a foundational usul al-fiqh dispute: what happens when a solitary hadith (khabar al-wahid) appears to contradict a clear Qur'anic verse? The Hanafi school sets a strict condition: the hadith must be interpreted or rejected to avoid opposing the Qur'an, because the Qur'an is definitive (qat'i) while the hadith is only probable (zanni). The majority (jumhur) disagree, allowing specification or restriction of the Qur'an by such hadith. Understanding this dispute is key to appreciating many fiqh differences, such as the ruling on housing for a thrice-divorced woman.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two sides and their core principle
Recognize the Hanafi vs Jumhur positions. Hanafi: 'What contains doubt cannot oppose what contains no doubt.' Jumhur: permit takhsis/taqyid of Qur'an by khabar al-wahid.
The core difference: Hanafi views any addition (ziyadah) as naskh; Jumhur see it as bayan/takhsis.
2
Understand the Hanafi justification
The solitary report may be true/false or contain error, while the Qur'an is qat'i. The probable cannot override the certain.
Hanafi principle: al-zanni la yu'arid al-qat'i.
3
Understand the Jumhur justification
Adding to the text is not always naskh; it may be clarification or specification. Equivalence in narrators is not required for bayan.
Jumhur distinguish between abrogation (naskh) and specification (takhsis).
4
Trace the thamarah al-khilaf
Apply to Fatimah bint Qays hadith: does a thrice-divorced woman get housing? Hanafi: yes (Qur'an 65:6). Others: no (based on hadith).
This practical difference shows the real impact of the usul dispute.
5
Evaluate which approach is more consistent with Hanafi usul
Hanafi usul holds that zanni cannot abrogate qat'i; thus any apparent conflict must be resolved through interpretation or rejection.
Consider the strength of dalil (proof) and the hierarchy of sources.

Chapter Two / Disagreement in the Text (Matn) (2) "What contains doubt cannot oppose what contains no doubt." Therefore, there is no basis for claiming they are equal in inference, let alone that they conflict. Hence we find the Hanafi jurists (2) and some Maliki jurists (3) when a khabar al-ahad (single-narrator report) conflicts with the Noble Qur'an, they require rejecting it or interpreting it in a manner that reconciles between them. They justify this condition by saying: 'The solitary report may be true or false, and may involve forgetfulness or error, while the Book is a definitive proof, so the probable cannot oppose the definitive; rather, it must be aligned with it through some interpretation.' On the other hand, we find the majority (jumhur) cancel this condition and permit specifying the general texts of the Book with a solitary report when there is conflict, just as they permit restricting the absolute texts with it. This is because the Hanafis and those who agree with them consider an addition to the text as abrogation (naskh) – and how can the definitive be overridden by the probable? The majority say: An addition to the text is not always from the category of abrogation; rather, it may be clarification (bayan), specification (takhsis), or restriction (taqyid). In the matter of clarification, equivalence in the number of narrators is not required. We can discern the effect of this disagreement in the divergence of jurists through the following examples: The first example: The hadith of Fatimah bint Qays who said: My husband divorced me three times and did not provide me with housing or maintenance. So I came to the Messenger of Allah and mentioned that to him. I said to him: 'He did not provide me with housing or maintenance.' He said: 'He spoke the truth.' (8) It was narrated by Malik (1), al-Shafi‘i (2), 'Abd al-Razzaq (3), al-Humaydi (4), Sa'id ibn Mansur (5), Ibn Sa'd (6), Ibn al-Ja'd (7), Ibn Abi Shaybah (8), Ahmad (1), al-Darimi (11), Muslim (12), Abu Dawud (13), Ibn Majah (14), al-Tirmidhi (15), al-Nasa'i (16), al-Tahawi (21), Ibn Hibban (22), and others (18) Ibn al-Jarud, and (18) and (19) al-Tabari (23) (5) The trustworthy Abu 'Uthman al-Khurasani Sa'id ibn Mansur ibn Shu'bah, resident of Mecca, died in the year 227 AH. See Tarikh al-Islam: 184, deaths (227 AH), Siyar A'lam al-Nubala' 10/586, and al-Taqrib (2399).
Source pages p. 152

Commentary
This passage presents a foundational usul al-fiqh dispute between the Hanafi school and the majority of other schools. The passage type is a usul dispute with an illustrative example. The author begins by stating the Hanafi rule: 'What contains doubt cannot oppose what contains no doubt.' This refers to the principle that a khabar al-wahid (a solitary hadith, which is zanni in both transmission and meaning) cannot contradict the Qur'an (which is qat'i). When such a conflict arises, the Hanafis require either rejecting the hadith or interpreting it to align with the Qur'an. The justification is that a solitary report is probabilistic (muhtamil) while the Qur'an is certain (qati'), so the probabilistic cannot override the certain. In contrast, the majority (jumhur, including Shafi'is, Malikis, and Hanbalis) permit using khabar al-wahid to specify (takhsis) the general ('amm) of the Qur'an, restrict (taqyid) its absolute (mutlaq), or clarify (bayan) its ambiguous. The key difference is that Hanafis view any addition (ziyadah) upon the Qur'anic text as abrogation (naskh), which is impermissible because you cannot abrogate a definitive proof with a probabilistic one. The majority argue that such additions are not necessarily abrogation; they can be clarifications or specifications, and for that purpose, equivalence of narrators is not required. The author then presents a practical example: the hadith of Fatimah bint Qays, in which the Prophet (peace be upon him) reportedly said that a thrice-divorced woman is not entitled to housing and maintenance. This hadith, narrated by many but still a khabar al-wahid (since many of these are ahad), appears to conflict with the Qur'anic verse that obligates housing for divorced women (65:6). Hanafis either interpret the verse as applying only to revocable divorce or reject the hadith. This example shows how the usul difference leads to divergent fiqh rulings.

Key Terms
خبر الواحد (khabar al-wahid): A solo or single-narrator report that reaches the level of tawatur; its transmission is zanni.
الزيادة على النص (al-ziyadah 'ala al-nass): Adding a ruling or condition to the textual proof; considered by Hanafis as naskh (abrogation) when it contradicts the text.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi usul discussed in the passage, what should be done when a khabar al-wahid contradicts a definitive Qur'anic text?
A) Accept the hadith and ignore the Qur'an
B) Reject the hadith entirely without consideration
C) Reject the hadith or interpret it to reconcile with the Qur'an
D) Combine both to create a new ruling

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi condition that khabar al-wahid cannot oppose the Qur'an is based on the hierarchy of proof: zanni cannot override qat'i.

Al-Sunnah as Source
intermediate
15 min
The Principle of Narrator's Contradiction to His Narration
Discussing whether a narrator's contrary action weakens his narration

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on the narrator's contradiction to his narration and evaluate al-Jassas's distinction versus the majority view.

Core Idea
A narrator's contrary action does not invalidate his narration; the apparent meaning of the text remains the binding proof.

This passage examines a critical principle in Hanafi usul: when a companion or narrator acts against a hadith he narrates, does that weaken the hadith? Some scholars argued it indicates abrogation or interpretation. The majority, however, maintain that the hadith's apparent meaning is primary and the narrator's action is not a valid objection. Understanding this principle clarifies many fiqh disputes, including the requirement of a guardian in marriage.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two initial positions
Determine the view that some Malikis and early Hanafis held: the narrator's contrary action shows he knew of abrogation or specification, so the narration is not acted upon. Then note al-Jassas's more detailed distinction.
The initial position rests on the assumption that a righteous narrator would not act against the truth without certain knowledge.
2
Analyze al-Jassas's two-case distinction
Examine the first case: the hadith admits interpretation — the narrator's interpretation is not followed, and the apparent meaning stands. Second case: the hadith does not admit interpretation — the narration is suspended.
Al-Jassas believes certainty that the text is unambiguous can be determined, leading to suspension.
3
Examine the majority's counter-argument
Study the reasoning that the narrator's action does not prove abrogation or interpretation; possibilities of forgetfulness, error, or taqlid exist. The apparent meaning (zahir) remains the primary evidence.
The majority includes most Hanafis, Shafi'is, and others, as seen in the quotes from al-Shafi'i and Ibn al-Qayyim.
4
Apply the principle to a fiqh example
Consider the dispute on the requirement of a guardian (wali) in marriage. The passage introduces this as an illustration of how the principle affects fiqh rulings.
The example is incomplete in this passage, but it shows the practical impact: the hadith 'No marriage without a guardian' is accepted despite some Companions acting otherwise.
5
Evaluate the thamarah al-khilaf
Identify the practical difference: the majority uphold the hadith, while the minority would set it aside. This affects whether the guardian's permission is a condition for a valid marriage.
The tarjih (preferred view) according to the text is with the majority.

وقول الصَّحَابِي - مهما كَانَتْ مكانته - لا تقاوم الوقوف بوجه النص، لا سيما إذا كَانَ النص لا يحتمل التأويل، وإنما يعدُّ هَذَا من اجتهادات ذَلِكَ الصَّحَابِي، والأمة ملزمة بالعمل بالنص، وغير ملزمة بالعمل باجتهادات الصَّحَابَة، قَالَ الشَّافِعِي – رَحِمَهُ الله -: كيف أترك الْحَدِيث بعمل من لَوْ عاصرته لحاججته» (۱).

Chapter Two / Disagreement in the Text. Among those conditions is that the narrator does not act contrary to his narration. Some Malikis agreed with them on this, because he only acts contrary to it if he is certain from a sound path of its abrogation, or its diversion from its apparent meaning by his interpretation or specification, whether this is from witnessing the condition of the Messenger of Allah (saw), or hearing a clear explicit text from him, or knowledge of the consensus of the Companions contrary to its purport. This then obliges him to speak according to the later evidence according to his knowledge. Abu Bakr al-Razi al-Jassas from the Hanafis made a distinction, holding that the narrated report in such a case falls into two states: First: that the report is susceptible to interpretation; in that case, the interpretation of the Companion and those below him is not taken, and the report remains upon its apparent meaning, acted upon by its explicit wording, unless evidence arises warranting its diversion to what the narrator interprets it. Second: that the report does not admit interpretation, and it is not possible that the wording of the hadith is an expression from the Companion; this is the one that is suspended in its acceptance and acting upon it. The majority of jurists and usul scholars disagree with him, for it does not follow from the Companion's contradiction of the hadith he narrates that he must have come across an abrogator for it, or that an interpretation occurred to him. Then the effective cause for the ruling is the apparent meaning of the wording in the report, which is established, and the contrary action of the narrator does not constitute a valid objection; because the possibility that he clung to what he thought was a proof, while it is not, exists, and the religiousness of the Companion and good opinion of him prevents him from deliberate error, but forgetfulness and mistake are possible for him, as they are possible for others. And the statement of the Companion, whatever his status, does not stand against the text, especially if the text does not admit interpretation; rather, this is considered among the ijtihadat of that Companion, and the community is bound to act by the text, and not bound to act by the ijtihadat of the Companions. Al-Shafi'i said: 'How can I leave the hadith for the action of someone whom, if I had lived contemporaneously with him, I would have argued with him?' And the hadith, if its chain is authentic and its evidence clear, is a proof against the community, including the Companion. Hence Ibn al-Qayyim said: 'What we profess to Allah and which we cannot do other than – and this is the intention in this chapter – is that if a hadith is authentic from the Messenger of Allah (saw), and no other hadith that abrogates it is authentic, then it is obligatory upon us and upon the community to take his hadith and leave everything that contradicts it, and we do not leave it for the contradiction of anyone, whoever he may be, whether the narrator or other. Because it is possible that the narrator forgot the hadith, or it was not present in his mind at the time of giving a fatwa, or he did not pay attention to its evidence for that issue, or he interpreted it with a weak interpretation, or there arose in his opinion something that contradicts it but is not actually contradictory, or he followed someone else in his fatwa contrary to it because he believed that person more knowledgeable than him, and that he only contradicted him for what is stronger than him. And if it were assumed that all of this is absent – and there is no way to know or even assume its absence – the narrator is not infallible, and his contradiction of what he narrated does not necessitate the fall of his integrity until his bad deeds outweigh his good deeds, and by contradicting this one hadith he does not attain that.' Whatever the case, this foundation has reflected on the jurisprudential field, and disagreements among jurists have been found whose reference is to this principle. We see this clearly from the following examples: The First Model: The Requirement of the Guardian in Marriage. The jurists differed regarding the requirement of the guardian's permission for the validity of the marriage contract into two opinions: First: No marriage contract without a guardian, and it is a condition for the validity of the contract. It is sound, and this is said by the majority, and it is narrated from Umar, Ali, Ibn Mas'ud, Ibn Abbas, Abu Hurayrah, and Aisha. And it was said by Sa'id ibn al-Musayyib, al-Hasan, Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz, Jabir ibn Zaid, al-Thawri, Ibn Abi Layla, Ibn Shubruma, Ibn al-Mubarak, Ubayd Allah al-Anbari, and Ishaq ibn...
Source pages p. 166

Commentary
This passage is an usul discussion about whether a narrator's practice contrary to his narration weakens the narration. The author presents the view that some Malikis and Hanafis (initially) hold that if a narrator acts against his own narration, it indicates he must have known it was abrogated or interpreted, so his narration is not to be taken. Then Abu Bakr al-Jassas (Hanafi) distinguishes: if the hadith admits interpretation, the narrator's interpretation is not accepted unless there is evidence; if the hadith does not admit interpretation, then the narration is suspended. The majority, however, reject this. They argue that the narrator's contrary action does not prove abrogation or interpretation; rather, the plain meaning of the hadith is the primary proof. The Companion could be mistaken, forgetful, or acting on a weaker ijtihad. The statement of al-Shafi'i and Ibn al-Qayyim emphasizes that the hadith is binding even if the narrator himself acts otherwise, because the narrator is not infallible. The passage then transitions to a fiqh example: the requirement of a guardian (wali) in marriage. This example illustrates how the principle of not deferring to a narrator's contrary action affects fiqh disputes. The example is introduced but incomplete; it lists the first opinion (guardian required) with many supporters. The second opinion (no guardian required) is not given in the text.

Key Terms
الراوي (al-rawi): The narrator of a hadith, who may be a Companion or later transmitter.
الرواية (al-riwaya): The narration or hadith itself that is transmitted.
التأويل (al-ta'wil): Interpretation of a text away from its apparent meaning based on evidence.
الناسخ (al-nasikh): An abrogating text that supersedes the earlier ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the majority of fuqaha and usuliyyun, if a narrator acts contrary to the hadith he narrates, what should be done?
A) The hadith is set aside because the narrator's action indicates abrogation.
B) The hadith is accepted, and the narrator's action is not considered a valid objection.
C) The hadith is suspended until further evidence clarifies the matter.
D) The narrator's interpretation is adopted over the apparent meaning.

Key Takeaway
A narrator's practice contrary to his narration does not invalidate the hadith; the apparent meaning remains the binding proof unless there is independent evidence of abrogation.

Khabar al-Wahid vs Qiyas: The Case of Wudu from Cooked Food
Analyzes the hadith dispute and establishes the principle that khabar al-wahid takes precedence over qiyas.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why Ibn Abbas rejected the hadith of wudu from fire and state the majority position on khabar al-wahid versus qiyas.

Core Idea
Khabar al-wahid, if authentic, takes precedence over qiyas in the majority view.

This lesson explores a classic usul dispute: when a solitary hadith seems to contradict analogical reasoning, which prevails? The case of wudu after eating cooked food serves as a concrete example. We will examine why Ibn Abbas rejected the hadith and how the majority of scholars resolved the conflict, establishing a key principle in hadith-based jurisprudence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core dispute
Determine the ruling in question: Is wudu required after eating food touched by fire? The hadith commands wudu, but qiyas (analogy to other foods) suggests it is not required.
2
Analyze Ibn Abbas's objection
The passage clarifies that Ibn Abbas did not reject the hadith because it contradicted qiyas, but because he believed it was abrogated by the Prophet's own action of eating a shoulder and praying without wudu.
Understanding this nuance is crucial to avoid the common misconception that the dispute was purely based on qiyas.
3
Assess the strength of the hadith
The author lists numerous Companions who narrated the hadith of wudu from fire, showing that it was not a weak solitary report but well-supported. This strengthens its case against claims of weakness.
Multiple chains of transmission (turuq) increase the reliability of a khabar al-wahid.
4
State the majority view
Ibn Jama'a and the majority of scholars (including al-Shafi'i and Ahmad) hold that a sound khabar al-wahid is accepted and preferred over opposing qiyas. This is the preponderant position.
This principle has wide application in fiqh.
5
Note the practical effect
The methodological disagreement on khabar al-wahid vs qiyas leads to different fiqh rulings. In the next examples, the passage will illustrate this impact on actual derivations.
The student should be alert to how usul disputes shape furu'.

Chapter Two / Disagreement in the Text. As for the hadith of wudu from what is touched by fire, Ibn Abbas's rejection of it was not based on opposition to qiyas, but rather the hadith according to Ibn Abbas was abrogated by the hadith: 'The Prophet (peace be upon him) ate a sheep's shoulder and prayed without performing wudu.' Moreover, Abu Hurayra was not alone in narrating the hadith of wudu from what is touched by fire, for he was joined in its narration by Abu Ayyub, Abu Talha, Zayd ibn Thabit, Umm Habiba, Aisha, Abu Musa al-Ash'ari, Sahl ibn al-Ash'ari, Sahl ibn al-Hanzaliyya, Umm Salama, Anas ibn Malik, Abdullah ibn Umar, Mu'adh ibn Jabal, Abdullah ibn Zayd, and others, until Malik and Abdullah... (footnotes). So the preferred view from the perspective of evidence and proof is what the majority of scholars held. Hence Ibn Jama'a said: The correct view upon which the imams of hadith or their majority are is that the solitary trustworthy connected report in all that is accepted and preferred over opposing qiyas, and this was stated by al-Shafi'i, Ahmad ibn Hanbal, and others among the imams of hadith, fiqh, and usul. However, this difference in stances regarding the conflict of khabar al-wahid with qiyas left an effect on fiqhi derivations, which we clearly perceive in the following examples.
Source pages p. 176

Commentary
This passage begins by discussing the well-known dispute concerning whether wudu is required after eating cooked food. The author clarifies that Ibn Abbas's rejection of the hadith commanding wudu was not due to its conflict with qiyas (analogical reasoning) but because he considered the hadith abrogated by the practice of the Prophet. The author then lists numerous companions who narrated the hadith, strengthening its transmission. After citing the narrators and their sources, the author concludes that the preponderant view is the majority position: that a sound khabar al-wahid (solitary report) is acceptable and takes precedence over qiyas that opposes it. This is the view of al-Shafi'i, Ahmad, and others. The passage ends by noting that this methodological difference (whether to prefer khabar al-wahid over qiyas) has practical effects on fiqh derivations, which will be illustrated with examples.

Key Terms
خبر الواحد (khabar al-wahid): A report narrated by one or a few narrators, not meeting the conditions of tawatur.
القياس (al-qiyas): Analogical reasoning used to derive rulings for new cases based on common 'illa.
منسوخ (mansukh): Abrogated; a ruling that has been superseded by a later revelation or sunnah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) He considered the hadith weak in transmission.
C) He held that the hadith was abrogated by the Prophet's action.
D) He thought the hadith applied only to certain foods.

Key Takeaway
A sound khabar al-wahid is accepted and preferred over opposing qiyas, but abrogation is a valid reason to set aside a hadith.

The Authority of Authentic Hadith Over Madinan Practice
Usul rule: authentic hadith prevails over Madinan practice

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the Hanafi position on the precedence of authentic solitary hadith over Madinan practice and evaluate the Maliki counter-argument.

Core Idea
An authentic hadith from the infallible Prophet cannot be overridden by any human practice, including that of Madinah.

This lesson examines a key usul dispute between the Hanafi and Maliki schools regarding the weight of the continuous practice of the people of Madinah (amal ahl al-Madinah). The Malikis consider this practice as a form of tawatur that can override a solitary hadith. The Hanafis, however, insist that an authentic hadith, being from the infallible Prophet, always takes precedence. We will analyze the arguments on both sides and the Hanafi critique.

Guided Path
1
Identify the dispute
State the exact issue: does the practice of Madinah override an authentic solitary hadith? The Malikis say yes, Hanafis no.
2
Understand the Maliki justification
The Malikis argue that Madinah's continuous practice from the Prophet's time constitutes a mutawatir transmission of the ruling, so a solitary hadith cannot contradict it.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafis respond that the Prophet's hadith is infallible while Madinan practice is human, and Madinah is only part of the ummah, not the whole.
4
Derive the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical consequence: Malikis may reject a solitary hadith that conflicts with Madinan practice; Hanafis will follow the hadith regardless.
5
Apply the Hanafi usul principle
In Hanafi usul, an authentic hadith is a primary source (dalil shar'i) that cannot be overridden by customary practice (urf) or local consensus.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المبحث السادس
مخالفة الحديث لعمل أهل المدينة
من المعلوم أن المدينة النبوية كَانَتْ مهبط الوحي ومركز السلطة التشريعية والدنيوية في الحقبة الثانية من الدعوة النبوية، وَلَمْ يؤثر عن أحد من الصحابة سواء من المهاجرين أو الأنصار مِمَّنْ سكنها أنَّهُ نزح عَنْهَا في حياة رَسُول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم
وكانوا في حياتهم العامة على تماس مَعَ التشريعات والأحكام، يعيشون ظروفها، ويفقهون عللها، ويقومون بمهمة نشرها وتعليمها، وهكذا ظلت أجيال الناس فيها تتلقى الأحكام جيلاً عن جيل، وَهُوَ مؤدٍ في نهاية المطاف إلى اعتبار إجماع أهلها نقلاً بالتواتر للحكم المعمول به).
لذا اشترط جمهور المالكية للعمل بخبر الآحاد أن لا يَكُون مخالفاً لعمل أهل
المدينة (٣) وتعللوا بما قدمنا ذكره.
والحق أن الْحَدِيث إذا صَحَ لَمْ يَكُنْ لقول أحدٍ كائناً من كان أن يعارض بِهِ، والحجة في نقل المعصوم ،فَقَط ، ثمَّ إن أهل المدينة جزء من الأمة لا كلها، فلا ينبني (۱) إعلام الموقعين ۲/ ۱۹ - ۲۰ و ۳۱۱، وفتح الباري ٤ / ٣٧٩. (۲) ترتيب المدارك ١/ ٦٤ - ٦٥، وإعلام الموقعين ٢/ ٣٧٤. (٣) إحكام الفصول ٤٨٦/١ (٥١١) فما بعدها.
The Sixth Section: Contradicting the Hadith to the Practice of the People of Madinah. It is known that the prophetic Madinah was the place of revelation and the center of legislative and worldly authority in the second period of the prophetic call, and it is not reported that any of the Companions, whether from the Muhajirun or the Ansar who lived there, left it during the lifetime of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him). They were in their public life in touch with legislations and rulings, experiencing their circumstances, understanding their causes, and undertaking the task of spreading and teaching them. Thus, successive generations of people therein received rulings generation after generation, which ultimately leads to considering the consensus of its people as a mutawatir transmission of the applied ruling. Therefore, the majority of Malikis stipulate for acting upon a solitary hadith that it not contradict the practice of the people of Madinah, and they justify it with what we have mentioned. The truth is that if the hadith is authentic, no one's statement, whoever they may be, can oppose it; the proof is only in the transmission of the infallible (Prophet). Moreover, the people of Madinah are a part of the ummah, not the whole, so...
Source pages p. 183

Commentary
This passage presents the Maliki position that the practice (amal) of the people of Madinah, considered as a continuous transmission (tawatur), can override a solitary hadith (khabar al-wahid). The author recounts the reasoning: Madinah's unique status as the center of revelation and the uninterrupted transmission of practice from the Prophet through generations. However, the author counters that an authentic hadith from the Prophet cannot be opposed by any human opinion, and that the Madinans are only part of the ummah, not the whole. This reflects the broader Hanafi usul principle that the hadith itself, when authentic, takes precedence over local practice, as Hanafis do not grant Madinan practice independent legal authority equal to hadith.

Key Terms
عمل أهل المدينة (amal ahl al-Madinah): The continuous practice of the people of Madinah, considered as a source of law by Malikis.
خبر الآحاد (khabar al-wahid): A hadith transmitted by one or a few narrators, not reaching tawatur.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Because the hadith comes from the infallible Prophet, while Madinan practice is from fallible humans.
C) Because the Malikis are a minority.
D) Because Madinan practice is limited to transactions.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, an authentic solitary hadith cannot be overridden by the practice of Madinah or any local custom.

Contradicting Hadith with the Practice of Medina
Discusses the Maliki claim that the practice of Medina can override ahad hadith and the Hanafi refutation using rational arguments.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position that an authentic hadith cannot be overridden by the practice of Medina (amal ahl al-madina) and contrast it with the Maliki view, using Ibn Hazm's rational arguments.

Core Idea
An authentic hadith cannot be opposed by any practice because the hadith is from the infallible Prophet, while the people of Medina are fallible.

The people of Medina lived at the heart of revelation, leading the Maliki school to consider their continuous practice as a form of consensus that can override a solitary hadith. But does later practice have the power to negate a direct prophetic report? In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi refutation of this principle, grounded in the epistemological priority of the infallible source.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two conflicting sources
The Maliki school claims that 'amal ahl al-madina' (practice of the people of Medina) transmitted tawatur can override an authentic ahad hadith. The Hanafi position rejects this. Identify both positions from the passage.
Focus on the first paragraph where the Maliki reasoning is mentioned.
2
Analyze the Hanafi counter-argument
The author states: 'al-haqq anna al-haditha idha sahha lam yakun li-qawli ahadin...' (the truth is that when a hadith is authentic, no one's statement can oppose it). Understand the underlying premise: the only binding proof is from the infallible (the Prophet).
Why does the infallibility of the source matter? Because fallible humans cannot overrule a definitive transmission.
3
Trace Ibn Hazm's rational arguments
Ibn Hazm presents two key points: (1) truth is independent of practice – a hadith is either true or false; practice cannot change its truth-value. (2) The timing of obligation – if practice is required before acting, it is equivalent to saying the practice is the source of obligation, which contradicts the hadith's authority.
These are logical (aqli) arguments that do not rely on textual evidence.
4
Examine the critique of Maliki definition
The passage questions whose practice is meant: the entire ummah (impossible due to known disagreement), a specific era (disagreement existed in every era), or specific individuals (internal disagreement among Medinans). Each alternative is problematic.
This discredits the claim that the practice is a homogeneous, binding consensus.
5
Apply the Hanafi usul principle
Based on this analysis, state the Hanafi rule: khabar al-ahad that is authentic is accepted unconditionally; no later practice can override it. This is because the Sunnah is an independent primary source.
Contrast with the Maliki condition that khabar al-ahad must not contradict 'amal ahl al-madina'.

(۱) إعلام الموقعين ۲/ ۱۹ - ۲۰ و ۳۱۱، وفتح الباري ٤ / ٣٧٩. (۲) ترتيب المدارك ١/ ٦٤ - ٦٥، وإعلام الموقعين ٢/ ٣٧٤. (٣) إحكام الفصول ٤٨٦/١ (٥١١) فما بعدها.
عَلَى موافقتهم جواز مخالفة الأحاديث المقبولة). وَقَدْ فند أدلتهم ابن حزم من وجوه حاصلها:
١ - إن الخبر المسند الصَّحِيح قَبْلَ العمل بِهِ أحق هُوَ أم باطل؟ فإن قالوا: حق، فسواء عمل به أهل المدينة أم لم يعملوا، لَمْ يزد الحق درجةً عملُهُم بِهِ وَلَمْ ينقصه إِن لَمْ يعملوا به، وإن قالوا باطل، فإن الباطل لا ينقلب حقاً بعملهم به، فثبت أن لا معنى لعمل أهل المدينة أو غيرهم. ٢- العمل بالخبر الصَّحِيح متى أثبت الله العمل بِهِ أقبل أن يعمل بِهِ أم بَعْدَ العمل بِهِ؟ فإن قالوا: قَبْلَ أن يعمل بِهِ فَهُوَ كقولنا. وإن قالوا: بَعْدَ أن يعمل بِهِ، لزمهم عَلَى هَذَا أن العاملين بِهِ هم الَّذِيْنَ شرعوا الشريعة، وهذا باطل. نقول عمل من تريدون عمل أمة مُحَمَّد صلى الله عليه وسلم كافة، أم عمل عصر دُونَ عصر، أم عمل رسول الله ، أم أبي بكر ، أم عمر، أم عمل صاحب من سكان المدينة مخصوصاً؟ فإن قالوا: عمل الأمة كلها، فلا يصح؛ لأن الخلاف بَيْنَ الأمة مشتهر، دائم الرد على من خالفهم، فلو كَانَتْ الأمة مجمعة عَلَى هَذَا القول فعلى من يردون؟! وإن قالوا عصر دُونَ عصر، فباطل أيضاً؛ لأنَّه ما من عصر إلا وقَدْ وجد فيه خلاف، ولا سبيل إلى وجود مسألة متفق عَلَيْهَا بَيْنَ أهل عصر ونقول لَهُمْ: أهل المدينة الّذِينَ جعلتم عملهم حجة رددتم بها خبر المعصوم اختلفوا فِيْمَا بَيْنَهُمْ أم لا؟ فإن قالوا: لا، فإن الموطأ يشهد بخلاف هَذَا، وإن قالوا: قُلْنَا: فما الَّذِي جعل اتباع بعضهم أولى من بَغض
وهم
نعم،
Sixth Topic: Contradicting Hadith with the Practice of the People of Medina. It is known that the Prophetic city was the revelation's descent and the center of legislative and worldly authority in the second era of the prophetic call, and it is not reported from any Companion, whether Muhajir or Ansar, that he left it during the lifetime of the Messenger of God, peace be upon him. They were in their public life in touch with legislations and rulings, living their circumstances, understanding their causes, and undertaking the task of spreading and teaching them. Thus generations of people there received rulings generation after generation, which ultimately leads to considering the consensus of its people as a mutawatir transmission of the practiced ruling. Therefore, the majority of Malikis stipulated for acting upon khabar al-ahad that it not contradict the practice of the people of Medina, and they reasoned with what we mentioned previously. The truth is that when a hadith is authentic, no one's statement, whoever it may be, can oppose it, and the proof is only in the transmission of the infallible. Furthermore, the people of Medina are part of the ummah, not all of it, so their agreement does not justify opposing accepted hadiths. Ibn Hazm refuted their evidence in several points: (1) The authentic musnad hadith before acting upon it: is it true or false? If they say true, then whether the people of Medina acted upon it or not makes no difference; they did not increase its truth by acting upon it, nor did they decrease it by not acting upon it. If they say false, then falsehood cannot be turned into truth by their action. So it is established that the practice of the people of Medina or others has no meaning. (2) Acting upon the authentic hadith: when did God establish acting upon it? Before acting upon it or after acting upon it? If they say before acting upon it, then it is like our statement. If they say after acting upon it, then it would follow that those who acted upon it are the ones who legislated the Sharia; this is false. We say: whose practice do you intend? The practice of the entire ummah of Muhammad, peace be upon him? Or the practice of a specific era? Or the practice of the Messenger of God? Or of Abu Bakr? Or of Umar? Or the practice of a specific Companion residing in Medina? If they say the practice of the whole ummah, that is invalid because disagreement among the ummah is well-known, and they constantly refute those who oppose them. If the ummah were united on this statement, whom would they be refuting? And if they say a specific era, that is also false because there is no era except that disagreement existed in it, and there is no way to find a matter agreed upon by the people of an era. And we say to them: The people of Medina, whose practice you made a proof, thus rejecting the report of the infallible — did they disagree among themselves or not? If they say no, then the Muwatta testifies otherwise. And if they say yes, we say: what made following some of them more deserving than others? And they [object]? Yes,
Source pages p. 183

Commentary
This passage is a discussion of a usul dispute regarding the authority of the practice of the people of Medina (amal ahl al-Madina) in relation to authentic hadith. The author begins by acknowledging the historical importance of Medina as the center of revelation and law, and states that its early inhabitants were directly connected to the legislative process. This led the Maliki school to consider the continuous practice of Medina as a form of ijtima' (consensus) that takes precedence over ahad hadith if they contradict it. The author then presents the counter-argument: the truth is that an authentic hadith cannot be opposed by anyone's opinion because the only definitive proof is from the infallible (the Prophet). The people of Medina are only a part of the ummah, not the whole, so their consensus cannot override accepted hadith. Ibn Hazm's refutation is then summarized in two main points: first, if a hadith is true, the practice of Medina cannot increase or decrease its truth; if false, it remains false regardless of practice. Second, the question of timing: if practice is required before acting, it contradicts the hadith's own authority; if after, it implies that practitioners are legislators. The passage then further critiques the Maliki position by questioning whose practice is meant—the whole ummah, a specific era, or specific individuals—each alternative being problematic. It concludes with a question about the internal disagreement among the people of Medina, citing the Muwatta as evidence. The overall stance is against prioritizing amal ahl al-Madina over authentic hadith, which aligns with the Hanafi view that the Qur'an and Sunnah are the primary sources.

Key Terms
عمل أهل المدينة (amal ahl al-madina): The continuous practice of the people of Medina, claimed by Malikis to constitute a form of consensus that can override ahad hadith.
خبر الآحاد (khabar al-ahad): A non-mutawatir hadith reported by one or a few narrators.
إجماع (ijma): Consensus of the scholars of the ummah on a ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the basis for the Hanafi rejection of the practice of Medina (amal ahl al-madina) as an overriding authority over authentic hadith?
A) The people of Medina did not practice the hadith, so it is unknown.
B) Only the Prophet's words are infallible; the people of Medina are fallible and their practice cannot change the truth of a hadith.
C) The practice of Medina is not transmitted at all.
D) The Hanafi school denies the authenticity of the practice.

Key Takeaway
An authentic hadith stands on its own as a binding proof; no later communal practice, even from Medina, can override it because authority rests solely with the infallible Prophet.

Al-Sunnah as Source
intermediate

Critique of 'Amal Ahl al-Madina as a Source Overriding Authentic Hadith
Rational critique of 'amal ahl al-madina as a legal source

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the logical flaws in the argument that Medina's practice can override an authentic hadith and apply the Hanafi usul principle that practice does not overrule textual evidence.

Core Idea
An authentic hadith is true in itself—practice cannot change its truth.

Some Maliki scholars argued that the established practice of the people of Medina ('amal ahl al-madina) could override an authentic hadith if the hadith contradicted that practice. Ibn Hazm, a Zahiri scholar, offered a devastating rational critique of this position. His arguments are largely in harmony with Hanafi usul, which does not grant practice independent authority over sound textual evidence. This lesson walks through Ibn Hazm's refutation step by step, allowing you to see why 'amal cannot overrule nass.

Guided Path
1
Identify the claim being refuted
The claim is that the established practice of the people of Medina can override an authentic hadith. Ibn Hazm attacks this by questioning the logical basis of giving practice authority over text.
This claim was primarily advanced by some Maliki scholars regarding the hadith of khiyar al-majlis.
2
First argument: truth is independent of practice
Ibn Hazm asks: is the authentic hadith true or false before being acted upon? If it is true, practice does not increase its truth; if false, practice cannot make it true. Therefore, practice is irrelevant to the authority of the hadith.
This is a purely logical argument that does not rely on any textual proof.
3
Second argument: who legislates?
If acting upon the hadith is what makes it binding, then the practitioners become the legislators. This is absurd because only Allah and His Messenger legislate.
This exposes a theological problem: binding authority comes from revelation, not from human action.
4
Third argument: whose practice?
Ibn Hazm asks for specification: is it the practice of the entire ummah, a specific era, or specific individuals? He shows each option is untenable: the ummah has disagreements, eras have disagreements, and individuals differ as recorded in the Muwatta'.
This argument undercuts the claim that there is a single, agreed-upon Medinese practice.

Source Text

١ - إن الخبر المسند الصَّحِيح قَبْلَ العمل بِهِ أحق هُوَ أم باطل؟ فإن قالوا: حق، فسواء عمل به أهل المدينة أم لم يعملوا، لَمْ يزد الحق درجةً عملُهُم بِهِ وَلَمْ ينقصه إِن لَمْ يعملوا به، وإن قالوا باطل، فإن الباطل لا ينقلب حقاً بعملهم به، فثبت أن لا معنى لعمل أهل المدينة أو غيرهم. ٢- العمل بالخبر الصَّحِيح متى أثبت الله العمل بِهِ أقبل أن يعمل بِهِ أم بَعْدَ العمل بِهِ؟ فإن قالوا: قَبْلَ أن يعمل بِهِ فَهُوَ كقولنا. وإن قالوا: بَعْدَ أن يعمل بِهِ، لزمهم عَلَى هَذَا أن العاملين بِهِ هم الَّذِيْنَ شرعوا الشريعة، وهذا باطل. نقول عمل من تريدون عمل أمة مُحَمَّد صلى الله عليه وسلم كافة، أم عمل عصر دُونَ عصر، أم عمل رسول الله ، أم أبي بكر ، أم عمر، أم عمل صاحب من سكان المدينة مخصوصاً؟ فإن قالوا: عمل الأمة كلها، فلا يصح؛ لأن الخلاف بَيْنَ الأمة مشتهر، دائمو الرد على من خالفهم، فلو كَانَتْ الأمة مجمعة عَلَى هَذَا القول فعلى من يردون؟! وإن قالوا عصر دُونَ عصر، فباطل أيضاً؛ لأنَّه ما من عصر إلا وقَدْ وجد فيه خلاف، ولا سبيل إلى وجود مسألة متفق عَلَيْهَا بَيْنَ أهل عصر ونقول لَهُمْ: أهل المدينة الّذِينَ جعلتم عملهم حجة رددتم بها خبر المعصوم اختلفوا فِيْمَا بَيْنَهُمْ أم لا؟ فإن قالوا: لا، فإن الموطأ يشهد بخلاف هَذَا، وإن قالوا: قُلْنَا: فما الَّذِي جعل اتباع بعضهم أولى من بغض وهم نعم،
... their agreement to allow contradicting acceptable hadith. Ibn Hazm refuted their arguments with points, summarized: 1. The authentic chain-narrated hadith before being acted upon: is it truth or false? If they say truth, then whether the people of Medina acted upon it or not, their acting upon it does not increase its truth and not acting upon it does not decrease it. If they say false, then falsehood cannot turn into truth by their acting upon it. So it is established that the practice of the people of Medina or others has no meaning. 2. Acting upon the authentic hadith: when God established acting upon it, is it before acting upon it or after? If they say before, then it is like our view. If they say after, then they must hold that the actors are the ones who legislated the Shari'ah, and this is false. We say: the practice of whom do you mean? The practice of the entire ummah of Muhammad (saws), or of a specific era, or of the Messenger, or of Abu Bakr, or of 'Umar, or of a specific Companion from among the inhabitants of Medina? If they say a particular era, that is also invalid because there is no era without disagreement, and there is no way to find a matter agreed upon by all of that era. Source pages p. 184

Commentary
This passage is a refutation by Ibn Hazm (a Zahiri scholar) of the argument that the practice of the people of Medina ('amal ahl al-madina) can override an authentic hadith. This argument was used by some Maliki scholars to reject the hadith on khiyar al-majlis. Ibn Hazm presents several rational objections: First, if a hadith is authentic, it is true regardless of whether people act on it; practice cannot change truth value. Second, if acting on a hadith establishes its authority, then only after practice would it become binding, implying the practitioners are legislators, which is absurd. Third, he questions whose practice is meant—the whole ummah, a specific era, etc. He argues that claiming consensus of the people of Medina is impossible because they themselves differed, as recorded in the Muwatta'. This critique demonstrates that 'amal ahl al-madina cannot be a source that overrides clear textual evidence. In Hanafi usul, the principle is similar: the practice of a particular region is not a source that can abrogate or overrule a sound hadith.

Key Terms
عمل أهل المدينة (‘amal ahl al-madina): The established practice of the people of Medina, used by some as a source of law.
الأحاديث المقبولة (al-ahadith al-maqbula): Acceptable hadiths that meet the criteria for being acted upon.
خبر المسند الصحيح (khabar al-musnad al-sahih): A hadith with an unbroken chain of trustworthy narrators going back to the Prophet.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Ibn Hazm's critique, why is the argument that 'acting on a hadith makes it binding' flawed?
A) It confuses truth with falsehood.
B) It implies that the practitioners are the ones who legislate the Shari'ah.
C) It requires the hadith to be weak before practice.
D) It is only applicable to non-authentic hadith.

Key Takeaway
An authentic hadith is authoritative in itself; the practice of a community cannot change its truth or override it, because truth is independent of human action.

Refuting the Maliki Condition for Khabar al-Ahad
Refuting the Maliki condition for khabar al-ahad

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate the Maliki condition for accepting khabar al-ahad and identify its refutation based on the Hanafi argument from multiple narrations and lack of consensus.

Core Idea
The Maliki condition that khabar al-ahad must not contradict Medinan practice fails here because many Medinans narrated the hadith.

The Malikis assert that a solitary hadith (khabar al-ahad) is not accepted if it contradicts the established practice of the people of Medina (amal ahl al-Madina). In this passage, the author systematically refutes this condition, using the hadith of khiyar al-majlis (option of the session) as a test case. The refutation proceeds on three levels: the condition is unique to the Malikis, the alleged consensus against the hadith is false, and the hadith itself is not truly solitary.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Maliki Condition
State the Maliki requirement: khabar al-ahad must not contradict amal ahl al-Madina. Note that this is a unique condition not accepted by other schools.
Understand that the condition is based on the authority of Medinan practice as a source of law.
2
Examine the First Refutation: Condition Not Binding
The author notes that even if the condition is valid, it only binds the Malikis themselves. It does not obligate others to reject the hadith.
This is a procedural objection: a school's self-imposed condition cannot be used to invalidate a hadith for others.
3
Analyze the Second Refutation: No Medinan Consensus
List the Medinan Companions and Successors who affirmed khiyar al-majlis (e.g., Umar, Uthman, Ibn Umar, Abu Hurayra, etc.). This disproves the claim that Medinan practice was unanimously against it.
Ibn Abi Dhi'b explicitly stated the hadith was 'well-known in Medina'.
4
Consider the Third Refutation: The Hadith is Not Ahad
Even if the condition is accepted, the hadith of khiyar al-majlis is not solitary (ahad) because seven Companions narrated it through multiple chains, making it mashhur (well-known).
The author lists the narrators and the major hadith collections in which their reports appear.
5
Draw the Usul Principle
Conclude that a claimed consensus (ijma) cannot be established when prominent scholars from that region narrate contrary reports. Additionally, multiple narrations raise the status of a hadith from ahad to mashhur, strengthening its authority.
This illustrates the Hanafi method of evaluating hadith and refuting objections based on weak claims of consensus.

الفصل الثاني / الاختلاف في الْمَتْن

1 - أن اشتراط المالكية للعمل بخبر الآحاد أن لا يَكُون مخالفاً لعمل أهل المدينة، شرط تفردوا به، فيكون لازماً لَهُمْ ولا يلزم غيرهم. 
2- على فرض التسليم - جدلاً - بكون هَذَا الَّذِي اشترطوه شرطاً للعمــل بـخـبـر الآحاد، فما اشترطوه غَيْر متحقق في هَذِهِ المسألة، فإنهم نصوا على أن إجماع أهل المدينة إذا عارضه خبر آحاد، قدم الإجماع. ودعوى إجماع أهل المدينة هنا منقوضة فَقَد سبق أن نقلنا القول بثبوت خيار المجلس عن عمر وعثمان وابن عمر وأبي هُرَيْرَةَ وسعيد بن المسيب والزهري وابن أبي ذئب والدراوردي، وهؤلاء جميعاً من أهل المدينة، فكيف تصح دعوى إجماعهم؟ حَتَّى إن ابن أبي ذئب لما قِيْلَ لَهُ أن مالكاً لا يعمل بهذا الْحَدِيث قَالَ: هَذَا خبر موطأ في المدينة، يريد أنَّه منتشر. 
3- وإذا أمعنا في التنزل معهم، والتسليم بأن هَذَا الشرط الَّذِي اشترطوه صَحِيح، وأن إجماع أهل المدينة متحقق فإنه يخدش استدلالهم عدم كون الحَدِيث آحادياً، وكيف يَكُون خبر آحاد وَقَدْ رَوَاهُ من الصَّحَابَة عدد غفير، وقفنا عَلَى رِوَايَة سبعة مِنْهُمْ، هم: 
أ. سمرة بن جندب وحديثه أخرجه ابن أبي شيبة، وأحمد، وابن ماجه، والنسائي، والطحاوي، والبيهقي. 
ب عَبْد الله بن عَمْرو بن العاص : وحديثه عِنْدَ أحمد، وأبي داود، والترمذي، والنسائي، والدارقطني، والبيهقي، وابن عَبْد البر. 
ج. ابن عباس: وأخرج حديثه ابن حبان، والبزار، وأبو بكر الإسماعيلي، والبيهقي. 
د. أبو هُرَيْرَةَ: حديثه عِنْدَ الطيالسي، وابن أبي شيبة، وأحمد، والطحاوي، والطبراني، وابن عدي. 
ه. عَبْد الله بن عمر: وَهُوَ أشهر طرق هَذَا الْحَدِيث، أخرجه مالك، والشافعي، وأحمد، والبخاري ومسلم، وأبو داود، والترمذي، وابن ماجه، والنسائي، وغيرهم. 
و. حكيم بن حزام: عِنْدَ الشَّافِعِيّ، والطيالسي، وأحمد.
Chapter Two: Disagreement in the Text (Matn)

1. The Malikis' condition for acting upon a solitary hadith (khabar al-ahad) is that it should not contradict the practice of the people of Medina. This is a condition unique to them, so it is binding upon them and not upon others. 2. Suppose we concede - for argument's sake - that this condition they stipulated is valid, then it is not fulfilled in this case. For they have stated that if the consensus of the people of Medina conflicts with a solitary hadith, consensus is given precedence. But the claim of consensus of the people of Medina here is refuted, for we have already transmitted the statement affirming the option of the session (khiyar al-majlis) from 'Umar, 'Uthman, Ibn 'Umar, Abu Hurayra, Sa'id ibn al-Musayyib, al-Zuhri, Ibn Abi Dhi'b, and al-Darawardi - all of whom are from Medina. So how can the claim of their consensus be valid? Indeed, when Ibn Abi Dhi'b was told that Malik did not act upon this hadith, he said: 'This hadith is well-known (mutawwa') in Medina,' meaning it is widespread. 3. And if we go further and concede to them that this condition is correct and that the consensus of the people of Medina is established, then their argument is still flawed because the hadith is not solitary! For how can it be solitary when a large number of the Companions have narrated it? We have come across the narrations of seven of them: a) Samura ibn Jundub: his hadith is recorded by Ibn Abi Shayba, Ahmad, Ibn Majah, al-Nasa'i, al-Tahawi, and al-Bayhaqi. b) 'Abdullah ibn 'Amr ibn al-'As: his hadith is found with Ahmad, Abu Dawud, al-Tirmidhi, al-Nasa'i, al-Daraqutni, al-Bayhaqi, and Ibn 'Abd al-Barr. c) Ibn 'Abbas: his hadith is narrated by Ibn Hibban, al-Bazzar, Abu Bakr al-Isma'ili, and al-Bayhaqi. d) Abu Hurayra: his hadith is found with al-Tayalisi, Ibn Abi Shayba, Ahmad, al-Tahawi, al-Tabarani, and Ibn 'Adi. e) 'Abdullah ibn 'Umar: this is the most famous chain of this hadith, recorded by Malik, al-Shafi'i, Ahmad, al-Bukhari and Muslim, Abu Dawud, al-Tirmidhi, Ibn Majah, al-Nasa'i, and others. f) Hakim ibn Hizam: his hadith is found with al-Shafi'i, al-Tayalisi, and Ahmad.
Source pages p. 187

Commentary
This passage is a usul dispute between the Hanafis (and others) and the Malikis regarding the condition for accepting a solitary hadith (khabar al-ahad). The Malikis require that the solitary hadith not contradict the practice (amal) of the people of Medina, deeming Medinan consensus as a higher authority. The author refutes this on multiple grounds. First, he notes that this condition is unique to the Malikis and not binding on others. Second, even if one accepts the condition, it does not apply here because there is no actual consensus of Medinans against the hadith of khiyar al-majlis; many prominent Medinan Companions and Successors affirmed it, including Ibn Abi Dhi'b who declared the hadith widespread. Third, the hadith is not even solitary because seven Companions narrated it through multiple chains, making it well-known (mashhur). The author then lists these Companions with references to major hadith collections. Thus, the Maliki condition fails both in principle and in application.

Key Terms
خبر الآحاد (khabar al-ahad): A hadith narrated by one or a few narrators at any level, not reaching the level of tawatur.
عمل أهل المدينة (amal ahl al-Madina): The established practice of the people of Medina, considered by Malikis as a source of law.
إجماع (ijma): Consensus of scholars; here claimed by Malikis but refuted by the existence of differing Medinan narrators.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why does the claim of Medinan consensus against the hadith of khiyar al-majlis fail?
A) Because the hadith is not authentic.
B) Because many Medinan Companions and Successors affirmed the hadith.
C) Because the Malikis do not accept consensus.
D) Because the hadith is mutawatir.

Key Takeaway
A claimed consensus collapses when prominent members of that community narrate contrary reports, and a hadith transmitted by multiple Companions is not solitary but mashhur, strengthening its authority.

Can a Khabar Ahad Contradict General Fiqh Rules?
Discussion of condition for khabar ahad acceptance regarding general rules

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate the condition that a khabar ahad must not contradict general rules, and apply the Hanafi position that specific texts can create exceptions.

Core Idea
A general rule is a summary of texts; an authentic hadith can be an exception, not a contradiction.

This lesson examines whether a solitary hadith (khabar ahad) must avoid contradicting general fiqh rules to be accepted. Early imams did not require this, but later Malikis derived such a condition from Imam Malik's methodology. We will analyze the reasoning behind both positions and see how this affects a practical fiqh ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition being debated
The condition: a khabar ahad must not contradict general fiqh rules for it to be acted upon.
General rules are derived from induction of many texts.
2
State the Hanafi/majority position
Early imams did not stipulate this condition; a hadith can be an exception to a general rule.
The rule is founded on texts, so a specific text refines it.
3
Understand the Maliki opposing position
Later Malikis reject a khabar ahad that contradicts a general rule because the rule represents multiple texts.
They view the rule as a point of agreement implying consensus.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The rule is only a summary of texts; a specific text takes precedence and creates an exception, not a nullification.
Contradiction does not invalidate the rule; it narrows its application.
5
Apply to a concrete fiqh case
Eating/drinking forgetfully in Ramadan: majority accept the hadith that the fast remains valid; Malikis may reject that hadith and require qada'.
This shows the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المبحث السابع
مخالفة الحديث للقواعد العامة في الفقه الإسلامي

لم يشترط أحد من الأئمة المتقدمين للعمل بخبر الآحاد، أن لا يخالف القواعد العامة، وذلك لأن القواعد العامة أصالة تؤسس عَلَى استقراء نصوص الشارع الحكيم ومن ثَمَّ تصاغ القاعدة بما يتفق مع مضامين النصوص.
إلا أننا وجدنا من خلال استقراء كتب الفقه أن المتأخرين من أصحاب مالك خرجوا بَعْض المسائل عَلَى هَذَا الشرط، وكأنهم فهموا من اجتهادات الإمام مالك أنَّه يشترط ذَلِكَ في خبر الآحاد لصحة العمل بمضمونه.
وعلى هَذَا فخبر الآحاد إذا خالف القواعد العامة فلا يعمل به عندهم، لأن القاعدة موطن اتفاق بَيْنَ الفقهاء من حَيْثُ المضمون الذي يعبر عن فحوى عدد من النصوص عن الشارع، فمخالفة خبر الآحاد لها مسقط للعمل به، إذ يتضمن مخالفة تِلْكَ النصوص المتظافرة عَلَى إثبات ما تضمنته تِلْكَ القاعدة.
ويمكننا الإجابة عن هَذَا الشرط : بأن القاعدة مهما بلغت فلا تعدو كونها تأسيساً عَلَى نصوص، فلا يمكن رد النص بها، والاحتكام حينئذ إلى النص، والتعارض لا يَكُون مبطلاً للقاعدة، بَلْ استثناء من مضمونها (۱).
أثر ذلك في اختلاف الفقهاء
حكم من أكل أو شرب ناسياً في نهار رمضان
اختلف الفقهاء فيمن أكل أو شرب ناسياً في نهار رَمَضَان، هَلْ يفسد صومه أم
لا؟ عَلَى قولين:
الأول: لا يفسد صوم من أكل أو شرب ناسياً، وَهُوَ قَوْل جمهور الفقهاء، وإليه
(۱) مسائل من الفقه المقارن ١ / ٢٤ و ٢٧٥ ، وأثر علل الْحَدِيث : ۱۹۲ - ۱۹۳.
The Seventh Section
Contradiction of the hadith to general rules in Islamic jurisprudence

None of the early imams stipulated for acting upon a hadith ahad that it must not contradict general rules, because general rules are originally established upon induction of the texts of the Wise Lawgiver, and then the rule is formulated in accordance with the contents of the texts.
However, we have found through induction of jurisprudence books that the later followers of Malik derived some issues upon this condition, as if they understood from the ijtihads of Imam Malik that he stipulates that for a khabar ahad for the validity of acting upon its content.
Thus, according to them, if a khabar ahad contradicts the general rules, it is not acted upon, because the general rule is a point of agreement among jurists in terms of its content which expresses the gist of a number of texts from the Lawgiver, so contradicting it nullifies acting upon it, since it entails contradiction of those multiple texts that establish what that rule contains.
We can respond to this condition: that no matter how great a rule is, it is nothing more than a foundation upon texts, so the text cannot be rejected by it, and the reference then is to the text, and the contradiction does not invalidate the rule, but rather it is an exception to its content.
The Effect of That in the Disagreement of Jurists
The Ruling of One Who Eats or Drinks Forgetfully During a Ramadan Day
The jurists differed concerning one who eats or drinks forgetfully during a Ramadan day, whether it invalidates his fast or not? Two opinions:
First: The fast of one who eats or drinks forgetfully is not invalidated, and this is the opinion of the majority of jurists, and to it...
Source pages p. 191

Commentary
This passage is an usul rule discussion about whether a khabar ahad (solitary hadith) can be rejected if it contradicts general fiqh rules. The author states that early imams did not stipulate such a condition. However, later Malikis derived this condition from Imam Malik's methodology. Their reasoning is that general rules represent the consensus of many texts, so an ahad report that opposes them must be discarded. The author refutes this: a rule is only a generalization from texts, and a specific hadith can be an exception to the rule, not a nullification. The example given is the ruling on eating/drinking forgetfully in Ramadan: the majority (including Hanafis and others) hold that the fast is not broken, based on a hadith that 'whoever eats forgetfully should complete his fast.' This hadith is a specific text that serves as an exception to the general rule that eating and drinking invalidate the fast.

Key Terms
القواعد العامة (al-qawa'id al-'ammah): General legal principles derived from the induction of many Shariah texts, such as 'harm must be removed' or 'certainty is not overridden by doubt.'
خبر آحاد (khabar ahad): A hadith that does not reach the level of tawatur; its transmission is from one, two, or a few narrators.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the author, what is the correct response to the condition that a khabar ahad must not contradict general fiqh rules?
A) Such a condition was stipulated by all early imams.
B) A general rule is founded on texts, so a specific text can create an exception without invalidating the rule.
C) A khabar ahad that contradicts a general rule is definitely rejected.
D) The condition is universally accepted among Malikis but not among others.

Key Takeaway
An authentic khabar ahad can refine a general fiqh rule, creating an exception without invalidating the rule.
