The Condition of Not Contradicting General Rules: A Hanafi Response
Refuting the condition that khabar wahid must conform to general rules

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school does not require a khabar wahid to conform to general rules, and evaluate the Maliki counter-argument using the principle that texts precede rules.

Core Idea
A general rule cannot override a specific text; the text is an exception, not a contradiction.

This passage examines a methodological condition sometimes attributed to the later Malikis: that a khabar wahid must not contradict established general rules (qawa'id 'amma). The author first notes that early imams did not impose such a condition. He then refutes it on the grounds that general rules are themselves founded on texts, so a specific, authentic text can constitute an exception to the rule without nullifying it. The lesson clarifies the Hanafi position that textual evidence takes priority over abstract principles.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Condition
State the condition that later Malikis allegedly impose: for a khabar wahid to be acted upon, it must not contradict general legal rules (qawa'id 'amma).
2
Understand the Basis of General Rules
Recognize that general rules are derived inductively from multiple texts of the Lawgiver. They represent the purport of numerous texts, not independent sources.
This is key to the refutation.
3
Analyze the Author's Refutation
Trace the argument: since rules are based on texts, a specific text (khabar wahid) can be an exception to the rule. The rule remains valid but does not override the text.
The author emphasizes that contradiction does not nullify the rule; it creates an exception.
4
Distinguish Contradiction from Exception
Note the subtle point: a khabar wahid that seems to contradict a general rule is not truly contradictory if it is authentic. It simply narrows the rule's scope.
This preserves the integrity of both the rule and the text.
5
Apply to a Concrete Example
Work through the example of the hadith 'لا وصية لوارث' (no bequest to an heir). The general rule from Quran 2:180 permits bequests; the khabar wahid restricts it. Hanafis accept the exception.

However, we found through surveying the books of fiqh that the later followers of Malik extracted some issues based on this condition, as if they understood from the ijtihad of Imam Malik that he stipulates that for a khabar wahid to be valid for acting upon its content. Accordingly, if a khabar wahid contradicts the general rules, it is not acted upon according to them, because the rule is a point of agreement among jurists in terms of the content that expresses the purport of a number of texts from the Lawgiver, so a khabar wahid contradicting it nullifies acting upon it, since it entails contradicting those corroborating texts that establish what that rule entails. We can respond to this condition: that no matter how great a rule is, it does not go beyond being founded on texts, so a text cannot be refuted by it, and the reference then is to the text, and contradiction does not nullify the rule, but rather is an exception from its content.

Commentary
This passage addresses a methodological condition attributed to later Malikis: that a khabar wahid must not contradict established general rules (qawa'id kulliyya) to be accepted. The author first notes that early imams did not impose this condition. General rules are derived from induction of multiple texts; thus they reflect the overall intent of the Lawgiver. However, the author refutes this condition by arguing that rules are secondary to texts; a specific text (khabar wahid) can constitute an exception to the general rule without invalidating the rule itself. The ruling is that a khabar wahid is not automatically rejected for contradicting a general principle; rather, the text is given priority, and the rule is understood as subject to exceptions.

Key Terms
خبر الآحاد (khabar al-ahad): A hadith narrated by one or few transmitters that does not reach the level of tawatur.
قواعد عامة (qawa'id 'amma): General legal principles derived from inductively surveying multiple texts of the Lawgiver.

A khabar wahid is not rejected for contradicting a general rule; the rule is subject to exception by the specific text.

How a Hadith Drives a Fiqh Dispute: Forgetful Eating in Ramadan
Presenting the disagreement on whether forgetful eating breaks the fast

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to analyze the hadith on forgetful eating using Hanafi usul principles and explain the Maliki counterargument based on qiyas.

Core Idea
Forgetful eating does not break the fast: the hadith's explicit command is decisive for the Hanafi school.

This passage presents a classic fiqh dispute as a case study in usul al-fiqh. The issue is whether a person who eats or drinks forgetfully during Ramadan invalidates their fast. The majority, including the Hanafi school, rely on a clear hadith from Abu Hurayra, while the Maliki school disagrees. Our goal is to dissect the textual evidence and see how different usul principles lead to divergent rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the dispute and positions
Read the passage and note the two opinions: (1) fast not broken (majority) and (2) fast broken and qada required (Maliki, etc.).
Focus on the schools mentioned for each position.
2
Locate the primary evidence
The majority cite the hadith: 'If he forgets and eats and drinks, let him complete his fast.' Identify the operative phrase and write it down.
The phrase 'فليتم صومه' is key.
3
Classify the textual category
Apply Hanafi usul terminology: is this phrase an amr (command), zahir (clear), or something else? Determine why the Hanafis consider it binding.
Think about the principle 'al-amr yufidu al-wujub'.
4
Examine the opposing argument
Although the passage does not detail the Maliki proof, infer from the dispute that they likely rely on qiyas with intentional eating or question the hadith's applicability. How would a Hanafi rebut this?
The Hanafi response would emphasize the explicit text over qiyas.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
What is the practical difference between the two rulings? State clearly whether qada is required or not.
This is the real-world outcome of the usul disagreement.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
حكم من أكل أو شرب ناسياً في نهار رمضان
اختلف الفقهاء فيمن أكل أو شرب ناسياً في نهار رَمَضَان، هَلْ يفسد صومه أم لا؟ عَلَى قولين:
الأول: لا يفسد صوم من أكل أو شرب ناسياً، وَهُوَ قَوْل جمهور الفقهاء، وإليه ذهب الحنفية، والشافعية، والحنابلة، والظاهرية، والزيدية، والإمامية.
الثاني: يفسد صوم من أكل أو شرب ناسياً، وَعَلَيْهِ القضاء، وبه قال ربيعة الرأي، والمالكية، والقاسمية من الزيدية.
الأدلة:
استدل القائلون بالمذهب الأول بأدلة عديدة، مِنْهَا:
ما رَوَاهُ أبو هُرَيْرَةَ - - أن رَسُول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قَالَ: «إذا نسي فأكل وشرب فليتم صومه، فإنما أطعمه الله وسقاه». رَوَاهُ عَبد الرزاق، وأحمد، والدارمي، والبخاري، ومسلم، وأبو داود، وابن ماجه، والترمذي، والنسائي، وابن الجارود.
Ruling on one who eats or drinks forgetfully during the day of Ramadan: The jurists differed concerning one who eats or drinks forgetfully during the day of Ramadan: does his fast break or not? On two opinions: First: the fast of one who eats or drinks forgetfully is not broken, and this is the opinion of the majority of jurists, and to it went the Hanafis, Shafi'is, Hanbalis, Zahiris, Zaydis, and Imamis. Second: the fast of one who eats or drinks forgetfully is broken, and he must make it up, and this was said by Rabi'a al-Ra'y, the Malikis, and the Qasimiyya among the Zaydis. Evidence: Those who held the first opinion adduced many proofs, among them: what Abu Hurayra narrated that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: "If he forgets and eats and drinks, let him complete his fast, for indeed Allah has fed him and given him drink." Narrated by 'Abd al-Razzaq, Ahmad, al-Darimi, al-Bukhari, Muslim, Abu Dawud, Ibn Majah, al-Tirmidhi, al-Nasa'i, and Ibn al-Jarud.
Source pages p. 191

Commentary
This passage presents a well-known fiqh dispute as an example of how differences in understanding hadith texts (matn) lead to juristic disagreement. The issue is whether forgetful eating or drinking invalidates the Ramadan fast. The majority, including the Hanafi school, hold that it does not, relying on a clear hadith from Abu Hurayra where the Prophet commands the person to complete his fast, implying no break. The second opinion, attributed to Malik and others, holds that the fast is broken and must be made up. The author here does not provide their proofs but hints that the dispute stems from differing interpretations of the hadith or its reliability. In Hanafi fiqh, this ruling is settled: forgetful eating does not break the fast (Zahir al-Riwayah).

Key Terms
ناسياً (nasiyan): Forgetfully, unintentionally, without intent to break the fast.
صوم (sawm): Fasting, specifically the Ramadan fast in this context.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Hanafis and Malikis
B) Hanafis, Shafi'is, Hanbalis, Zahiris, Zaydis, and Imamis
C) Malikis and Zaydis
D) All schools agree

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that forgetful eating does not break the fast, based on the explicit hadith; the Maliki school disagrees, showing how differing usul principles produce legal diversity.

Unintentional Eating While Fasting: Text vs. Analogy
Analyzing the hadith on unintentional eating and its implications for qada

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the usul principle that governs the conflict between a khabar ahad and qiyas, and evaluate the Hanafi tarjih.

Core Idea
A solitary hadith that is explicit overrides even sound analogy.

This passage examines a classic usul dispute: does the hadith about unintentional eating while fasting override the general principle and qiyas? The Hanafi school prioritizes the explicit text, while the Maliki school upholds qiyas over a khabar ahad that contradicts general principles. Understanding this conflict illuminates the Hanafi rule that there is no ijtihad where there is an explicit text (nas).

Guided Path
1
Identify the two opposing proofs
Locate the hadith (khabar ahad) and the qiyas based on the general principle that unintentional acts do not discharge obligations. Notice how each school uses its preferred proof.
2
Examine the Hanafi position
State why the Hanafi school adopts the hadith and rejects the qiyas. Refer to the principle 'لا اجتهاد مع النص' (no ijtihad where there is a text).
3
Analyze the Maliki counter-argument
Understand the Maliki reasoning: the hadith is a khabar ahad and contradicts the general principle, so it is not acted upon. Also note the claim that the hadith may be restricted to supererogatory fasts.
4
Apply the Hanafi tarjih
The decisive principle: an explicit text (nass) takes precedence over qiyas, even if the text is a khabar ahad. The Hanafi response explicitly states that the analogy is invalid because it contradicts the text.
5
State the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: Hanafi holds no qada required; Maliki holds qada required. This difference stems solely from the methodological weight given to the two types of evidence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفصل الثاني / الاختلاف في الْمَتْن
ووجه الدلالة أن النص ظاهر في أن الأكل والشرب بالنسبة للصائم ناسياً لا يؤثر في الصوم، والنص مطلق من حَيْثُ عدم تقييد الصيام بكونه فرضاً أو نفلاً. قَالَ ابن دَقِيْقِ العِيْدِ: «عمدة من لَمْ يوجب القضاء هَذَا الْحَدِيث وما في معناه أو ما يقاربه، فإنه أمر بالإتمام وسمى الذي يتم صوماً، وظاهره حمله على الحقيقية الشرعية، وإذا كَانَ صوماً وقع مجزئاً، ويلزم من ذَلِكَ عدم وجوب القضاء». ثُمَّ قَالَ: «وإذا دار اللفظ بَيْنَ حمله عَلَى المعنى اللغوي والشرعي، كَانَ حمله عَلَى الشرعي أولى». وأجاب من قَالَ بالمذهب الثاني عن هَذَا الاستدلال بما يأتي: ١. قالوا: هَذَا الْحَدِيث خبر آحاد ، وَقَدْ عارض القاعدة العامة التي تقول: النسيان لا يؤثر في باب المأمورات» . أي لا يؤثر من ناحية براءة ذمة المكلف منه. قَالَ ابن العربي: «أصل مالك في أن خبر الواحد إذا جاء بخلاف القواعد لَمْ يعمل به» فما يفسد الصوم بعدمه على وجه العمد، فإنه يفسده على وجه النسيان، كَمَا في النية، والصيام ركنه الإمساك، فإذا فات الركن في العبادة وجب الإتيان بِهِ، وَقَدْ تعذر هنا، فاقتضى الحكم بفساد صومه. قَالَ ابن دَقِيقِ العِيْدِ: ذهب مالك إلى إيجاب القضاء وَهُوَ القياس، فإن الصوم قَدْ فات ركنه وَهُوَ من باب المأمورات والقاعدة تقتضي أن النسيان لايؤثر في باب المأمورات»، وأفاض الْقَاضِي ابن العربي في تأييد مذهب مالك، فَقَالَ: «هَذَا الْحَدِيْثِ صَحِيح مليح ينظر إلى مطلقه دُونَ تثبت جَمِيع فقهاء الأمصار، وقالوا: من أفطر ناسياً لا قضاء عَلَيْهِ، تعلقاً بقول النبي الهلال في الصَّحِيح: «إن الله أطعمك وسقاك». وتطلع مالك إلى المسألة من طريقها، فأشرف عَلَيْهَا فرأى في مطلعها: أن عَلَيْهِ القضاء؛ لأن الصوم عبارة عن الإمساك عن الأكل، فلا يوجد مَعَ الأكل لأنه ضده، وإذا لَمْ يبق ركنه وحقيقته لَمْ يوجد، وَلَمْ يَكُنْ ممتثلاً ولا قاضياً ما عَلَيْهِ، ألا ترى أن مناقض شرط الصَّلاة وَهُوَ الوضوء: الحدث، إذا وجد سهواً أو عمداً أبطل الصَّلاة؛ لأن الأضداد لا جماع مَعَ أضدادها شرعاً ولاحساً، وَلَيْسَ لهذا الأصل معارض إلا الكلام في الصَّلاة». ٢. حمل الْحَدِيث عَلَى صوم التطوع دُونَ الفرض، بحجة أن الْحَدِيث لَمْ يقع فِيهِ تعيين رَمَضَان، فيصار إلى حمله عَلَى التطوع .. حمل الْحَدِيث عَلَى أمر الصائم الَّذِي تَكُوْن هَذِهِ حاله بإتمام صيام ذَلِكَ اليوم، وسقوط الإثم عَنْهُ ، لَكِنْ يجب عَلَيْهِ قضاؤه). ٤. قال ابن العربي: «وهذا الْحَدِيث يوافق القاعدة في رفع الإثم فقبل في ذَلِكَ، ولا يوافقها في بقاء العبادة بَعْدَ ذهاب ركنها أشتاتاً فَلاَ يعمل بِهِ». وأجيب عَنْهُمْ: أما أولاً: فالقياس المذكور قياس غَيْر صَحِيح؛ لكونه في مقابلة النص، ولا اجتهاد في مورد النص، وَقَدْ ذَكَرَ البرماوي في شرح العمدة: أن شرط القياس عدم مخالفة النص
Chapter Two: Disagreement in the Text. And the aspect of evidence is that the text is apparent that eating and drinking for the fasting person unintentionally does not affect the fast, and the text is absolute in terms of not restricting the fast to being obligatory or supererogatory. Ibn Daqiq al-Eid said: 'The main proof for those who do not require qada is this hadith and what is in its meaning or close to it, for it commands completion and called the one who completes it fasting, and its apparent meaning is to be understood in the legal sense. If it is fasting, it is valid, and consequently qada is not required.' Then he said: 'When a word is ambiguous between its linguistic and legal meanings, understanding it in the legal sense is preferable.' Those who hold the second school responded to this deduction as follows: 1. They said: This hadith is a solitary report (khabar ahad) and it contradicts the general principle that unintentional acts do not affect matters of commands. That is, it does not affect the liability of the obligated person. Ibn al-Arabi said: 'Malik's principle is that if a solitary report contradicts the principles, it is not acted upon.' So whatever invalidates the fast if done intentionally, invalidates it if done unintentionally, as in the case of intention. The pillar of fasting is abstention; if the pillar is missed in an act of worship, it must be performed, and it is impossible here, so the ruling is that the fast is invalid. Ibn Daqiq al-Eid said: 'Malik held that qada is required, and that is analogy, for the pillar of fasting has been missed, and it belongs to the category of commands, and the principle dictates that unintentional acts do not affect commands.' Al-Qadi Ibn al-Arabi elaborated in support of Malik's school, saying: 'This hadith is sound and good, but its unrestricted application is not followed by all jurists of the regions. They said: Whoever breaks his fast unintentionally has no qada, clinging to the Prophet's statement in the Sahih: 'Allah has fed you and given you drink.' But Malik looked at the matter from its proper path and saw that qada is required because fasting means abstaining from eating; so eating cannot coexist with it as it is its opposite. Since its pillar and reality are no longer present, the fast does not exist, and the person is neither fulfilling his obligation nor making it up. Do you not see that what nullifies the condition of prayer, namely ablution, is hadath (impurity); if it occurs forgetfully or intentionally, it invalidates prayer, because opposites do not coexist with their opposites legally or sensibly. There is no counterargument to this principle except speech in prayer.' 2. Restricting the hadith to supererogatory fasts, not obligatory, on the grounds that the hadith does not specify Ramadan, so it is to be applied to supererogatory fasts... 3. Restricting the hadith to the command that the fasting person in this situation complete the fast and sin is removed, but qada is still required. 4. Ibn al-Arabi said: 'This hadith agrees with the principle in removing sin, so it is accepted in that respect, but it does not agree in that an act of worship remains after its pillar has gone in pieces, so it is not acted upon.' And they were answered: As for the first point, the analogy mentioned is invalid because it contradicts the text, and no ijtihad is allowed where there is a text. Al-Birmawi mentioned in Sharh al-Umda that the condition of analogy is that it does not contradict the text.
Source pages p. 193

Commentary
This passage presents a classic usul al-fiqh dispute: does a specific hadith (khabar ahad) override general principles (qawa'id) and qiyas? The Hanafi position is that the hadith about unintentional eating while fasting, which the Prophet said 'Allah fed you and gave you drink', indicates that the fast remains valid and no qada is required. The hadith is absolute, applying to both fard and nafl fasts. Ibn Daqiq al-Eid argues that the hadith is the main proof; it commands completion, calls it fasting in the legal sense, so it is valid, hence no qada. The opposing school (Maliki) argues that the hadith is ahad and contradicts the principle that unintentional acts do not discharge obligations. They analogize to other acts: just as forgetting one's intention invalidates the fast, so does forgetting to abstain. They also claim the hadith may be restricted to voluntary fasts. The Hanafi response counters that analogy cannot stand against an explicit text (no ijtihad in the presence of nas). The text here supports the Hanafi view by rejecting the qiyas as invalid. The author's own conclusion is that the hadith's textual evidence outweighs the analogy.

Key Terms
خبر آحاد (khabar ahad): A hadith that does not reach the level of tawatur, narrated by one or a few chains.
القياس (qiyas): Analogical deduction based on the 'illa of a ruling.
النص (al-nass): An explicit text from Quran or Sunnah with clear ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position presented in this passage, what is the condition for qiyas to be valid?
A) It must be based on a clear 'illa.
B) It must not contradict an explicit text (nas).
C) It must be supported by ijma.
D) It must be preferred by the majority of scholars.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, an explicit text (nass) overrides qiyas even if the text is a khabar ahad; no ijtihad where there is a text.

Deriving the Ruling on Forgetful Eating in Ramadan
Defending a solitary hadith against qiyas objection

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi usul principle of treating a khabar wahid as an independent rule, and complete the istinbat chain to derive the ruling on forgetful eating in Ramadan.

Core Idea
A solitary hadith can establish an independent rule for fasting, overriding general qiyas.

This lesson examines how Hanafi usul deals with a khabar wahid that seems to contradict a general principle. We will follow the author's three-part defense of the hadith on forgetful eating, then trace the istinbat from the general hadith of 'wudi'a 'an ummati' to the specific ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the hadith and its textual category
Locate the primary hadith: 'Whoever breaks his fast in Ramadan forgetfully, there is no qada upon him nor kaffarah.' Classify its transmission (khabar wahid) and its textual category (amm or khass?).
The hadith is a khabar wahid (zanni al-thubut) but its wording is explicit (qati' al-dalala).
2
Understand the objection and the response
The objection is that this khabar wahid contradicts the general principle (qiyas with prayer). Ibn Hajar's response: the hadith is an independent rule for fasting, so analogizing to prayer is invalid.
The author uses Ibn Hajar's argument to defend the hadith's applicability.
3
Analyze the third proof: the Prophet's statement
The phrase 'for Allah fed him and gave him drink' indicates the action is divinely attributed, not to the person, thus not breaking the fast. This is a textual indication (mash'ur) of validity.
Al-Khattabi's explanation reinforces that forgetfulness is a necessity removing liability.
4
Trace the istinbat chain from the general principle
Start with the general hadith 'My ummah has been absolved of mistake, forgetfulness, and compulsion.' This is a general ('amm) text. Apply takhsis to exclude forgetfulness from liability, then use qiyas to include fasting under this general ruling.
The Hanafi principle: al-amm yufidu al-wujub, but here it is used for pardoning.
5
Assess cross-madhhab reading
Some early scholars rejected the hadith because it contradicted qiyas. They required qada. The Hanafi position is that the hadith is authentic and takes precedence over qiyas.
The thamarah al-khilaf: difference in whether qada is required.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفصل الثاني / الاختلاف في الْمَتْن
وكون الْحَدِيث خبر واحد مخالف للقاعدة أمر فِيهِ نظر، وعلل هَذَا الحافظ ابن حجر فَقَالَ: «لأَنَّهُ – يعني: الْحَدِيث المذكور - قاعدة مستقلة بالصيام فمن عارضه بالقياس عَلَى الصَّلاة أدخل قاعدة في قاعدة وَلَوْ فتح باب رد الأحاديث الصَّحِيحَة بمثل هَذَا لما بقي من الْحَدِيث إلا القليل).
وأما ثانياً: فقد ورد التصريح بتعيين رَمَضَان في بَعْض طرق الْحَدِيث، فأخرج ابن خزيمة (٢)، ومن طريقه ابن حبان (٣)، وأخرجه الطبراني () والدارقطني () ، والحاكم () ، ومن طريقه البيهقي () ، كلهم من طريق مُحَمَّد بن عَمْرو بن علقمة، عن أبي سلمة بن عَبْد الرَّحْمن، عن أبي هُرَيْرَةَ، مرفوعاً: «من أفطر في شهر رَمَضَان ناسياً فَلَا قضاء عَلَيْه ولا كفارة».
وأما ثالثاً: فإن قوله صلى الله عليه وسلم في نهاية الْحَدِيث: «فإنما أطعمه الله وسقاه»، دليل عَلَى صحة صومه، فَهُوَ مشعر بأن الفعل الصادر مِنْهُ غَيْر مضاف إليه، والحكم بكونه مفطراً يحتاج إِلَى إضافته إلَيْهِ. لذا قَالَ الخطابي: (معناه أن النسيان ضرورة، والأفعال الضرورية غير مضافة في الحكم إلى فاعلها وغير مؤاخذ بها، والقياس مطرد إلا أن يكثر النسيان، فإنه إذا تتابع أخرج العبادة عن حد القربة، وردها إلى حد العدم).
ثُمَّ إن الحكم بصحة صوم الصائم الآكل أو الشارب ناسياً يتفق مع ما عهدناه من مبادئ التشريع وأصول الاستنباط عن الشارع الحكيم في عدم مؤاخذة المكلف في أبواب حقوق الله تَعَالَى إلا بما فعله عن قصد، ومصداق هَذَا قوله تَعَالَى: ﴿ وَلَكِنْ يُؤَاخِذُكُمْ بِمَا كَسَبَتْ قُلُوبُكُمْ ﴾ ، والنسيان لَيْسَ من كسب القلب). وقد ثبت عن رَسُول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم أَنَّهُ قَالَ: «وضع عن أمتي الخطأ والنسيان وما استكرهوا عَلَيْه». رَوَاهُ الطحاوي، وابن حبان، والدارقطني، والحاكم، والبيهقي. والصوم داخل في عموم هَذَا الأصل. ولهذا يبدو لي رجحان ما ذهب إِلَيْهِ جمهور الفقهاء.
Chapter Two: Differences in the Text. And that the hadith is a solitary hadith contrary to the principle is a matter of consideration. Al-Hafiz Ibn Hajar explained this saying: 'Because it – meaning the mentioned hadith – is an independent rule concerning fasting, so whoever opposes it by analogy with prayer introduces one rule into another, and if the door of rejecting authentic hadith by such means were opened, little of the hadith would remain.' Secondly: There has come explicit specification of Ramadan in some chains of the hadith: Ibn Khuzaymah, and through him Ibn Hibban, and al-Tabarani, al-Daraqutni, al-Hakim, and through him al-Bayhaqi, all from the route of Muhammad ibn 'Amr ibn 'Alqamah, from Abu Salamah ibn 'Abd al-Rahman, from Abu Hurayrah, marfu': 'Whoever breaks his fast in the month of Ramadan forgetfully, there is no qada upon him nor kaffarah.' Thirdly: The Prophet's saying at the end of the hadith: 'For Allah fed him and gave him drink' is evidence for the validity of his fast, for it indicates that the action emanating from him is not attributed to him, and the ruling that it breaks the fast requires its attribution to him. Hence al-Khattabi said: 'Its meaning is that forgetfulness is a necessity, and necessary actions are not attributed in ruling to their doer and are not held against him, and analogy applies except when forgetfulness becomes frequent, for if it recurs, it takes the act of worship out of the limit of devotion and returns it to the limit of nullity.' Further, the ruling that the fasting person who eats or drinks forgetfully has a valid fast agrees with what we have witnessed of the principles of legislation and the methods of inference from the Wise Lawgiver in not holding the accountable person liable in matters of the rights of Allah except for what he does intentionally, and the confirmation of this is His statement: 'But He will hold you accountable for what your hearts have earned,' and forgetfulness is not from the earnings of the heart. And it has been established from the Messenger of Allah that he said: 'My ummah has been absolved of mistake, forgetfulness, and what they are compelled to do.' This was narrated by al-Tahawi, Ibn Hibban, al-Daraqutni, al-Hakim, and al-Bayhaqi. And fasting is included in the generality of this principle. Therefore, it appears to me the preponderance of what the majority of jurists have held.
Source pages p. 195

Commentary
This passage is a scholarly analysis of the hadith regarding forgetful eating or drinking in Ramadan and the resulting ruling that no qada (make-up) or kaffarah (expiation) is required. The author first addresses an objection: that the hadith is a khabar wahid (solitary tradition) contradicting the general principle (qiyas with prayer). He cites Ibn Hajar's refutation, who argues that the hadith establishes an independent rule for fasting, so analogizing to prayer would improperly merge two distinct fields. Second, the author points out that some chains of the hadith explicitly specify 'Ramadan,' strengthening its applicability. Third, he analyzes the Prophet's phrase 'for Allah fed him and gave him drink' to show that the action is divinely attributed, not to the person, thus not breaking the fast. He then quotes al-Khattabi's explanation that forgetfulness is a necessity, and necessary acts do not incur liability unless forgetfulness becomes habitual. The author concludes by connecting this to the Qur'anic principle that accountability is only for intentional acts (Quran 2:225) and the hadith absolving the ummah of error, forgetfulness, and compulsion. Fasting falls under this general principle, so the ruling is sound.

Key Terms
نسيان (nisyan): Forgetfulness; lack of intention in an action.
قضاء (qada): Making up a missed obligatory fast.
كفارة (kaffarah): Expiation required for breaking a Ramadan fast intentionally.
خبر واحد (khabar wahid): A solitary hadith not reaching tawatur.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the hadith cited, what is the ruling on someone who eats forgetfully in Ramadan?
A) Qada is required, but not kaffarah.
B) Both qada and kaffarah are required.
C) Neither qada nor kaffarah is required.
D) The fast is invalid, but no kaffarah.

Key Takeaway
A solitary hadith with clear wording can establish a specific rule for fasting, overriding general qiyas.

Hadith Abbreviation and Its Impact on Fiqh Differences
Four opinions on abbreviating hadith with a practical example

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four opinions on abbreviating hadith and apply the preferred opinion to determine the permissibility of a given abbreviation.

Core Idea
Abbreviating a hadith is permissible only if the omitted part is independent and the narrator is knowledgeable.

This passage explores the permissibility of abbreviating hadiths. Scholars differed, leading to four main opinions. The fourth, preferred by Ibn al-Salah, allows abbreviation under strict conditions. Understanding this helps explain why narrators' abbreviations can cause juristic disagreements, as seen in the famous wudu hadith.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Four Opinions
List the four opinions on abbreviating hadith: absolute prohibition, absolute permissibility (with al-'Iraqi's condition), conditional permissibility if the full version is narrated elsewhere, and conditional permissibility if the narrator is knowledgeable and the omitted part is unrelated.
2
Examine the Reasoning
Understand the reasoning behind each opinion. The first fears defect; the second allows; the third requires a full narrative elsewhere; the fourth focuses on the narrator's expertise and independence of the omitted part.
3
Note Conditions of the Preferred Opinion
The fourth opinion requires the narrator to be knowledgeable and discerning, and the omitted part must be distinct and unrelated to the transmitted part, so that meaning is not impaired.
4
Analyze the Concrete Example
Shu'bah abbreviated the hadith 'No wudu except from sound or wind,' omitting the context 'If any of you is in prayer...' This led to a different understanding compared to the full version.
5
Identify the Thamarah al-Khilaf
The practical consequence: from the abbreviated version, one might think wudu is required after any sound or wind, while the full version limits it to within prayer and requires both hearing and smell.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المبحث الثامن
اختلاف الحديث بسبب الاختصار
اختلف الناس في جواز اختصار الحديث، والاقتصار على بعضه، وكانت لهم مذاهب في هذا:
الأول: المنع مطلقاً من اختصار الحديث، بناءاً على المنع من الرواية بالمعنى لأن حذف بعض الحديث ورواية بعضه ربما أحدث الخلل فيه، والمختصر لا يشعر.
الثاني: الجواز مطلقاً، وبه قال مجاهد، ويحيى بن معين، وغيرهما. قال الحافظ العراقي: ينبغي تقييد الإطلاق بما إذا لم يكن المحذوف متعلقاً بالمأتي به تعلقاً يخل بالمعنى حذفه كالاستثناء والحال ونحو ذلك، كما سيأتي في القول الرابع. فإن كان كذلك لم يجز بلا خلاف، وبه جزم أبو بكر الصيرفي وغيره، وهو واضح.
الثالث: إن لم يكن رواه على التمام مرة أخرى هو أو غيره لم يجز، وإن كان رواه على التمام مرة أخرى هو أو غيره جاز.
الرابع: يجوز اختصار الحديث والاقتصار على بعضه إذا كان فاعل ذلك عالماً عارفاً، وكان ما تركه متميزاً عما نقله غير متعلق به، بحيث لا يختل البيان، ولا تختلف الدلالة فيما نقله بترك ما تركه.
وهذا المذهب هو الذي صححه ابن الصلاح وغيره، وعلل ذلك بقوله: «لأن الذي نقله والذي تركه - والحالة هذه - بمنزلة خبرين منفصلين في أمرين لا تعلق لأحدهما بالآخر».
وقد ترتب على اختصار بعض الرواة للأحاديث، خلاف بين الفقهاء في بعض جزئيات الفقه الإسلامي، ونستطيع أن نمثل ذلك بما يأتي:
روى شعبة، عن سهيل بن أبي صالح عن أبيه، عن أبي هريرة عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال: لا وضوء إلا من صوت أو ريح. هكذا روى شعبة الحديث مختصراً، نبّه على ذلك حفاظ الحديث ونقاده، فأبو حاتم الرازي يقول: «هذا وهم، اختصر شعبة متن هذا الحديث، فقال: لا وضوء إلا من صوت أو ريح، ورواه أصحاب سهيل عن سهيل، عن أبيه، عن أبي هريرة، عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال: إذا كان أحدكم في الصلاة فوجد ريحاً من نفسه فلا يخرجن حتى يسمع صوتاً أو يجد ريحاً».
Eighth Section: Difference of Hadith Due to Abbreviation. People differed regarding the permissibility of abbreviating a hadith and restricting it to part of it, and they had schools of thought in this: First: absolute prohibition of abbreviating a hadith, based on the prohibition of narration by meaning because deleting some of the hadith and narrating part of it might cause a defect in it, and the abbreviated does not indicate. Second: absolute permissibility, and this was said by Mujahid, Yahya ibn Ma'in, and others. Al-Hafiz al-'Iraqi said: It is necessary to restrict the absolute to when the deleted part is not related to the narrated part in a way that its deletion would impair the meaning, such as an exception, a circumstantial clause, and the like, as will come in the fourth opinion. If it is like that, it is not permissible without dispute, and Abu Bakr al-Sayrafi and others asserted it, and it is clear. Third: If he did not narrate it in full another time, he or someone else, it is not permissible; if he narrated it in full another time, he or someone else, it is permissible. Fourth: It is permissible to abbreviate a hadith and restrict it to part of it if the doer is knowledgeable and discerning, and what he left out is distinct from what he transmitted, not related to it, such that the exposition is not impaired and the indication does not differ in what he transmitted due to leaving what he left. This school is the one that Ibn al-Salah and others declared correct, and he justified it by saying: 'Because what he transmitted and what he left out - in this situation - are like two separate reports regarding two matters, no relation between them.' And the abbreviation of some narrators of hadith resulted in disagreement among jurists in some particulars of Islamic jurisprudence, and we can exemplify that with the following: Shu'bah narrated from Suhayl ibn Abi Salih from his father from Abu Hurayra from the Prophet, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, said: 'No wudu except from sound or wind.' This is how Shu'bah narrated the hadith abbreviated. The hadith memorizers and critics pointed that out. Abu Hatim al-Razi says: 'This is an error; Shu'bah abbreviated the text of this hadith and said: No wudu except from sound or wind, while the companions of Suhayl narrated from Suhayl, from his father, from Abu Hurayra, from the Prophet, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, said: If any of you is in prayer and finds wind from himself, let him not leave until he hears a sound or finds a smell.'
Source pages p. 196

Commentary
This passage is a detailed discussion on the permissibility of abbreviating hadiths and its impact on juristic differences. The author presents four opinions: (1) absolute prohibition, (2) absolute permissibility but with the condition from al-'Iraqi that the omitted part must not affect meaning, (3) permissibility only if the full version has been narrated elsewhere, and (4) permissibility if the narrator is knowledgeable and the omitted part is independent. The author follows Ibn al-Salah in preferring the fourth opinion. The passage then provides a concrete example: Shu'bah's abbreviation of the hadith about wudu from sound or wind led to a different understanding. The full version includes the context of being in prayer, which affects the ruling on when to leave prayer. This shows how abbreviation can cause juristic disagreements.

Key Terms
اختصار الحديث (ikhtiṣār al-ḥadīth): رواية جزء من الحديث دون باقيه
الرواية بالمعنى (al-riwāyah bil-maʿnā): رواية الحديث بلفظ غير لفظ النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم مع أداء المعنى

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What was the error in Shu'bah's narration of the hadith about wudu?
A) He narrated it with a wrong chain.
B) He omitted the context of being in prayer, changing the ruling.
C) He added words not from the Prophet.
D) He narrated it twice with different meanings.

Key Takeaway
The permissibility of hadith abbreviation depends on the narrator's knowledge and the independence of the omitted part; violation can lead to fiqh differences.

ورود حديث الآحاد فيما تعم به البلوى: Hanafi Principle on Solitary Reports
Defining and defending the Hanafi principle on ahad hadith in widespread matters

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi principle regarding ahad hadith in matters of general necessity, identify the primary evidence from the actions of the Companions, and analyze the counter-argument from the opposing school.

Core Idea
A solitary report in a matter of general necessity is not acceptable; corroboration is required.

The Hanafis hold that matters which occur frequently and are needed by all people (ما تعم به البلوى) must be transmitted by a large number of narrators; if a solitary report (خبر الآحاد) is brought for such a matter, it raises doubt and requires hesitation. This lesson examines the evidence from the actions of Caliphs Abu Bakr and Umar, who refused to act on solitary reports until corroborated, and the counter-argument that they themselves accepted solitary reports in other cases.

Guided Path
1
Define the term
Understand the meaning of 'ما تعم به البلوى' as matters that occur frequently and all people need to know.
2
Identify the Hanafi principle
The Hanafis argue that such matters naturally call for mass transmission, so a solitary report is suspect.
3
Examine the evidence from Abu Bakr
Abu Bakr did not accept al-Mughirah's solitary report about the grandmother's inheritance until a second companion confirmed it.
4
Examine the evidence from Umar
Umar demanded multiple witnesses for the hadith on seeking permission before accepting it from Abu Musa.
5
Analyze the counter-argument
The opposing school points out that the same caliphs accepted solitary reports in other instances, such as Abu Bakr accepting 'A'ishah's report about the garment.
The passage cuts off but this is the gist.

المبحث التاسع
ورود حديث الآحاد فيما تعم به البلوى
يجدر بنا قَبْلَ الدخول في هَذِهِ المسألة أن نتعرف عَلَى المقصود من قَوْل الفقهاء: «ما تعم به البلوى». فمعناه عندهم ما كثر وقوعه ويحتاج إلى العِلْم بِهِ جَمِيع الناس، وما كَانَتْ هَذِهِ صورته فإن الدواعي تدعو إلى أن ينقله العدد الجمّ فيكون بمثابة الخبر المتواتر أو المَشْهُور، ووروده بخبر الآحاد ريبة توجب التوقف في قبول الخبر وهذا ما جنح إليه الحنفية ().
واستدلوا بالآثار الَّتِي رويت عن صحابة رَسُول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم، مِمَّا يدل ظاهرها عَلَى ذَلِكَ:
العمل بهذا الشرط، ومن
١. ماروي عن قبيصة بن ذؤيب قَالَ: جاءت الجدة إلى أبي بكر تسأله ميراثها، قَالَ فَقَالَ لها: «مالك في كتاب الله شيء، ومالك في سنة رَسُول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم شيء، فارجعي حَتَّى أسأل الناس»، فسأل الناس فقال المغيرة بن شعبة: حضرت رَسُول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم فأعطاها السدس، فَقَالَ أبو بكر: هَلْ معك غيرك؟ فقام مُحَمَّد بن مسلمة الأنصاري فَقَالَ مِثْل ما قَالَ المغيرة بن شعبة فأنفذه لها أبو بكر (۱).
٢. عن أبي سعيد الخدري قَالَ: استأذن أبو موسى عَلَى عمر، فَقَالَ: «السلام عليكم أأدخل؟» قَالَ عمر: واحدة، ثُمَّ سكت ساعة، ثُمَّ قَالَ: «السلام عليكم أأدخل؟» قَالَ عمر: اثنان، ثُمَّ سكت ساعة فَقَالَ: «السلام عليكم أأدخل؟» فَقَالَ عمر: ثلاث، ورجع أبو موسى، فَقَالَ عمر للبواب: ما صنع؟ قَالَ: رجع. قَالَ: عَلي بِهِ، فلما جاءه قَالَ: ما هذا الَّذِي صنعت؟ قَالَ: السنة. قَالَ: السنة؟ والله لتأتيني عَلَى هَذَا ببرهان أو بينة أو لأفعلن بك. قَالَ: فأتانا ونحن رفقة من الأنصار فَقَالَ: يا معشر الأنصار ألستم أعلم الناس بحديث رَسُول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم؟ ألم يقل رَسُول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم: «الاستئذان ثلاث، فإن أذن لَكَ، وإلا فارجع»، فجعل القوم يمازحونه، قَالَ أبو سعيد: ثُمَّ رفعت رأسي إِلَيْهِ فقلت: فما أصابك في هَذَا من العقوبة فأنا شريكك. قَالَ: فأتى عمر فأخبره بِذَلِكَ، فَقَالَ عمر: ما كنت علمت بهذا (۲).
ولا معارض من الصَّحَابَة لفعل الخليفتين، فكان إجماعاً مِنْهُمْ عَلَى مضمون فعلهما (۳).
وأجيب عن استدلالهم هذا:
بأن دعوى الإجماع منقوضة بفعل عدد من الصحابة، إذ قبل كثير منهم أخبار الآحاد وقبلوها، بل ورد هذا عن الخليفتين أميري المؤمنين اللذين استدلوا بفعلهما،
ومن ذلك:
-١- قبل الخليفة أبو بكر حديث ابنته أم المؤمنين عائشة في قدر الثوب الذي
Chapter Nine: The Coming of Solitary Reports in Matters of General Necessity. It behooves us before entering into this issue to know what the jurists mean by 'what is of general necessity'. According to them, its meaning is that which frequently occurs and which all people need to know. When something is of this nature, the motivations (to transmit it) would call for a large number (of transmitters) to convey it, so it would be like a mutawatir or mashhur report. Its coming as a solitary report raises doubt that necessitates hesitation in accepting the report. This is what the Hanafis inclined towards. They argued with the reports narrated from the Companions of the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, the apparent meaning of which indicates that: action upon this condition, and among them: 1. What is narrated from Qabisah ibn Dhu'ayb who said: The grandmother came to Abu Bakr asking for her inheritance. He said to her: 'You have nothing in the Book of Allah, and you have nothing in the Sunnah of the Messenger of Allah. So go back until I ask the people.' He asked the people, and al-Mughirah ibn Shu'bah said: I witnessed the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, and he gave her the sixth. So Abu Bakr said: 'Is there anyone else with you?' Then Muhammad ibn Maslamah al-Ansari stood and said the same as al-Mughirah ibn Shu'bah, so Abu Bakr executed it for her. (1) 2. From Abu Sa'id al-Khudri who said: Abu Musa sought permission from 'Umar, saying: 'Peace be upon you, may I enter?' 'Umar said: 'One,' then paused for a while. Then he said: 'Peace be upon you, may I enter?' 'Umar said: 'Two,' then paused for a while. Then he said: 'Peace be upon you, may I enter?' 'Umar said: 'Three.' So Abu Musa went back. 'Umar asked the doorman: 'What did he do?' He said: 'He went back.' He said: 'Bring him to me.' When he came, he said: 'What is this that you did?' He said: 'The Sunnah.' He said: 'The Sunnah? By Allah, you must bring me proof or evidence for this, or I will do such and such to you.' He said: So he came to us, and we were a group of Ansar. He said: 'O Ansar! Are you not the most knowledgeable of people about the hadith of the Messenger of Allah? Did not the Messenger of Allah say: "Seeking permission is three times; if you are given permission, (enter), otherwise, go back."' The people began to joke with him. Abu Sa'id said: Then I raised my head to him and said: 'Whatever punishment befalls you in this, I am your partner.' He said: Then he came to 'Umar and informed him of that. So 'Umar said: 'I did not know this before.' (2) There is no opposition from the Companions to the action of the two caliphs, so it was a consensus from them on the content of their action. (3) And it was answered regarding their argument: that the claim of consensus is refuted by the action of a number of Companions, for many of them accepted solitary reports and acted upon them, indeed this is reported from the two caliphs themselves, the commanders of the faithful, whose action they used as proof. Among that: (1) The caliph Abu Bakr accepted the hadith of his daughter, the Mother of the Believers 'A'ishah, concerning the amount of the garment which...
Source pages p. 199

Commentary
This passage opens with a new section (المبحث التاسع) addressing a key usul principle: how to treat isolated reports (خبر الآحاد) when they pertain to matters of general necessity (ما تعم به البلوى). The author first defines the term: matters that occur frequently and which all people need to know. According to the Hanafis, the natural motivation for transmitting such matters would lead to widespread transmission, so their coming as solitary reports creates suspicion requiring pause before acceptance. The Hanafi evidence is two examples from the Companions Abu Bakr and Umar, who both refused to act on single reports until corroborated. In the first example, Abu Bakr asked the grandmother to return until he could ask others, and only acted after two Companions testified. In the second, Umar threatened to punish Abu Musa for acting on a solitary report about the etiquette of seeking permission, until Abu Musa brought multiple Ansar witnesses. The author then notes the claim that there was no opposition from the Companions, implying consensus. However, the passage then presents a counter-argument: many Companions, including the very same caliphs, accepted solitary reports in other instances. The text begins to list examples but cuts off. The lesson thus presents the Hanafi position and the beginning of the rebuttal.

Key Terms
ما تعم به البلوى (ma ta'ummu bihi al-balwa): Matters that occur frequently and which all people need to know.
خبر الآحاد (khabar al-ahad): A solitary report that does not meet the conditions of tawatur or shuhrah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafis, what is the definition of 'ما تعم به البلوى' (matters of general necessity)?
A) Matters that are widely known by everyone
B) Matters that occur frequently and all people need to know
C) Matters that are mentioned in the Quran
D) Matters that are agreed upon by the scholars

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school requires that matters of general necessity be established by widely transmitted reports (tawatur/shuhrah), not by solitary reports.

Khabar al-Wahid in Matters of Common Occurrence: Debating the Companions' Practice
Presents opponents' evidence from Abu Bakr and Umar and the rebuttal citing their acceptance of khabar al-wahid

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the opposing positions on whether the Companions accepted khabar al-wahid in matters of common occurrence, and evaluate the Hanafi rebuttal using counterexamples from Abu Bakr and Umar.

Core Idea
The Companions accepted khabar al-wahid in common matters – Abu Bakr and Umar proved it themselves.

This lesson examines a key usul dispute: did the Companions reject khabar al-wahid in widespread matters? Some scholars argue yes, citing incidents where Abu Bakr and Umar demanded corroboration. However, the Hanafi school demonstrates that the same caliphs accepted single-narrator reports in equally common matters. You will analyze both sets of evidence and understand why the Hanafi position is supported by the Companions' actions.

Guided Path
1
State the opponents' claim and evidence
Identify the incidents of the grandmother's inheritance (Abu Bakr) and istidhan (Umar) where corroboration was sought. Understand how these are used to argue that the Companions did not accept khabar al-wahid in common matters.
Note that the opponents also claim a consensus (ijma) of the Companions on this rejection.
2
Identify the Hanafi counter-evidence
Review the incidents where Abu Bakr accepted Aisha's report about the shroud and day of death, and Umar accepted her report about ghusl from circumcision. Both are explicitly described as matters of common occurrence (mimma ta'ummu bihi al-balwa).
3
Analyze the distinction between the incidents
Understand the Hanafi response: Abu Bakr's hesitation was because the grandmother's inheritance was a well-known matter (shuhra), not due to rejection of khabar; Umar's demand was either a test or because he was unaware of the hadith. The counter-examples show clear acceptance.
This step addresses the apparent contradiction.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: if khabar al-wahid is accepted in common matters, many rulings can be established by single-narrator reports; if not, tawatur or public knowledge is required. The Hanafi position allows flexibility in deriving rulings.
This is the core of the usul dispute.
5
Evaluate the tarjih (preferred view)
Based on the textual evidence, the Hanafi position is stronger because it directly cites the same caliphs accepting khabar al-wahid. The opponents' evidence is reinterpreted without contradicting the principle of acceptance.
The passage favors the Hanafi view.

'Umar said: 'You have differed in my presence, and you are the best of Badr, so how will the people after you be?' So he sent to 'A'ishah, and she said: 'When the circumcised part passes the circumcised part, ghusl becomes obligatory.' Then 'Umar said: 'I do not want to hear anyone saying 'water is from water' except that I will make him an example.' And this matter is also of common occurrence. And other incidents and traditions that strengthen in the mind of the observer the acceptance of ahad reports in matters of common occurrence or otherwise. As for the two incidents they used as evidence, it is possible to answer about them: that Abu Bakr hesitated regarding the report of al-Mughirah because what he reported was a well-known matter, so he wanted

Commentary
This passage presents a key dispute in usul al-fiqh regarding the acceptance of khabar al-wahid (single-narrator hadith) in matters that are widespread and affect the general public (ma ta'ummu bihi al-balwa). The opponents argue that the Companions, particularly Abu Bakr and Umar, did not accept such reports in these matters, citing two incidents: the case of the grandmother's inheritance where Abu Bakr sought corroboration, and the story of istidhan (seeking permission) where Umar demanded proof. They claim this constituted a consensus (ijma) of the Companions. The rebuttal, however, demonstrates that the same caliphs accepted khabar al-wahid in equally widespread matters: Abu Bakr accepted Aisha's report about the shroud and the day of the Prophet's death, and Umar accepted her report about ghusl from the meeting of circumcised parts. The author concludes that these examples strengthen the position that khabar al-wahid is accepted even in matters of common occurrence. The response to the specific incidents is cut off, but it hints that Abu Bakr's hesitation was due to the report being of a well-known matter (shuhra), not because of a general principle of rejection. This is a classic Hanafi position, as the Hanafi school generally accepts khabar al-wahid without requiring public knowledge in matters of common occurrence, unlike some other schools.

Key Terms
خبر الواحد (khabar al-wahid): A hadith narrated by one or a few narrators, not reaching the level of tawatur.
ما تعم به البلوى (ma ta'ummu bihi al-balwa): Matters that are widespread and involve the general public, such that knowledge of them should be common.
إجماع (ijma): Consensus of the mujtahidun of the ummah on a ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following incidents is used in the passage to show that Abu Bakr accepted a khabar al-wahid in a matter of common occurrence?
A) The hadith about the grandmother's inheritance from al-Mughirah ibn Shu'bah
B) The hadith about the shroud and day of the Prophet's death from Aisha
C) The hadith about seeking permission from Abu Musa al-Ash'ari
D) The hadith about ghusl from meeting of circumcised parts from Aisha

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi position that khabar al-wahid is accepted in matters of common occurrence is supported by the practice of Abu Bakr and Umar.

Acceptance of Khabar al-Ahad in Matters of Common Need
Discussion of the principle and historical incidents

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate the arguments for and against accepting khabar al-ahad in matters of common need and state the majority Hanafi position.

Core Idea
A solitary report (khabar al-ahad) is accepted in all matters if its conditions are met; common need is no exception.

This passage resolves a key usul debate: whether khabar al-ahad is acceptable in matters of widespread occurrence. The author presents companion incidents—Abu Bakr and Umar—used by some to argue rejection, then refutes them and affirms the majority rule.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contested rule
Is khabar al-ahad accepted in matters of common need (ta'ummu bihi al-balwa)? Some argue that the companions hesitated, indicating rejection.
2
Analyze the two historical incidents
Examine the incidents of Abu Bakr questioning Aisha about the shroud and Umar accepting Aisha's report on ghusl. What do they suggest about the acceptance of solitary reports?
Focus on why the companions acted as they did.
3
Examine the author's refutation
The author explains that Abu Bakr and Umar sought verification, not rejection. Their actions were precautionary, not a denial of the principle.
This is the key counterargument against those who claim rejection.
4
State the preponderant view
The majority of scholars (جمهور) hold that khabar al-ahad is acted upon in all matters if it meets the conditions of acceptance. The proofs for acting on khabar al-ahad do not differentiate.
This is the conclusion of the passage.
5
Connect to the general usul principle
The rule that khabar al-ahad is accepted universally is derived from the general commands in the Quran and Sunnah to follow the Prophet's reports, which are unconditional.

أما الحادثتان اللتان استدلوا بهما، فيمكن الإجابة عنها: بأن أبا بكر إنما توقف في خبر المغيرة، لأن ما أخبر عنه أمر مشهور، فأراد التثبت فيه (١). وأما عمر فلأن أبا موسى أخبره الحديث عقب إنكاره عليه، فأراد عمر الاستثبات في خبره لهذه القرينة (٢). فالراجح ما ذهب إليه جمهور أهل العلم من أن خبر الآحاد يعمل به وإن كان مما تعم به البلوى إذا استوفى شروط القبول للاحتجاج به من حيث ثبوته عن رسول الله ، ذلك أن الأدلة الشرعية الدالة على وجوب العمل بخبر الآحاد لم تفرق بين عموم البلوى وغيرها.
Chapter Two: Discrepancy in the Text. (1) 201. God... He shrouded the Prophet therein. Al-Bukhari, Muslim, and others narrated from Aisha that she entered upon Abu Bakr and he asked: 'In how many cloths did you shroud the Prophet?' She said: 'In three Sahuli garments, no shirt nor turban.' And he asked: 'On which day did the Prophet die?' She said: 'Monday.' Both matters (the shroud and the day of his death) are of common concern. And the Caliph Umar, the Commander of the Faithful, accepted the report of the Mother of the Believers Aisha regarding the obligation of ghusl from the meeting of the two circumcised parts. Al-Tahawi narrated from Ubaydullah ibn Adi ibn al-Khiyar: The companions of the Prophet were discussing ghusl from janaba in the presence of Umar. Some said: 'When the two circumcised parts meet, ghusl becomes obligatory.' Others said: 'Water is from water.' Umar said: 'You have differed with me while you are the best of Badr; how will the people after you? Ali said: 'O Commander of the Faithful, if you want to know, send to the wives of the Prophet and ask them.' So he sent to Aisha, who said: 'When the two circumcised parts meet, ghusl becomes obligatory.' Umar then said: 'I will not hear anyone say "water is from water" except I make an example of him.' This is also a matter of common concern. And other incidents and reports that strengthen in the observer the acceptance of solitary reports in matters of common concern or otherwise. As for the two incidents they adduced, the response is: Abu Bakr paused regarding the report of Mughirah because what he reported was a well-known matter, so he wanted to verify it. As for Umar, because Abu Musa reported the hadith after his denial of it, so Umar wanted to confirm his report due to this circumstance. The preponderant view is that of the majority of scholars: solitary reports are acted upon even if they are in matters of common concern, provided they meet the conditions of acceptance for being evidence from the Prophet, because the legal proofs indicating the obligation of acting upon solitary reports do not distinguish between general common concern and other matters.

Commentary
This passage discusses the usul rule regarding the acceptance of khabar al-ahad (solitary report) in matters that are of common occurrence (mimma ta'ummu bihi al-balwa). The author presents two historical incidents. First, Abu Bakr al-Siddiq (ra) questioned Aisha (ra) about the shroud and death day of the Prophet, but later he accepted her report. Some used this to argue that Abu Bakr initially hesitated, implying that solitary reports are not accepted in common matters. However, the author explains that Abu Bakr did not reject the report; he merely sought verification because the matter was well-known. Second, Umar ibn al-Khattab (ra) at first denied the report that water is from water, but after Aisha informed him, he accepted and warned against contradicting it. The author argues that these incidents actually support the acceptance of khabar al-ahad in common matters. The preponderant view is that of the majority of scholars who hold that solitary reports are to be acted upon in all matters if they fulfill the conditions of acceptance, as the general proofs for accepting khabar al-ahad are unconditional.

Key Terms
خبر الآحاد (khabar al-ahad): A report transmitted by one or a few narrators, not reaching the level of tawatur.
تعم به البلوى (ta'ummu bihi al-balwa): Matters that are of common occurrence and general need among the people.

Understanding the First Opinion on Touching the Penis: The Authority of Early Scholars
List of scholars supporting the first opinion

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the legal significance of a list of scholars supporting a fiqh opinion and explain why it does not constitute ijma'.

Core Idea
A list of supporters indicates strength, not consensus.

This passage introduces a classic dispute in uṣūl al-fiqh: whether touching the penis invalidates wuḍū’. The author lists the prominent early scholars who held that it does. Understanding how such lists function in legal argumentation is key to distinguishing between evidence and authority. In this lesson, we will examine the first opinion and its supporters, and learn how to evaluate such citations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed ruling
Determine the exact fiqh issue: does touching the private part (penis) break wudu?
This is a known point of ikhtilaf between schools.
2
Recognize the first opinion
The first opinion states that wudu is broken and must be renewed upon touching.
Note that this is the view of the majority of listed scholars.
3
Analyze the list of supporters
Examine the names: they include many Companions and later Tabi'un. What does their agreement indicate? Is it evidence of ijma?
Ijma requires unanimous agreement of all Mujtahids, not just a selection.
4
Understand the argument
The supporters likely relied on a specific hadith (e.g., hadith of Busra). Their acceptance suggests the hadith was considered authentic and applicable.
The passage itself does not cite the hadith, but the context implies it.
5
Note the limitation
The list does not settle the dispute; it only shows that the first opinion has strong early support. Other schools, like the Hanafis, hold the opposite view.
Recognize that a list of supporters is an argument of authority, not a conclusive proof.

اختلف الفقهاء في من مس ذكره أو ما في معناه، هل ينتقض وضوؤه أم لا؟
وافترقوا على قولين:
الأول: إذا مس المتوضئ فرجه انتقض وضوؤه، وعليه الوضوء من جديد، وبه قال جمهور أهل العلم من الصحابة فمن بعدهم، منهم: عمر بن الخطاب، وابنه عبد الله ابن عمر، والبراء بن عازب، وزيد بن خالد الجهني، وجابر بن عبد الله، وأبو أيوب الأنصاري، وزيد بن ثابت وعائشة، وأم حبيبة، وبسرة بنت صفوان، وعطاء بن أبي رباح، وطاووس، وعروة بن الزبير، وسليمان بن يسار وأبان بن عثمان)، والزهري، و مجاهد، ومكحول، وجابر بن زيد، والشعبي، وعكرمة، ومصعب بن سعد
First Model: Breaking Wudu by Touching the Penis. The jurists differed concerning one who touches his penis or the like; does his wudu break or not? They split into two opinions. First: If the one in wudu touches his private part, his wudu breaks, and he must perform wudu anew. This is the view of the majority of scholars from the Companions and after them, including: Umar ibn al-Khattab, his son Abdullah ibn Umar, al-Bara' ibn Azib, Zayd ibn Khalid al-Juhani, Jabir ibn Abdullah, Abu Ayyub al-Ansari, Zayd ibn Thabit, Aisha, Umm Habiba, Busra bint Safwan, Ata' ibn Abi Rabah, Tawus, Urwa ibn al-Zubayr, Sulayman ibn Yasar, Aban ibn Uthman, al-Zuhri, Mujahid, Makhul, Jabir ibn Zayd, al-Sha'bi, Ikrima, and Mus'ab ibn Sa'd.
Source pages p. 202

Commentary
This passage presents the first example of how differences in hadith lead to differences in fiqh rulings. The issue is whether touching the penis invalidates wudu. The author states that jurists are divided into two opinions. He then lists the supporters of the first opinion: that wudu is broken. The list includes many prominent Companions (like Umar, his son, Jabir, Aisha) and later scholars (like Ata', Tawus, al-Zuhri). This indicates the strength of this view among early generations. Note that the second opinion will be discussed subsequently. This example shows that even though there is a solitary hadith on the matter (not mentioned here), the acceptance of that hadith by these scholars leads them to adopt this ruling. The author is showing how the text of a hadith (or its interpretation) causes a difference of opinion.

Key Terms
نقض الوضوء (naqd al-wudu): The invalidation of the state of wudu, requiring a new wudu.
مس الذكر (mass al-dhakar): Touching the penis with the hand.
جمهور (jumhur): The majority of scholars; in this context, a large number of early authorities supporting the first opinion.

Key Takeaway

The Binding Nature of Khabar al-Wahid in Matters of General Necessity
Principle of acting upon solitary hadith in cases of general necessity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi (majority) position on khabar al-wahid in matters of umum al-balwa and identify the condition for its acceptance.

Core Idea
Khabar al-wahid is binding even in matters of general necessity if the conditions of acceptance are met.

This lesson explores a key principle in Hanafi usul al-fiqh: that a solitary hadith (khabar al-wahid) is accepted as evidence even when the matter is one of general occurrence (umum al-balwa). Some scholars argue that general necessity requires widespread knowledge, so a solitary report is insufficient. However, the majority of scholars, including the Hanafis, maintain that as long as the hadith meets the conditions of acceptance (shurut al-qabul) from the Prophet, it is binding. This passage, part of a discussion on differences in hadith texts, establishes the preponderant view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Issue
What is the dispute about? The use of khabar al-wahid in matters of umum al-balwa (general necessity).
General necessity refers to matters that affect the majority of people, making widespread knowledge expected.
2
State the Majority Position
Khabar al-wahid is acted upon in such matters if conditions of acceptance are met.
The passage explicitly states this is the preponderant view (al-rajih).
3
Understand the Proof
The general legal proofs requiring action upon khabar al-wahid do not differentiate between general necessity and other matters.
The author refers to 'adillah shar'iyyah' that indicate wujub al-`amal bi khabar al-wahid.
4
Note the Opposing View
Some scholars (e.g., some Shafi'is) argue that umum al-balwa requires a higher level of transmission.
This is the ikhtilaf that the author addresses.
5
Conclude with Conditions
Acceptance depends on fulfilling the conditions of authenticity and narrator reliability.
The passage mentions 'shurut al-qabul' regarding thubut from the Prophet.

Commentary
This passage is from a chapter on differences in the text (matn) of hadith. When Abu Musa narrated a hadith that 'Umar initially rejected, 'Umar sought verification due to the context. The author then states the preponderant view: khabar al-wahid (solitary report) is to be acted upon even in matters of general necessity (umum al-balwa), as long as it meets the conditions for acceptance (shurut al-qabul). This is because the general textual proofs requiring action upon khabar al-wahid do not differentiate between cases of general necessity and others. This ruling is based on the principle that the Shari'ah's evidence for accepting khabar al-wahid is general and unrestricted.

Key Terms
خبر الآحاد (khabar al-ahad): A hadith transmitted by one or a few narrators that does not reach the level of tawatur, yet is binding as evidence if it meets the conditions of acceptance.
عموم البلوى (umum al-balwa): Matters of general occurrence that affect the majority of people, making widespread knowledge expected.

Hanafi Objection to the Hadith of Busra: The Dawa'i Principle
Dispute over hadith of Busra: Hanafi critique based on dawa'i

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the Hanafi objection to the hadith of Busra and apply the principle of dawa'i to evaluate a khabar wahid.

Core Idea
A khabar wahid can be rejected if widespread transmission would have been expected due to common occurrence.

This lesson explores a classic usul dispute: the Hanafi rejection of the hadith of Busra regarding touching the penis nullifying wudu. Rather than simply accepting or rejecting the hadith based on its chain, the Hanafis raise a sophisticated argument about the incentives for transmission (dawa'i). Understanding this objection illuminates how Hanafi usul evaluates solitary narrations when the subject matter is frequent and public.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed ruling
First, recognize that the dispute is about whether touching the penis (mass al-dhakar) nullifies wudu. The Hanafi position is that it does not; the majority (including Shafi'is, Malikis, Hanbalis) hold that it does.
The thamarah al-khilaf: validity of prayer after touching without wudu.
2
State the opposing evidence
The main evidence for the nullification position is the hadith of Busra bint Safwan: 'Whoever touches his penis, let him perform wudu.' Identify this as a khabar wahid (a single-narrator hadith).
The hadith is ahad, not mutawatir.
3
Analyze the Hanafi objection
The Hanafis object on two grounds: first, questioning the hadith's authenticity (thubut), and second, arguing that the ruling should have been widely transmitted (dawa'i) because the act is common and the Prophet's modesty would not allow him to state it privately to one woman. Focus on the second: the dawa'i objection.
Al-Sarakhsi's argument about the Prophet's shyness and the presence of senior companions.
4
Understand the dawa'i principle
The dawa'i principle states that if a ruling concerns an action that occurs frequently and is publicly relevant, then if it were authentic, it would have been transmitted by many companions. A solitary narration in such a context is considered unreliable.
This is a Hanafi-specific usul tool, not used by Shafi'is.
5
Apply the principle to derive the Hanafi ruling
Since the hadith of Busra is the only strong evidence for nullification, and it fails the dawa'i test, the Hanafi school maintains the original ruling: touching the penis does not nullify wudu.
The prayer of one who touches and prays without wudu is valid according to Hanafis.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفصل الثاني / الاختلاف في المتن
- وَهُوَ يتكلم عن نواقض الوضوء : ومطلق مس ذكره المتصل».
قال أبو عمر بن عبد البر: واستقر قوله (وفي الاستذكار: والذي تقرر عَلَيْهِ المذهب عِنْدَ أهل المغرب من أصحابه أن لا إعادة عَلَى من صلى بَعْدَ أن مسه قاصداً وَلَمْ يتوضأ إلا في الوقت فإن خرج الوقت فَلا إعادة عَلَيْهِ»(۲).
رِوَايَة الإمام أحمد (۳) : إذا مس الرجل ذكره انتقض وضوؤه، ولا فرق بَيْنَ العامد والساهي، وفي رِوَايَة عَنْهُ اشتراط التعمد، ولا فرق بَيْنَ باطن الكف وظاهرها، وَلَيْسَ عَلَيْهِ نقض بمسه بذراعه، وَعَنْهُ في رِوَايَة عَلَيْهِ الوضوء، ولا فرق في كُلِّ هَذَا بَيْنَ ذكره وذكر غيره صغيراً أو كبيراً حياً أو ميتاً، وفي الذكر المقطوع رِوَايَتَانِ. وأما حلقة الدبر ففيها رِوَايَتَانِ، وفي شمول كُلّ هَذَا للمرأة رِوَايَتَانِ عَنْهُ: النقض وعدمه، والأشهر عَنْهُ أن يكون اللمس من غير حائل(4). الثاني: لَيْسَ عَلَى من مس ذكره وضوء، ووضوؤه صَحِيح، وبه قَالَ من الصحابة علي وابن مسعود وعمار بن ياسر وحذيفة وأبو الدرداء وعمران بن الحصين والنخعي وشريك والحسن بن حي وعبيد الله بن الحسن، وَهُوَ رِوَايَة عن سعد بن أبي وقاص وأبي هُرَيْرَةَ وسعيد بن جبير وسعيد بن المسيب والحسن البصري)
قال في الروض النضير: «وَهُوَ المحفوظ عن أئِمَّة أهل البيت (). وإليه ذهب الحنفية والزيدية والإمامية، وَهُوَ رِوَايَة عن الإمام أحمد)، و به جزم ابن المنذر ، واختاره العُتقي وسحنون من المالكية).
الأدلة
استدل من قَالَ بنقض الوضوء من مس الذكر بجملة أدلة، من بينها حَدِيث بسرة بنت صفوان أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قَالَ: «مَن مس ذكره فليتوضأ»). وَقَدْ رد الحنفية الاستدلال بهذا الْحَدِيث مِن وَجْهَيْنِ:
الأول: الطعن في الْحَدِيث من ناحية الثبوت).
الثاني: الاعتراض عَلَيْهِ من حَيْثُ إن بسرة تفردت بنقله، والفرض أن ينقله عدد كبير؛ لتوافر الدواعي على نقله (۱) ، قَالَ السرخسي: (ما بال رَسُول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم لَمْ يقل هَذَا بَيْنَ يدي كبار الصَّحَابَة، حَتَّى لَمْ ينقله أحد مِنْهُمْ، وإنما قَالَهُ بَيْنَ يدي بسرة؟ وَقَدْ كَانَ رَسُول الله أشد حياءً من العذراء في خدرها (۱۲) .
ويتفرع عن إيرادهم هَذَا الاعتراض بِمَا يأتي: ا ورد في بَعْض الروايات أن مروان بعث شرطياً إلى بسرة، فنقل الْحَدِيث عَنْهَا
Chapter Two / Disagreement in the Text
- It speaks about nullifiers of wudu: absolute touching of one's attached penis.
Abu Umar ibn Abd al-Barr said: His statement is settled (and in al-Istidhkar: and what the school settled upon according to the people of the Maghrib from his companions is that there is no repetition upon one who prayed after touching it intentionally and did not perform wudu except within the time; if the time exits, then no repetition upon him).
Narration of Imam Ahmad: If a man touches his penis, his wudu is nullified, and there is no difference between intentional and forgetful; and in a narration from him there is condition of intentionality, and no difference between the inside of the palm and its outside, and he is not required to repeat due to touching with his forearm, and in a narration from him, wudu is required, and in all of this there is no difference between his penis and another's, small or large, alive or dead, and regarding the severed penis there are two narrations. As for the anal ring, there are two narrations, and regarding the inclusion of all this for women there are two narrations from him: nullification and non-nullification, and the most famous from him is that the touch be without a barrier. The second: there is no wudu upon one who touches his penis, and his wudu is valid, and this is the view of the companions Ali, Ibn Mas'ud, Ammar ibn Yasir, Hudhayfa, Abu Darda, Imran ibn Husayn, al-Nakha'i, Sharik, al-Hasan ibn Hayy, Ubaydullah ibn al-Hasan, and it is a narration from Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas, Abu Hurayra, Sa'id ibn Jubayr, Sa'id ibn al-Musayyab, and al-Hasan al-Basri.
He said in al-Rawd al-Nadir: It is the preserved (view) from the Imams of Ahl al-Bayt, and the Hanafis, Zaydis, and Imamis went to it, and it is a narration from Imam Ahmad, and Ibn al-Mundhir asserted it, and al-Utqi and Sahnun from the Malikis chose it.
Evidence: Those who said that touching the penis nullifies wudu adduced a set of evidence, among them the hadith of Busra bint Safwan that the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Whoever touches his penis, let him perform wudu.' The Hanafis rejected the inference from this hadith in two ways: First: disparaging the hadith from the aspect of authenticity. Second: objecting to it from the angle that Busra alone narrated it, while the assumption is that a large number should have narrated it due to the abundant incentives for its transmission. Al-Sarakhsi said: 'Why did the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) not say this in the presence of senior companions, so that none of them narrated it, but only said it in the presence of Busra? And the Messenger of Allah was more shy than a virgin in her seclusion.' And branching from their raising of this objection comes what follows: in some narrations, Marwan sent a policeman to Busra, so she narrated the hadith from her.
Source pages p. 205

Commentary
This passage is a dispute (ikhtilaf) concerning the ruling on touching the penis and whether it nullifies wudu. The author presents the various positions of the schools, beginning with the Maliki view (no repetition required except within the time) and the Hanbali view with multiple narrations from Imam Ahmad, then the second position that no wudu is required, attributed to many companions and later scholars. The Hanafi position is clearly stated: no wudu required, and this is the view favored by the Hanafi, Zaydi, Imami schools, and also held by some Malikis and a narration from Ahmad. The evidence for the opposing view is the hadith of Busra. The Hanafi response is twofold: first, questioning the hadith's authenticity (thubut), and second, arguing that it was narrated by a single woman (Busra) whereas such a ruling should have been widely transmitted due to the frequent occurrence of the act; al-Sarakhsi emphasizes the Prophet's modesty as a reason for not publicizing the ruling. The text ends by noting that Marwan sent a policeman to Busra to confirm the hadith, implying that the ruling was not well-known among the companions. The commentary follows the author's sequence: positions, evidence, Hanafi critique.

Key Terms
مس الذكر (mass al-dhakar): Touching the male genital organ (penis) with the hand, with or without a barrier according to different views.
نقض الوضوء (naqd al-wudu): The invalidation of wudu by specific actions or events.
خبر الواحد (khabar al-wahid): A hadith narrated by one or a few transmitters, not reaching tawatur.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary Hanafi objection to using the hadith of Busra as evidence for wudu nullification by touching the penis?
A) The hadith contradicts a stronger Quranic verse.
B) Busra was not a trustworthy narrator.
C) The hadith was narrated by a single woman (khabar wahid) while the ruling should have been widely transmitted due to frequent occurrence.
D) The hadith only applies to women.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school does not consider touching the penis as nullifying wudu, primarily because the key hadith (Busra) is judged unreliable due to the dawa'i objection from Hanafi usul.
