Refuting Objections to the Hadith of Busrah: Chain and Contradiction Analysis
Textual analysis of objections and responses to the hadith of Busrah on wudu after touch.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate the Hanafi usul principle that a solitary hadith in a matter of general need raises doubt, and to explain the chain argument defending the hadith of Busrah.

Core Idea
A solitary hadith in a matter of general need is suspect in Hanafi usul — Busrah's hadith is defended by showing multiple connected chains.

This passage presents four objections raised against the hadith of Busrah (commanding wudu after touching the penis) and their rebuttals. The objections include chain weakness, contradiction with the hadith of Talq, the solitary nature in a matter of general need, and the gender of the narrator. The author then defends Busrah's hadith by tracing multiple connected chains from 'Urwah to Busrah, and also notes that many critics consider Talq's hadith more authentic. This analysis exposes the evidentiary debate between Hanafis and Shafi'is on this fiqh issue.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four objections
List the objections: chain via unknown policeman, contradiction with Talq's hadith, solitary hadith in a matter of general need, and ruling specific to men narrated by a woman.
The passage explicitly numbers them as first, second, third, fourth but only responds to the first and partly second in this excerpt.
2
Trace the chain variations from 'Urwah to Busrah
Map the three paths: (1) 'Urwah – Marwan – Busrah; (2) 'Urwah – policeman – Busrah; (3) 'Urwah directly from Busrah. Understand Ibn Hibban's explanation that Marwan and the policeman are 'removed' from the chain.
This shows the hadith is not munqati' (disconnected) as claimed.
3
Understand the usul principle 'ta'mm bihi al-balwa'
Define the principle: a hadith about a common occurrence that is only transmitted as ahad creates doubt because it should have been widely known. Hanafis use this to reject ahad hadith in such matters.
This is a key Hanafi usul tool, not rejection without reason.
4
Compare the strengths of Busrah's and Talq's hadith
Note that critics like al-Fallas and Ibn al-Madini consider Talq's hadith more firmly established (athbat) than Busrah's. However, the passage also defends Busrah's hadith as authentic through multiple chains.
This contradiction is resolved by preferring one over the other based on strength and usul principles.
5
Synthesize the Hanafi reliance on Talq's hadith and istihsan
The Hanafi school follows the hadith of Talq and istihsan (juristic preference) to rule that touching the penis does not invalidate wudu. This lesson shows that the Hadith of Busrah is not unanimously weak, but the Hanafis have valid grounds to prefer Talq's hadith.
The passage does not issue a fatwa but exposes the basis for disagreement.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفصل الثاني الاختلاف في المتن
وسمعه منه عروة، وهذا الشرطي مجهول. فتبين أن سَمَاع عروة عن طريق مجهول، فَلاً تقوم الحجة بإخباره.
٠٢ أن هَذَا الْحَدِيْث يعارض حَدِيث طلق بن عَلِيّ الحنفي في تَرْك الوضوء من مسه، وَقَدْ قَالَ التِّرْمِذِيّ في حَدِيث طلق «هَذَا الْحَدِيث أحسن شيء روي في الباب».
إِن هَذَا الْحَدِيث حَدِيث آحاد، وَقَد ورد فيما تعم به البلوى، وهذه ريبة توجب التوقف في قبوله.
أنَّهُ تضمن حكماً يختص بالرجال، وَقَدْ روته امرأة.
ونجيب عن هَذِهِ الاعتراضات بِمَا يأتي:
أما الأول: فإنه قد ورد في بَعْض طرق الْحَدِيث التصريح بأن عروة سمعه مباشرة من غَيْر واسطة من بسرة. فأخرج أحمد، وابن الجارود، وابن حبان، والدارقطني، والحاكم، والبيهقي في السنن وفي مَعْرِفَة السنن والآثار، هَذَا الْحَدِيث وفيه التصريح بسماع عروة من بسرة.
ولنسق رِوَايَة ابن الجارود ليتضح هَذَا، فروى بإسناده عن هشام بن عروة، عن أبيه، عن مروان بن الحكم عن بسرة، أن النبي الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قَالَ: «من مس ذكره فليتوضأ». قَالَ عروة: سألت بسرة فصدقته.
ومن خلال التتبع للطرق الَّتِي روي بِهَا الْحَدِيث، نقف على ثلاث طرق للحديث من طريق عروة، هي:
١ عروة، عن مروان عن بسرة.
٢. تذاكر عروة ومروان نواقض الوضوء، فأرسل مروان شرطياً إلى بسرة، فذكرت الْحَدِيث. فتكون حقيقة الرّوَايَة: عروة، عن الشرطي، عن بسرة.
٣. عروة، عن بسرة مباشرة.
وَقَدْ أجاد الحَافِظ ابن حبان في تفسير هَذَا التنوع قائلاً:
(وأما خبر بسرة الَّذِي ذكرناه، فإن عروة بن الزبير سمعه من مروان بن الحكم عن بسرة، فَلَمْ يقنعه ذَلِكَ حَتَّى بعث مروان شرطياً لَهُ إلى بسرة فسألها، ثُمَّ أتاهم فأخبرهم بمثل ما قالت بسرة، فسمعه عروة ثانياً عن الشرطي عن بسرة، ثُمَّ لَمْ يقنعه ذَلِكَ حَتَّى ذهب إِلَى بسرة فسمع منها. فالخبر عن عروة عن بسرة متصل لَيْسَ بمنقطع، وصار مروان والشرطي كأنهما عاريتان يسقطان من الإسناد). وَقَالَ الحَافِظ ابن حجر: جزم ابن خزيمة وغير واحد من الأئمة بأن عروة سمعه من بسرة.
وأسهب أبو عَبْد الله الحَاكِم في التدليل عَلَى هَذَا، بعرض نفيس.
عَلَى أن الْحَدِيْث مروي عَنْهَا من غَيْر طريق عروة.
وأما اعتراضهم الثاني: الحفاظ النقاد فحديث طلق بن عَلِيّ الحنفي حَدِيث صَحِيح، صححه جمع من مِنْهُمْ: عَمْرو بن عَلِيّ الفلاس، وعلي بن المديني، والطحاوي، وابن حبان، والطبراني، وابن حزم وَقَالَ الفلاس: «هُوَ عندنا أثبت من حَدِيث بسرة». وَقَالَ ابن المديني: «هُوَ عندنا أحسن من حَدِيث بسرة».
Chapter Two: Disagreement in the Matn. And 'Urwah heard it from him, and this policeman is unknown. So it becomes clear that 'Urwah's hearing is by way of an unknown person, so proof is not established by his report. Second: This hadith contradicts the hadith of Talq ibn 'Ali al-Hanafi about not performing wudu' from touching it, and al-Tirmidhi said about the hadith of Talq: 'This hadith is the best thing narrated in the chapter.' Third: This hadith is a solitary hadith, and it has come in a matter of general need, and this is a doubt that necessitates pausing in accepting it. Fourth: It includes a ruling specific to men, and a woman narrated it. We respond to these objections as follows: As for the first: It has come in some chains of the hadith the explicit statement that 'Urwah heard it directly without intermediary from Busrah. Ahmad, Ibn al-Jarud, Ibn Hibban, al-Daraqutni, al-Hakim, and al-Bayhaqi in al-Sunan and in Ma'rifat al-Sunan wa al-Athar narrated this hadith and in it is the explicit statement of 'Urwah's hearing from Busrah. And let us present the narration of Ibn al-Jarud to clarify this: he narrated by his chain from Hisham ibn 'Urwah, from his father, from Marwan ibn al-Hakam, from Busrah, that the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Whoever touches his penis, let him perform wudu'. 'Urwah said: I asked Busrah and she confirmed it. Through tracing the paths by which the hadith was narrated, we come across three paths from 'Urwah: 1) 'Urwah, from Marwan, from Busrah. 2) 'Urwah and Marwan discussed the nullifiers of wudu, so Marwan sent a policeman to Busrah, and she mentioned the hadith. So the reality of the narration is: 'Urwah, from the policeman, from Busrah. 3) 'Urwah, from Busrah directly. And al-Hafiz Ibn Hibban excelled in explaining this variety, saying: 'As for the report of Busrah that we mentioned, 'Urwah ibn al-Zubayr heard it from Marwan ibn al-Hakam from Busrah, but he was not satisfied with that until Marwan sent a policeman of his to Busrah and asked her, then he came to them and informed them the like of what Busrah said, so 'Urwah heard it a second time from the policeman from Busrah. Then he was not satisfied with that until he went to Busrah and heard from her. So the report from 'Urwah from Busrah is connected, not disconnected, and Marwan and the policeman become as if they are removed from the chain.' And al-Hafiz Ibn Hajar said: 'Ibn Khuzaymah and more than one of the imams affirmed that 'Urwah heard it from Busrah.' And Abu 'Abd Allah al-Hakim elaborated on this with a valuable presentation. Moreover, the hadith is narrated from her through other than the path of 'Urwah. As for their second objection: The critical memorizers consider the hadith of Talq ibn 'Ali al-Hanafi to be authentic; a group of them authenticated it: 'Amr ibn 'Ali al-Fallas, 'Ali ibn al-Madini, al-Tahawi, Ibn Hibban, al-Tabarani, and Ibn Hazm. Al-Fallas said: 'It is, in our view, more firmly established than the hadith of Busrah.' And Ibn al-Madini said: 'It is, in our view, better than the hadith of Busrah.'
Source pages p. 207

Commentary
This passage is a textual analysis fiqh dispute. The author presents four objections raised against the hadith of Busrah (that touching the penis requires wudu) and then responds to them. The first objection concerns the chain: 'Urwah is said to have heard it through an unknown policeman. The author refutes this by showing multiple chains: 'Urwah heard it directly from Busrah in one path, and through Marwan and the policeman in others. Ibn Hibban's explanation confirms the chain is connected. The second objection is contradiction with the hadith of Talq, which commands not doing wudu after touch. The author notes that many hadith critics consider Talq's hadith more authentic. The third objection (solitary hadith in a matter of general need) and fourth (ruling specific to men narrated by a woman) are mentioned but not answered in this excerpt. The Hanafi school, following Abu Hanifa, relies on the hadith of Talq and other evidences to rule that touching the penis does not invalidate wudu. This passage, while defending Busrah's hadith, also acknowledges the strength of Talq's hadith in the eyes of many scholars. The analysis here is from a modern academic work on the effect of hadith differences on fiqh; it does not issue a fatwa but exposes the evidentiary basis for disagreement.

Key Terms
حديث آحاد (Hadith Ahad): A solitary hadith that does not reach the level of tawatur.
تعم به البلوى (Ta'mm bihi al-balwa): A matter that is commonly encountered by the general public, necessitating widespread knowledge.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the Hanafi justification for not requiring wudu after touching the penis, despite the hadith of Busrah?
A) The hadith of Busrah is fabricated.
B) The hadith of Talq is considered more authentic by many critics, and istihsan supports it.
C) The hadith of Busrah is abrogated.
D) The Hanafis reject all ahad hadith.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi preference for Talq's hadith over Busrah's is based on a combination of hadith criticism, the usul principle of ta'mm bihi al-balwa, and istihsan.

Resolving Conflicting Hadiths: The Case of Bursa and Talq
Analyzing the chains of conflicting hadiths on wudu'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to analyze conflicting hadith chains and apply the Hanafi usul principle of tarjih based on chain strength and critic consensus to determine the preferred hadith.

Core Idea
Chain strength and critic consensus can override a single connected chain when determining fiqh rulings.

This lesson examines how Hanafi usul handles conflicting hadiths that appear equally authentic. Through the case of wudu' breaking by touching private parts, we see how chain criticism and the opinions of hadith critics lead to a preferred ruling. You will learn to assess the strength of different chains and understand the tarjih mechanism used by Hanafi scholars.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Conflicting Hadiths
Locate the two hadiths: the hadith of Bursa (touching breaks wudu') and the hadith of Talq (touching does not break wudu'). Note the different rulings they support.
2
Analyze the Chain of Bursa
Examine the chain: 'Urwa heard it from Marwan and a policeman before hearing it directly from Bursa. Ibn Hibban argues it is still connected, but intermediaries exist.
This connects to the objection that the chain might be disconnected.
3
Analyze the Chain of Talq
Trace the chain: Mulazim ibn 'Amr from 'Abd Allah ibn Badr from Qays ibn Talq from his father Talq (marfu'). Evaluate each narrator's trustworthiness based on critic statements.
Critics like al-Fallas and Ibn al-Madini declared this hadith 'athbat' (more firmly established) than Bursa's.
4
Apply Tarjih (Preference)
Hanafi scholars prefer the Talq hadith because it is considered stronger by numerous hadith critics, despite Bursa's chain being connected.
The thamarah al-khilaf: Hanafi says wudu' not broken; Shafi'i says it is.
5
Derive the Hanafi Ruling
Based on the preferred dalil, state that touching private parts does not nullify wudu' according to the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفصل الثاني / الاختلاف في المتن
تذاكر عروة ومروان نواقض الوضوء، فأرسل مروان شرطياً إلى بسرة، فذكرت الحديث. فتكون حقيقة الرواية: عروة، عن الشرطي، عن بسرة. عروة، عن بسرة مباشرة.
وقد أجاد الحافظ ابن حبان في تفسير هذا التنوع قائلاً: (وأما خبر بسرة الذي ذكرناه، فإن عروة بن الزبير سمعه من مروان بن الحكم عن بسرة، فلم يقنعه ذلك حتى بعث مروان شرطياً له إلى بسرة فسألها، ثم أتاهم فأخبرهم بمثل ما قالت بسرة، فسمعه عروة ثانياً عن الشرطي عن بسرة، ثم لم يقنعه ذلك حتى ذهب إلى بسرة فسمع منها. فالخبر عن عروة عن بسرة متصل ليس بمنقطع، وصار مروان والشرطي كأنهما عاريتان يسقطان من الإسناد). وقال الحافظ ابن حجر: جزم ابن خزيمة وغير واحد من الأئمة بأن عروة سمعه من بسرة.
وأسهب أبو عبد الله الحاكم في التدليل على هذا، بعرض نفيس.
على أن الحديث مروي عنها من غير طريق عروة.
وأما اعتراضهم الثاني: الحفاظ النقاد فحديث طلق بن علي الحنفي حديث صحيح، صححه جمع منهم: عمرو بن علي الفلاس، وعلي بن المديني، والطحاوي، وابن حبان، والطبراني، وابن حزم. وقال الفلاس: «هو عندنا أثبت من حديث بسرة». وقال ابن المديني: «هو عندنا أحسن من حديث بسرة».

بيان طرق هذا الحديث فيما يأتي:
فقد رواه عن طلق ابنه قيس، وقيس هذا تكلم فيه بغير حجة، ووثقه أحمد وابن معين والعجلي وذكره ابن حبان في ثقاته.
وقد روي بأربع طرق: رواه ابن أبي شيبة، وأبو داود، والترمذي، والنسائي، والدارقطني، وابن الجارود، والطحاوي، والبيهقي، من طريق ملازم بن عمرو، عن عبد الله بدر، عن قيس بن طلق بن علي، عن أبيه، مرفوعاً.
وعبد الله بن بدر: هو ابن عميرة الحنفي السحيمي اليمامي، جد ملازم بن عمر لأبيه، وقيل: لأمه. وثقه ابن معين وأبو زرعة والعجلي، وذكره ابن حبان في الثقات، وقال ابن حجر: «كان أحد الأشراف: ثقة».
وملازم بن عمرو: هو ابن عبد الله بن بدر الحنفي السحيمي اليمامي، وثقه أحمد وابن معين وأبو زرعة والنسائي، وذكره ابن حبان في ثقاته، وقال أبو حاتم: لا بأس به صدوق، وقال الحافظ ابن حجر: «صدوق».
وانطلاقاً من هذا الطريق القوي صححه من صححه من الأئمة، وإليه يشير كلام الإمام الترمذي، إذ يقول بعد أن رواه من هذا الطريق: (وقد روى هذا الحديث أيوب ابن عتبة، ومحمد بن جابر، عن قيس بن طلق عن أبيه. وقد تكلم بعض أهل الحديث في محمد بن جابر وأيوب بن عتبة، وحديث ملازم بن عمرو، عن عبد الله بن
Chapter Two / Difference in the Text. 'Urwa and Marwan discussed the nullifiers of wudu', so Marwan sent a policeman to Bursa, and she mentioned the hadith. So the reality of the narration is: 'Urwa, from the policeman, from Bursa; and 'Urwa, from Bursa directly. And al-Hafiz Ibn Hibban excelled in explaining this variety, saying: 'Regarding the report of Bursa which we mentioned, 'Urwa ibn al-Zubayr heard it from Marwan ibn al-Hakam from Bursa, but that did not satisfy him until Marwan sent a policeman of his to Bursa and asked her, then he came to them and informed them of what Bursa had said, so 'Urwa heard it a second time from the policeman from Bursa, then that did not satisfy him until he went to Bursa and heard it directly from her. So the report from 'Urwa from Bursa is connected, not disconnected, and Marwan and the policeman became like two 'gifts' that drop from the chain.' And al-Hafiz Ibn Hajar said: 'Ibn Khuzaymah and more than one of the imams were certain that 'Urwa heard it from Bursa.' And Abu 'Abd Allah al-Hakim elaborated on proving this with a valuable presentation. Further, the hadith is narrated from her through other than the route of 'Urwa. As for their second objection: the critical hadith preservers, the hadith of Talq ibn 'Ali al-Hanafi is a sound hadith, authenticated by a group including: 'Amr ibn 'Ali al-Fallas, 'Ali ibn al-Madini, al-Tahawi, Ibn Hibban, al-Tabarani, and Ibn Hazm. Al-Fallas said: 'It is more firmly established with us than the hadith of Bursa.' Ibn al-Madini said: 'It is better with us than the hadith of Bursa.' Explanation of the chains of this hadith follows: His son Qays narrated it from Talq, and this Qays was criticized without proof, but Ahmad, Ibn Ma'in, and al-'Ijli declared him trustworthy, and Ibn Hibban mentioned him among the trustworthy. It has been narrated through four routes: narrated by Ibn Abi Shaybah, Abu Dawud, al-Tirmidhi, al-Nasa'i, al-Daraqutni, Ibn al-Jarud, al-Tahawi, and al-Bayhaqi, through the route of Mulazim ibn 'Amr, from 'Abd Allah Badr, from Qays ibn Talq ibn 'Ali, from his father, raised (to the Prophet). 'Abd Allah ibn Badr: he is Ibn 'Umayra al-Hanafi al-Suhaymi al-Yamami, the grandfather of Mulazim ibn 'Umar from his father's side, and it is said: from his mother's side. Ibn Ma'in, Abu Zur'ah, and al-'Ijli declared him trustworthy, and Ibn Hibban mentioned him among the trustworthy, and Ibn Hajar said: 'He was one of the nobles: trustworthy.' Mulazim ibn 'Amr: he is Ibn 'Abd Allah ibn Badr al-Hanafi al-Suhaymi al-Yamami. Ahmad, Ibn Ma'in, Abu Zur'ah, and al-Nasa'i declared him trustworthy, and Ibn Hibban mentioned him among his trustworthy narrators, and Abu Hatim said: 'No problem with him, truthful (saduq),' and al-Hafiz Ibn Hajar said: 'Saduq.' Based on this strong route, those of the imams who authenticated it did so, and it is to this that the statement of Imam al-Tirmidhi refers, as he says after narrating it through this route: 'Ayyub ibn 'Utbah and Muhammad ibn Jabir narrated this hadith from Qays ibn Talq from his father. Some scholars of hadith spoke about Muhammad ibn Jabir and Ayyub ibn 'Utbah, and the hadith of Mulazim ibn 'Amr, from 'Abd Allah ibn...'
Source pages p. 208

Commentary
This passage is a textual analysis of two conflicting hadiths concerning the nullification of wudu' by touching the private parts. The author examines the chains of the hadith of Bursa (which indicates that touching breaks wudu') and the hadith of Talq (which indicates it does not). The discussion begins by addressing an objection regarding the chain of Bursa: that 'Urwa heard it through intermediaries. Ibn Hibban clarifies that 'Urwa actually heard it directly from Bursa after first hearing it through Marwan and a policeman, so the chain is connected. Thus the claim of disconnection is refuted. Then the author moves to the second objection: the hadith of Talq is weak. The author lists many hadith critics who authenticated Talq's hadith, including 'Amr ibn 'Ali al-Fallas and 'Ali ibn al-Madini, who explicitly stated it is stronger than Bursa's hadith. The author then details the chain of Talq's hadith, which goes: Mulazim ibn 'Amr from 'Abd Allah ibn Badr from Qays ibn Talq from his father Talq (marfu'). Each narrator is evaluated as trustworthy or acceptable, establishing the chain as 'strong' (qawi). The passage ends with al-Tirmidhi's remark that other weaker chains exist, but the strong chain is through Mulazim. The overall aim is to demonstrate the strength of the Talq hadith, supporting the Hanafi position that touching the private parts does not break wudu', as opposed to others who follow the Bursa hadith.

Key Terms
المتن (al-matn): The text of a hadith, distinct from its chain (isnad).
الإسناد (al-isnad): The chain of narrators transmitting the hadith.
أثبت (athbat): More firmly established; a term used by critics to indicate a hadith is stronger than another.
ثقات (thiqat): Trustworthy narrators (plural of thiqa).
صحيح (sahih): Sound; a hadith with a continuous chain of trustworthy narrators and no hidden defects.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How many ways did 'Urwa hear the hadith of Bursa according to Ibn Hibban?
A) One way directly from Bursa
B) Two ways: from Marwan and from the policeman
C) Three ways: from Marwan, from the policeman, and directly from Bursa
D) Four ways: from Marwan, from the policeman, from Bursa, and from another companion

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school resolves conflicting hadith by analyzing chain strength and preferring the hadith deemed 'athbat' (more firmly established) by major critics.

Evaluating Hadith Chains: The Case of Talq ibn Ali
Textual analysis of hadith chains evaluating narrator reliability.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi methodology of evaluating multiple hadith chains to determine the most authentic narration for legal deduction.

Core Idea
A hadith's authenticity depends on its chain; the strongest chain determines the operative ruling in Hanafi fiqh.

This lesson explores the classical Hanafi approach to weighing conflicting hadith chains. Using the hadith of Talq ibn Ali, we see how scholars like al-Tirmidhi prioritized one chain over others based on narrator reliability. You'll learn to identify key narrator criticism terms and understand how Hanafi usul accepts weaker chains when corroborated.

Guided Path
1
Identify the main chains in the text
Locate the four chains mentioned: via Mulazim ibn 'Amr, via Ayyub ibn 'Utbah, via Muhammad ibn Jabir, and the unnamed chain via Qays alone.
Focus on the first chain as the strongest.
2
Recognize narrator criticism terminology
Identify terms like 'thiqah', 'saduq', 'da'if', and 'layyin' used for narrators such as 'Abdullah ibn Badr, Mulazim, and Ayyub.
Note that 'da'if' due to memory still allows elevation.
3
Apply the Hanafi principle of elevation
Understand that a hadith with a memory-weak narrator can be elevated if supported by corroborating chains (mutaba'at/shawahid).
This is a key Hanafi usul principle not shared by all schools.
4
Determine the strongest chain per al-Tirmidhi
Identify why the Mulazim chain is considered 'asahh wa ahsan' — because both 'Abdullah ibn Badr and Mulazim are thiqah or saduq.
This chain is preferred despite other chains having weaker narrators.
5
Connect the chain analysis to fiqh ruling
Reflect that the derived ruling (e.g., wiping the head once in wudu) is based on the strongest chain, and Hanafis accept this ruling while others may not.
The thamarah al-khilaf is acceptance vs rejection of the ruling.

الفصل الثاني / الاختلاف في المتن وبيان طرق هَذَا الْحَدِيث فِيْمَا يأتي: فَقَدْ رَوَاهُ عن طلق ابنه قيس، وقيس هَذَا تكلم فيه بغير حجة، ووثقه أحمد وابن مَعِينٍ والعجلي وذكره ابن حبان في ثقاته. وَقَدْ روي بأربع طرق: رَوَاهُ ابن أبي شيبة، وأبو داود، والترمذي، والنسائي، والدارقطني، وابن الجارود، والطحاوي، والبيهقي، من طريق ملازم بن عَمْرو، عن عَبْد الله بدر، عن قيس بن طلق بن علي، عن أبيه، مرفوعاً. وعبد الله بن بدر: هُوَ ابن عميرة الحنفي السحيمي اليمامي، جد ملازم بن عمر لأبيه، وَقِيلَ: لأمه. وثقه ابن مَعِينٍ وأبو زرعة والعجلي، وذكره ابن حبان في الثقات، وَقَالَ ابن حجر: «كَانَ أحد الأشراف: ثقة». وملازم بن عَمْرو: هُوَ ابن عَبْد الله بن بدر الحنفي السحيمي اليمامي، وثقه أحمد وابن مَعِيْن وأبو زرعة والنسائي، وذكره ابن حبان في ثقاته، وَقَالَ أبو حاتم: لا بأس به صدوق، وَقَالَ الحافظ ابن حجر: «صدوق». وانطلاقاً من هَذَا الطريق القوي صححه من صححه من الأئمة، وإليه يشير كلام الإمام التِّرْمِذِيّ، إذ يَقُوْل بَعْدَ أن رَوَاهُ من هَذَا الطريق: (وَقَدْ رَوَى هَذَا الْحَدِيث أَيوب ابن عتبة، ومحمد بن جابر، عن قيس بن طلق عن أبيه. وَقَدْ تكلم بَعْض أهل الْحَدِيث في محمد بن جابر وأيوب بن عتبة، وحديث ملازم بن عَمْرو، عن عَبْد الله بن بدر أصح وأحسن). رَوَاهُ الطيالسي، وأحمد، والطحاوي، والبيهقي، من طرق عن أيوب بن عتبة، عن قيس بن طلق عَنْهُ. وأيوب قَالَ أحمد: ضعيف وفي رِوَايَة ثقة، إلا أنَّهُ لا يقيم حَدِيث يَحْيَى بن أبي كَثِيْر وَقَالَ ابن مَعِيْنِ: لَيْسَ بالقوي، ومرة: لَيْسَ بشيء، ومرة: ضعيف، ومرة: لَيْسَ حديثه بشيء، ومرة: لا بأس بهِ، وَقَالَ الفلاس: ضعيف وَكَانَ سيئ الحفظ، وَهُوَ من أهل الصدق. وَقَالَ ابن المديني والجوزجاني وابن عمار ومسلم: ضعيف. وَقَالَ العجلي: يكتب حديثه وَلَيْسَ بالقوي. وَقَالَ البُخَارِيّ: هُوَ عندهم لين. ومن تأمل أقوال هَؤُلاَءِ الأئمة يجد أنهم تكلموا فيه من جهة الحفظ لا من جهة العدالة، وَعَلَيْهِ فحديثه قابل للارتقاء فِيْمَا إذا اعتضد بالمتابعات والشواهد، وَهُوَ متابع في روايته عن قيس كَمَا يعلم من تفصيل هَذِهِ الطرق. رَوَاهُ عَبْد الرزاق، وأحمد، وابن ماجه، والدارقطني، والحازمي، وابن الجارود، والطبراني في الكبير، من طرق عن مُحَمَّد بن جابر.
Chapter Two / Difference in the Text and Explanation of the Chains of This Hadith as follows: It was narrated from Talq by his son Qays, and Qays was spoken about without evidence, and Ahmad, Ibn Ma'een, and al-'Ijli declared him trustworthy, and Ibn Hibban mentioned him among his reliable narrators. And it has been narrated through four chains: Ibn Abi Shaybah, Abu Dawud, al-Tirmidhi, al-Nasa'i, al-Daraqutni, Ibn al-Jarud, al-Tahawi, and al-Bayhaqi narrated it via the chain of Mulazim ibn 'Amr, from 'Abdullah ibn Badr, from Qays ibn Talq ibn Ali, from his father, raised (marfu'). 'Abdullah ibn Badr: he is Ibn 'Umairah al-Hanafi al-Suhaimi al-Yamami, the maternal grandfather of Mulazim ibn 'Amr, and it is said paternal. Ibn Ma'een, Abu Zur'ah, and al-'Ijli declared him trustworthy, and Ibn Hibban mentioned him among the reliable, and Ibn Hajar said: 'He was one of the nobles, trustworthy.' Mulazim ibn 'Amr: he is the son of 'Abdullah ibn Badr al-Hanafi al-Suhaimi al-Yamami; Ahmad, Ibn Ma'een, Abu Zur'ah, and al-Nasa'i declared him trustworthy, and Ibn Hibban mentioned him among his reliable narrators, and Abu Hatim said: 'There is no problem with him, truthful (saduq),' and al-Hafiz Ibn Hajar said: 'Truthful.' Based on this strong chain, those who authenticated it did so, and the words of Imam al-Tirmidhi point to this, for he said after narrating it from this chain: 'And this hadith was narrated by Ayyub ibn 'Utbah and Muhammad ibn Jabir, from Qays ibn Talq from his father. Some scholars of hadith spoke about Muhammad ibn Jabir and Ayyub ibn 'Utbah, and the hadith of Mulazim ibn 'Amr, from 'Abdullah ibn Badr is more authentic and better.' Al-Tayalisi, Ahmad, al-Tahawi, and al-Bayhaqi narrated it via chains from Ayyub ibn 'Utbah, from Qays ibn Talq from him. Regarding Ayyub: Ahmad said: weak, and in one narration: trustworthy, except that he does not uphold the hadith of Yahya ibn Abi Kathir. Ibn Ma'een said: not strong, and once: not good, and once: weak, and once: his hadith is nothing, and once: no problem with him. Al-Fallas said: weak, and he had a bad memory, and he is from the people of truthfulness. Ibn al-Madini, al-Juzjani, Ibn 'Ammar, and Muslim said: weak. Al-'Ijli said: his hadith is written but not strong. Al-Bukhari said: he is, according to them, lenient (layyin). And whoever contemplates the statements of these imams will find that they spoke about him with regard to memory, not integrity. Therefore, his hadith can be elevated if supported by follow-ups and witnesses, and he is followed in his narration from Qays as is known from the details of these chains. 'Abd al-Razzaq, Ahmad, Ibn Majah, al-Daraqutni, al-Hazimi, Ibn al-Jarud, and al-Tabarani in al-Kabir narrated it via chains from Muhammad ibn Jabir.
Source pages p. 209

Commentary
This passage is a textual analysis of the various chains of a hadith transmitted by Talq ibn Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) through his son Qays. The author first notes that Qays ibn Talq has been criticized without evidence, but he is declared trustworthy by major critics. The hadith has four main chains. The first and strongest chain is via Mulazim ibn 'Amr, from 'Abdullah ibn Badr, from Qays, from his father. Both 'Abdullah ibn Badr and Mulazim ibn 'Amr are authenticated by multiple hadith masters. Because of this chain's strength, Imam al-Tirmidhi and other scholars authenticated this hadith, preferring it over the other chains that involve Ayyub ibn 'Utbah and Muhammad ibn Jabir, who are weaker. The text then details the criticisms of Ayyub ibn 'Utbah, showing that most imams considered him weak due to poor memory, not dishonesty. This means his hadith can be strengthened by corroboration. The third chain via Muhammad ibn Jabir is also weak. In Hanafi methodology, hadiths with weak chains can be elevated if they have supporting evidence. The author implies that the preferred ruling derived from this hadith—whatever it is about—is based on the strongest chain through Mulazim ibn 'Amr. This analysis is typical of Hanafi usul, where the authenticity of a hadith is determined by scrutinizing individual narrators and chains, and the most reliable chain is adopted for legal deduction.

Key Terms
ثقة (thiqah): A narrator who is reliable and trustworthy in transmission.
ضعيف (da'if): A weak narrator due to poor memory or other defects, but not necessarily blameworthy in religion.
صدوق (saduq): A narrator who is truthful but may have slight memory issues; acceptable.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) The chain via Muhammad ibn Jabir
C) The chain via Mulazim ibn 'Amr from 'Abdullah ibn Badr
D) The chain via Qays ibn Talq alone

Key Takeaway
The strength of a hadith in Hanafi usul is determined by its most reliable chain; weak narrators with memory issues can be compensated by corroborating evidence.

Elevating a Weak Hadith: Multiple Chains as Proof
Textual analysis of hadith chains on wudu after touching penis

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate the acceptability of a hadith with multiple weak chains by applying Hanafi principles of mutaba'at and shawahid.

Core Idea
A hadith with weak narrators can become a legal proof if supported by multiple chains (mutaba'at and shawahid).

This passage illustrates a core Hanafi usul principle: cumulative strength through multiple transmissions. Even if individual narrators are criticized for weak memory, their combined reports can reach the level of hujjah. We will trace the chains of the hadith on touching the penis and see how the author constructs his argument.

Guided Path
1
Identify the primary narrator and its critique
First, identify the main narrator in the first chain: Ayyub bin 'Utbah. Note the criticisms from various hadith masters: they speak about his memory, not his truthfulness.
This distinction is crucial: memory issues can be compensated, lying cannot.
2
Determine the type of weakness
Check if the weakness is in memory (hifz) or in justice (adalah). The passage shows all critiques are about memory, not lying. Thus the narrator is weak but not discarded entirely.
Hanafi usul accepts such narrators when corroborated.
3
List the supporting chains (mutaba'at)
Identify the other chains: (1) via Muhammad bin Jabir (weak, but supported), (2) via 'Abd al-Hamid bin Ja'far and Ayyub bin Muhammad (both weak). These are mutaba'at that follow the same line of transmission from Qays bin Talq.
The author also mentions shawahid (witnesses) but focuses on mutaba'at.
4
Evaluate the combined strength
Combine the chains. The author argues that although each chain has weaknesses, together they elevate the hadith to the level of hujjah. The first chain even by itself is considered a standing proof.
Hanafi method: multiple weak chains can strengthen each other when weaknesses are in memory.
5
Refute counter-arguments
Examine the criticism of Abu Hatim and Abu Zur'a. The author shows that their weakening was specifically about the chain via Muhammad bin Jabir, not all chains. Their criticism of Qays bin Talq is isolated and not supported by other critics.
This demonstrates careful textual analysis: one must limit the scope of a critic's statement.

وأيوب قَالَ :أحمد ضعيف وفي رِوَايَة ثقة، إلا أنَّهُ لا يقيم حَدِيث يَحْيَى بن أبي كَثِيْر وَقَالَ ابن مَعِيْنِ: لَيْسَ بالقوي، ومرة: لَيْسَ بشيء، ومرة: ضعيف، ومرة: لَيْسَ حديثه بشيء، ومرة: لا بأس بهِ، وَقَالَ الفلاس: ضعيف وَكَانَ سيئ الحفظ، وَهُوَ من أهل الصدق. وَقَالَ ابن المديني والجوزجاني وابن عمار ومسلم: ضعيف. وَقَالَ العجلي: يكتب حديثه وَلَيْسَ بالقوي. وَقَالَ البُخَارِيّ: هُوَ عندهم لين

ومحمد بن جابر: هُوَ ابن سيار السحيمي الحنفي الضرير، ضعيف، ضعفه غَيْر واحد من الأئمة.
ه رَوَاهُ ابن عدي من طريق عبد الحميد بن جعفر، عن أيوب بن مُحَمَّد العجلي، عن قيس بن طلق، عن أبيه، به.
وعبد الحميد بن جعفر، وأيوب بن مُحَمَّد، كلاهما متكلم فيه. وإذا ضممنا هَذِهِ الطرق إلى بعضها، ارتقى الْحَدِيث إِلَى حيّز الاحتجاج، عَلَى أن الطريق الأولى عِنْدَ انفرادها حجة قائمة.
وأمـا مـا نـقـل عـن الحافظين أبي حاتم وأبي زرعة الرازيين من تضعيفهم لهذا الْحَدِيث، فالمتأمل لصيغة السؤال، يجد أنهما لَمْ يعمما الحكم، فَقَدْ قَالَ ابن أبي حاتم: سألت أبي وأبا زرعة عن حَدِيث رَوَاهُ مُحَمَّد بن جابر، عن قيس بن طلق، عن أبيه، أنَّه سأل رَسُوْلَ الله صلى الله عليه وسلم هَلْ في مس الذكر وضوء، قَالَ: لا. فَلَمْ يثبتاه، وقالا: قيس بن طلق لَيْسَ مِمَّنْ تقوم به الحجة ووهماه.
فالسؤال مقيد بطريق مُحَمَّد بن جابر، وَهُوَ ضعيف اتفاقاً، ولا جدال في كونه ضعيفاً فيما إذا تفرد، فكيف بثلاث طرق أخرى إحداها حجة لو انفردت!! وأما غمزهما لقيس بن طلق، فَلَمْ يوافقهما عَلَيْهِ أحد من النقاد، وَقَد تقدم الكلام عَنْهُ عَلَى أَن الحَافِظ عَبْد الحق الإشبيلي أورد هَذَا الْحَدِيث في أحكامه الوسطى ساكتاً عَنْهُ وَهُوَ يقتضي صحته عنده. فتعقبه الحافظ ابن القطان قائلاً: «والحديث
Chapter Two / Disagreement in the Text. 'Badr is more authentic and more beautiful.' It was narrated by al-Tayalisi, Ahmad, al-Tahawi, and al-Bayhaqi through chains from Ayyub bin 'Utbah, from Qays bin Talq from him. And Ayyub: Ahmad said weak, and in a narration trustworthy, except that he does not establish the hadith of Yahya bin Abi Kathir. Ibn Ma'in said: not strong, once: not anything, once: weak, once: his hadith is not anything, once: no harm in him. Al-Fallas said: weak and he had bad memory, and he is from the people of truthfulness. Ibn al-Madini, al-Juzjani, Ibn 'Ammar, and Muslim said: weak. Al-'Ijli said: his hadith is written but not strong. Al-Bukhari said: he is according to them lenient. And whoever contemplates the sayings of these imams finds that they spoke about him from the aspect of memory, not from the aspect of justice. Therefore his hadith is capable of elevation when supported by follow-ups (mutaba'at) and witnesses (shawahid). And he is followed in his narration from Qays as is known from the detail of these chains. It was narrated by 'Abd al-Razzaq, Ahmad, Ibn Majah, al-Daraqutni, Ibn al-Jarud, and al-Tabarani in al-Kabir, through chains from Muhammad bin Jabir, from Qays bin Talq, from his father, with it. And Muhammad bin Jabir: he is Ibn Sayyar al-Suhaymi al-Hanafi al-Darir, weak, declared weak by more than one of the imams. And it was narrated by Ibn 'Adi from the path of 'Abd al-Hamid bin Ja'far, from Ayyub bin Muhammad al-'Ijli, from Qays bin Talq, from his father, with it. And 'Abd al-Hamid bin Ja'far and Ayyub bin Muhammad, both are spoken about. And if we combine these chains together, the hadith rises to the level of proof (hujjah), despite the fact that the first path by itself is a standing proof. As for what is transmitted from the two memorizers Abu Hatim and Abu Zur'a al-Raziyan of their weakening this hadith, the one who contemplates the form of the question finds that they did not generalize the ruling. For Ibn Abi Hatim said: I asked my father and Abu Zur'a about a hadith narrated by Muhammad bin Jabir, from Qays bin Talq, from his father, that he asked the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace: 'Is there wudu from touching the penis?' He said: 'No.' So they did not affirm it, and they said: Qays bin Talq is not one whose proof stands, and they declared him mistaken. So the question is restricted to the path of Muhammad bin Jabir, and he is weak by agreement, and there is no argument that he is weak when alone. So what about three other paths, one of which is a proof if alone? And as for their criticism of Qays bin Talq, none of the critics agreed with them. And the discussion about him has preceded. And indeed the memorizer 'Abd al-Haqq al-Ishbili recorded this hadith in his 'al-Ahkam al-Wusta' without comment, which implies its authenticity according to him. Then the memorizer Ibn al-Qattan followed up saying: 'And the hadith...'
Source pages p. 210

Commentary
This passage is a detailed textual analysis of a hadith regarding whether touching the penis necessitates wudu. The author examines multiple chains of transmission to demonstrate that despite individual weaknesses, the hadith as a whole is strong enough to be used as legal proof (hujjah). The discussion begins by listing narrators and their evaluations, focusing on Ayyub bin 'Utbah, who is criticized for memory issues but not for untruthfulness. The author argues that such narrators can be elevated if their hadith is supported by mutaba'at (follow-ups) and shawahid (witnesses). Then three chains are presented: one via Ayyub bin 'Utbah from Qays bin Talq, another via Muhammad bin Jabir (who is weak), and a third via 'Abd al-Hamid bin Ja'far and Ayyub bin Muhammad. Combining these, the hadith reaches the level of being hujjah. The author also refutes the criticism of Abu Hatim and Abu Zur'a by noting that their weakening was specifically about the chain of Muhammad bin Jabir, not all chains. Furthermore, their criticism of Qays bin Talq is isolated, and the hadith was accepted by later scholars like 'Abd al-Haqq al-Ishbili. This methodological discussion shows how a hadith with multiple weak chains can be deemed acceptable for legal inference in Hanafi usul al-fiqh.

Key Terms
متابعات (mutāba‘āt): Supporting chains that share the same narrator but come through different lines.
شواهد (shawāhid): Witnessing reports from other Companions that support the meaning.
الحجة (al-ḥujjah): A proof that is sufficient for establishing a legal ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the main reason the hadith about touching the penis and wudu is considered acceptable as proof?
A) It has a single authentic chain via Muhammad bin Jabir.
B) It is supported by multiple chains that collectively strengthen it.
C) All narrators in the chains are considered trustworthy by consensus.
D) The hadith is explicitly mentioned in the Quran.

Key Takeaway
A hadith with multiple weak chains can become a proof (hujjah) in Hanafi usul if the weaknesses are in memory and not justice, and if the chains collectively corroborate.

Defending the Hadith of Talq: Chain Authentication and Refutation of Criticism
Defending the hadith of Talq against criticism

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the usul method of combining weak chains (turuq) to elevate a hadith to the level of proof (hujja) and evaluate criticisms of narrators by pinpointing their scope.

Core Idea
A hadith elevated by multiple supporting chains becomes a proof, even if one chain is weak.

When a hadith is narrated through multiple chains, its strength is not determined by the weakest link alone. In this passage, the author defends the hadith of Talq—which states that touching the penis does not require wudu—by showing that although one chain contains a weak narrator (Muhammad bin Jabir), the hadith is supported by several other chains, one of which is independently sound. He also refutes the criticism of two hadith masters (Abu Hatim and Abu Zur'a) by demonstrating that their critique was limited to that specific weak chain, not to the hadith as a whole. Understanding this method is crucial for evaluating how Hanafi usul uses multiple narrations to establish a reliable proof.

Guided Path
1
Identify the target hadith and its basic chains
First, note that the author discusses the hadith of Talq. Identify that the initial chain is through Muhammad bin Jabir (weak), but two other chains are mentioned (via Abd al-Hamid bin Ja'far and Ayyub bin Muhammad, both criticized). Also, the author later lists eight Companions who narrated the hadith, showing it is not a khabar ahad.
The key is to see the author's strategy: starting from a weak chain, then building up to multiple chains.
2
Understand the principle of combining chains (turuq)
The author argues that when weak chains are combined, the hadith rises to the level of being a proof (hujja). This is a Hanafi usul principle: multiple weak chains can support each other to reach a degree of acceptability, especially if at least one chain is strong.
This is distinct from the Shafi'i approach, which often requires each chain to be sound independently.
3
Analyze the criticism of Abu Hatim and Abu Zur'a
The author notes that these two imams weakened the hadith. But the author points out that their criticism was specifically about the narration via Muhammad bin Jabir, not the hadith in general. The question they were asked was restricted to that path.
This shows the importance of precise attribution in criticism: a narrator being weak does not automatically make every version of the hadith weak.
4
Assess the evaluation of Qays bin Talq
The critics also disparaged Qays bin Talq (a narrator in the chain), but the author argues that no other critic agreed with them. This is a common pattern: a narrator may be acceptable if only a few critics object.
In Hanafi usul, the reliability of a narrator is established by the majority of critics, not by isolated negative opinions.
5
Refute the claim that it is a khabar ahad
The author counters the argument that the hadith is a solitary (ahad) narration by listing eight Companions who narrated it. This demonstrates that the hadith is widely transmitted, strengthening its authority.
The more companions narrating a hadith, the closer it is to tawatur, but here it is used to refute the claim of being a weak ahad report.

وأما غمزهما لقيس بن طلق، فَلَمْ يوافقهما عَلَيْهِ أحد من النقاد، وَقَد تقدم الكلام عَنْهُ عَلَى أَن الحَافِظ عَبْد الحق الإشبيلي () أورد هَذَا الْحَدِيث في أحكامه الوسطى ساكتاً عَنْهُ وَهُوَ يقتضي صحته عنده. فتعقبه الحافظ ابن القطان قائلاً: «والحديث مختلف فيه، فينبغي أن يقال فيه: حسن». فهذا أقل أحوال الْحَدِيْثِ، وَإلا فَهُوَ صَحِيح. أما الفصل الثاني / الاختلاف في الْمَتْنِ وجه التوفيق بَيْنَ حديثي بسرة وطلق فسيأتي فيما بعد. وأما الثالثة: فادعاء أنَّهُ خبر آحاد ادعاء منقوض فالحديث مروي ثمانية من الصَّحَابَة هم: ١. عَبْد الله بن عمرو: أخرجه أحمد (۳)، وابن الجارود، والطحاوي (٤) والدارقطني () والبيهقي، والحازمي، من طريق عَمْرو بن شعيب، عن أبيه، عن جده. نقل التِّرْمِذِيّ عن البُخَارِي أَنَّهُ قَالَ: حَدِيث عَبْد الله بن عَمْرو في مس الذكر، هُوَ عندي صحيح. ۲. زید بن خالد الجهني: رَوَاهُ ابن أبي شيبة، وأحمد (١)، والطحاوي (۱۱)، والبزار (۱۳)، والطبراني (١٣)، وابن عدي (۱۳)، ۳. عبد الله بن عمر بن الخطاب عِنْدَ الدَّارَ قُطني (۱۹)، وفي إسناده: عبد الله بن عمر العمري ضعيف. وأخرجه أيضاً: الطحاوي (۱۷) والبزار (۱۸) والطبراني (۱۹). وفي إسناد الطحاوي والبزار صدقة بن عَبْد الله ضعيف (۲)، وهاشم بن زيد أيضاً (٢١). أما الطبراني ففي إسناده العلاء بن سليمان الرقي، ضعيف جداً (٢٢).
Chapter Two / Disagreement in the Text: From Qays bin Talq, from his father, from him. Muhammad bin Jabir: he is Ibn Sayyar al-Sahimi al-Hanafi al-Darir, weak, declared weak by more than one of the imams (1). Ibn Adi narrated it via Abd al-Hamid bin Ja'far (3), from Ayyub bin Muhammad al-Ijli, from Qays bin Talq, from his father, from him. And Abd al-Hamid bin Ja'far and Ayyub bin Muhammad, both are criticized. And if we combine these chains together, the hadith rises to the level of being a proof, even though the first chain alone is an established proof. As for what was transmitted from the two memorizers Abu Hatim and Abu Zur'a al-Raziyan of their weakening of this hadith, the one who ponders the form of the question finds that they did not make a general ruling. For Ibn Abi Hatim said: I asked my father and Abu Zur'a about a hadith narrated by Muhammad bin Jabir, from Qays bin Talq, from his father, that he asked the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him): 'Is there wudu from touching the penis?' He said: 'No.' So they did not confirm it, and they said: Qays bin Talq is not one by whom the proof is established, and they considered him deluded. So the question is restricted to the path of Muhammad bin Jabir, and he is weak by agreement, and there is no dispute that he is weak when alone. So how about three other paths, one of which is a proof if it stood alone! As for their disparagement of Qays bin Talq, no critic agreed with them on it, and the discussion about him has preceded. Source pages p. 211

Commentary
This passage is a detailed hadith analysis defending the authenticity of the hadith of Talq, which states that touching the penis does not require wudu. The author begins by discussing the chain through Muhammad bin Jabir, who is weak, but then points out that there are three other chains, one of which is strong on its own. When combined, the hadith becomes an acceptable proof. The criticism from Abu Hatim and Abu Zur'a is shown to be specific to the weak chain of Muhammad bin Jabir, not to the hadith itself. Their disparagement of Qays bin Talq is not supported by other critics. The author cites authorities like al-Hafiz Abd al-Haqq al-Ishbili and Ibn al-Qattan who consider the hadith at least hasan if not sahih. The passage then refutes the claim that the hadith is a khabar ahad by listing eight Companions who narrated it, thereby showing it is well-known. The author provides examples of three Companions: Abdullah bin Amr (whose version al-Bukhari considered sahih), Zayd bin Khalid al-Juhani, and Abdullah bin Umar (whose chain has some weak narrators). The overall aim is to establish the strength of the hadith of Talq as evidence for the Hanafi ruling that wudu is not broken by touching the penis.

Key Terms
خبر آحاد (khabar ahad): A hadith narrated by a limited number of chains, not reaching mutawatir. The author argues this hadith is not ahad because it is narrated by eight Companions.
حجة (hujja): A proof that can be used to derive a ruling. The author says the hadith reaches the level of hujja due to multiple chains.
ضعيف (da'if): A hadith or narrator that does not meet the criteria for authenticity. Used here for Muhammad bin Jabir and some other narrators.

A hadith strengthened by multiple chains, even if some are weak, can become a valid proof (hujja) in Hanafi usul, as demonstrated by the defense of the hadith of Talq.

Strengthening a Hadith Through Multiple Chains: The Case of مس الذكر
Textual analysis of a hadith through multiple chains to evaluate strength

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate the strength of a hadith by identifying multiple chains (turuq) and applying the Hanafi principle of taqwiya (strengthening) through mutaba'at and shawahid.

Core Idea
A hadith becomes strong (qawi) when multiple chains corroborate it, even if some chains contain weak narrators.

This passage examines a specific hadith that some critics claimed was a weak solitary report (khabar ahad). The author, a Hanafi usuli, refutes this by listing multiple Companion narrators and their chains, showing that the collective strength elevates the hadith to a level sufficient for legal evidence. Understanding this methodology—how weak chains can be compensated by multiplicity—is essential for evaluating hadith in Hanafi usul al-fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the objection being refuted
Read the opening lines: the claim that the hadith is a khabar ahad (solitary report) and therefore weak. The author calls this claim 'refuted.'
The objection is that a single-chain hadith lacks certainty (zanni) and is not strong enough for obliging wudu.
2
List the Companion narrators
The author names eight Companions. The passage details four: Abdullah ibn Amr, Zayd ibn Khalid, Abdullah ibn Umar, and Abu Huraira. Count them and note that the multiplicity negates the 'solitary' label.
Even if some chains are weak, the presence of multiple Companions shows the hadith is not isolated.
3
Examine the chains for each narrator
For each Companion, the author cites narrators and their grades. Note the weak narrators (e.g., Abdullah ibn Umar al-Amri, Sadaqa ibn Abdullah, al-Ala ibn Sulayman al-Raqqi). Understand that the author acknowledges weaknesses but does not dismiss the hadith.
The focus is not on individual strength but on the cumulative effect.
4
Understand the strengthening principle
Read the key sentence: 'From the totality of these chains, the hadith is strengthened.' This is the Hanafi principle that multiple chains (turuq) can lift a hadith from weak to strong, even if each alone is weak.
This principle is called taqwiya bi al-turuq (strengthening through chains). It relies on the concept of mutaba'at (follow-ups) and shawahid (supporting evidence).
5
Apply to the Abu Huraira version
The author cites a full wording of Abu Huraira's hadith and notes that despite a weak narrator (Yazid ibn Abd al-Malik al-Nawfali), a stronger narrator (Nafi ibn Abi Nu'aym) supports him. This is a mutaba'ah that strengthens the hadith.
Ibn Hibban's comment shows the Hanafi reliance on stronger narrators within the multiplicity.

As for the second chapter / Differences in the Text. The method of reconciliation between the hadith of Busra and the hadith of Talq will come later. As for the third [claim]: the assertion that it is a solitary hadith (khabar ahad) is refuted because the hadith is narrated by eight Companions: 1. Abdullah ibn Amr: Ahmad (3), Ibn al-Jarud, al-Tahawi (4), al-Daraqutni, al-Bayhaqi, and al-Hazimi narrated it from the chain of Amr ibn Shu'ayb, from his father, from his grandfather. Al-Tirmidhi narrated from al-Bukhari that he said: 'The hadith of Abdullah ibn Amr about touching the penis is, in my view, authentic.' 2. Zayd ibn Khalid al-Juhani: Ibn Abi Shayba, Ahmad (1), al-Tahawi (11), al-Bazzar (13), al-Tabarani (13), and Ibn Adi (13) narrated it. 3. Abdullah ibn Umar ibn al-Khattab: al-Daraqutni (19) narrated it, and in its chain is Abdullah ibn Umar al-Amri who is weak. Also al-Tahawi (17), al-Bazzar (18), and al-Tabarani (19) narrated it. In the chain of al-Tahawi and al-Bazzar there is Sadaqa ibn Abdullah who is weak (2), and Hashim ibn Zayd also (21). As for al-Tabarani, in its chain is al-Ala' ibn Sulayman al-Raqqi, very weak (22). [Footnotes:] ... And al-Hakim narrated it (1) and in its chain is Abd al-Aziz ibn Aban, who is accused of lying. Ibn Adi narrated it (3) and in it also is al-Ala' ibn Sulayman al-Raqqi. And it was also narrated (4) and in it is Ayyub ibn Utba, whose condition has been mentioned earlier, and Abdullah ibn Abi Ja'far (5). From the totality of these chains, the hadith is strengthened. 4. Abu Huraira: with the wording: 'If one of you touches his private part with his hand, such that there is no barrier or covering between them, let him perform wudu as for prayer.' Al-Shafi'i, al-Bazzar, al-Tahawi, Ibn Hibban, al-Tabarani, Ibn al-Sakan, Ahmad, al-Daraqutni, al-Bayhaqi, al-Baghawi, al-Hakim, and al-Hazimi narrated it. And it is a strong hadith. Yazid ibn Abd al-Malik al-Nawfali (18) is followed in his narration by Nafi' ibn Abi Nu'aym. Ibn Hibban said: 'Our argument from this report is based on Nafi' ibn Abi Nu'aym, not on Yazid ibn Abd al-Malik al-Nawfali' (19).
Source pages p. 212

Commentary
This passage is a textual analysis of the hadith concerning the obligation of wudu after touching the private parts (مس الذكر). The author, a Hanafi scholar, addresses differences in the text (متن) of the hadith and refutes the claim that it is merely a solitary report (خبر آحاد) by showing that it was narrated by multiple Companions. He lists four narrators: Abdullah ibn Amr, Zayd ibn Khalid al-Juhani, Abdullah ibn Umar, and Abu Huraira. For each, he examines the chains, noting weaknesses and strengths. The hadith of Abu Huraira is given in full: 'If one of you touches his private part with his hand, such that there is no barrier or covering between them, let him perform wudu as for prayer.' The author concludes that despite individual weak narrators, the collective strength of multiple chains (طرق) makes the hadith strong (قوي) and usable as evidence. This is a standard Hanafi methodology: a hadith can be elevated from weak to strong if it has multiple corroborating chains (mutaba'at and shawahid). The passage demonstrates how fiqh rulings (here, wudu after touching) are derived from hadith after careful evaluation of their authenticity.

Key Terms
خبر آحاد (khabar ahad): A hadith narrated by only one or two chains at each level, which gives it presumptive (zanni) rank in both transmission and evidence.
متن (matn): The text of the hadith, as opposed to the chain (sanad). Differences in the matn refer to variations in wording.
طريق (tariq): A chain of narration for a hadith. Multiple turuq strengthen a hadith even if some are weak.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the main argument in the passage against the claim that the hadith of touching the private part is a weak solitary report?
A) The hadith is present in Sahih al-Bukhari.
B) The hadith is narrated by eight Companions and has multiple chains, so it is strengthened.
C) The hadith is mutawatir because it is narrated by many.
D) The hadith has a single very strong chain that overrides all others.

Key Takeaway
A hadith with multiple chains (turuq) is strengthened to a reliable level even if some chains individually are weak, as demonstrated by the analysis of the hadith of touching the private part.

Strengthening Hadith through Multiple Chains (Taqwiyah)
Analyzing multiple hadith chains for the same ruling

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle of taqwiyah by identifying multiple weak chains (turuq) and evaluating their collective probative value for a hadith.

Core Idea
Multiple weak chains can collectively strengthen a hadith to an acceptable level for legal proof in Hanafi usul.

In Hanafi usul, a hadith is not necessarily discarded because its chain contains a weak narrator. This lesson examines how classical scholars relied on multiple transmission paths to strengthen the hadith on wudu after touching the private parts. By analyzing the chains reported from Abu Hurayra, Aisha, and Umm Habiba, you will see how the principle of taqwiyah (strengthening) operates in practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the primary hadith and its original chain
Locate the Abu Hurayra hadith with the wording commanding wudu. Note the weak link: Yazid ibn Abd al-Malik al-Nawfali, who is unanimously considered weak.
Weak narrators: عبد العزيز بن أبان (abandoned), العلاء بن سليمان الرقي, أيوب بن عتبة.
2
List the alternative chains and narrators
Note the chains from Abu Hurayra via Nafi' ibn Abi Nu'aym (reliable) and from Aisha and Umm Habiba. Each chain has its own weakness, but collectively they support the same text.
Ibn Hibban says: 'Our argument is based on Nafi' ibn Abi Nu'aym, not Yazid.'
3
Apply the principle of taqwiyah
Explain that the multiplicity of chains, even if some are weak, can elevate the hadith to the level of 'qawi' (strong) or 'hasan li ghayrihi'. This is a recognized mechanism in Hanafi usul.
The passage states: 'From the totality of these paths, the hadith is strengthened.'
4
Assess the final status of the hadith
Conclude that the hadith is now considered strong enough to be used as legal evidence for the obligation of wudu after touching private parts.
The Hanafi position: wudu is obligatory, based on this and other evidence.
5
Note the criticism of the Umm Habiba chain
Al-Bukhari noted a break between Makhul and Anbasa. This does not undermine the overall strength because the hadith is supported by other chains.
This shows that not all alternative chains are strong, but the overall mass is sufficient.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفصل الثاني / الاختلاف في المتن
ورواه الحاكم وفي إسناده عبد العزيز بن أبان، متروك متهم ورواه ابن عدي وفيه أيضاً: العلاء بن سليمان الرقي.
ورواه أيضاً وفيه: أيوب بن عتبة، وَقَدْ تقدم بَيَان حاله، وعبد الله بن أبي جعفر.
ومن مجموع هَذِهِ الطرق يتقوى الْحَدِيث.
٤. أبو هُرَيْرَةَ: بلفظ: «إذا أفضى أحدكم بيده إِلَى فرجه، حَتَّى لا يَكُوْن بينه حجاب ولا ستر فليتوضأ وضوءه للصلاة».
أخرجه الشَّافِعِي، والبزار، والطحاوي، وابن حبان، والطبراني، وابن السكن، وأحمد، والدارقطني، والبيهقي، والبغوي، والحاكم، والحازمي.
وَهُوَ حَدِيْث قوي، تابع يزيد بن عَبْد الملك النوفلي عَلَى روايته نافع بن أبي نعيم قال ابن حبان: احتجاجنا في هذا الخبر بنافع بن أبي نعيم دُونَ يزيد بن عبد الملك النوفلي.
قَالَ ابن عَبْد البر: «كَانَ هَذَا الْحَدِيث لا يعرف إلا ليزيد بن عبد الملك النوفلي هَذَا، وَهُوَ مجتمع عَلَى ضعفه، حَتَّى رَوَاهُ عَبْد الرَّحْمن بن القاسم - صاحب مالك عن نافع بن أبي نعيم القارئ، وَهُوَ إسناد صالح - إن شاء الله -، وَقَدْ أَثنى ابن مَعِينٍ عَلَى عَبْد الرَّحْمن بن القاسم في حديثه ووثقه، وَكَانَ النسائي يثني عَلَيْهِ أيضاً في نقله مالك لحديثه، ولا أعلمهم يختلفون في ثقته، وَلَمْ يروِ هَذَا الْحَدِيْثِ عَنْهُ، نافع بن أبي نعيم ويزيد بن عبد الملك إلا أصبغ بن الفرج».
٥. أم المؤمنين عَائِشَة مرفوعاً: ولفظ حديثها ويل للذين يمسون فروجهم ثُمَّ يصلون ولا يتوضئون». رَوَاهُ الطحاوي والبزار والدارقطني واللفظ لَهُ.
٦. أم المؤمنين أم حبيبة مرفوعاً: ولفظه: «من مس ذكره فليتوضأ».
رَوَاهُ ابن أبي شيبة، وابن ماجه، والترمذي، والطحاوي، وأبو يعلى، والطبراني، والبيهقي، وابن عبد البر من طرق عن مكحول، عن عنبسة بن أبي سُفْيَان، عن أم حبيبة، بِهِ. ونقل التِرْمِذِيّ عن البُخَارِيّ أَنَّهُ قَالَ: «مكحول لم يسمع من عنبسة».
Chapter Two / Variation in the Text. And al-Hakim narrated it, and in his chain is Abd al-Aziz ibn Aban, abandoned and accused; and Ibn Adi narrated it, and in it also: al-Ala ibn Sulayman al-Raqi. And it was also narrated, and in it: Ayyub ibn Utba, and his condition has preceded, and Abdullah ibn Abi Ja'far. From the totality of these paths, the hadith is strengthened. 4. Abu Hurayra: with the wording: 'If one of you puts his hand to his private part until there is no veil or covering between them, let him perform ablution as for prayer.' Ash-Shafi'i, al-Bazzar, al-Tahawi, Ibn Hibban, al-Tabarani, Ibn al-Sakan, Ahmad, al-Daraqutni, al-Bayhaqi, al-Baghawi, al-Hakim, and al-Hazimi narrated it. And it is a strong hadith; Yazid ibn Abd al-Malik al-Nawfali was followed in his narration by Nafi' ibn Abi Nu'aym. Ibn Hibban said: 'Our argument in this report is based on Nafi' ibn Abi Nu'aym, not Yazid ibn Abd al-Malik al-Nawfali.' Ibn Abd al-Barr said: 'This hadith was only known from Yazid ibn Abd al-Malik al-Nawfali, and he is unanimously considered weak, until Abd al-Rahman ibn al-Qasim - the companion of Malik - narrated it from Nafi' ibn Abi Nu'aym al-Qari, and it is a sound chain - if Allah wills - and Ibn Ma'in praised Abd al-Rahman ibn al-Qasim for his hadith and declared him trustworthy, and al-Nasa'i also praised him in his transmission of Malik's hadith, and I do not know them to differ on his reliability, and this hadith was not narrated from him - Nafi' ibn Abi Nu'aym and Yazid ibn Abd al-Malik - except by Asbagh ibn al-Faraj.' 5. Umm al-Mu'minin A'isha as a marfu' hadith: the wording of her hadith: 'Woe to those who touch their private parts then pray without performing ablution.' Al-Tahawi, al-Bazzar, and al-Daraqutni narrated it - the wording is his. 6. Umm al-Mu'minin Umm Habiba as a marfu' hadith: its wording: 'Whoever touches his penis should perform ablution.' Ibn Abi Shayba, Ibn Maja, al-Tirmidhi, al-Tahawi, Abu Ya'la, al-Tabarani, al-Bayhaqi, and Ibn Abd al-Barr narrated it via multiple paths from Makhul, from Anbasa ibn Abi Sufyan, from Umm Habiba. And al-Tirmidhi reported from al-Bukhari that he said: 'Makhul did not hear from Anbasa.'
Source pages p. 213

Commentary
This passage is a textual analysis of hadiths concerning the obligation of ablution (wudu) after touching the private parts. The author first discusses the chain of the hadith from Abu Hurayra, noting that although individual narrators like Abd al-Aziz ibn Aban and al-Ala ibn Sulayman are weak or accused, the multiplicity of chains strengthens the hadith to the level of 'hasan li ghayrihi' or 'qawi'. The conclusion 'From the totality of these paths, the hadith is strengthened' is a key principle in hadith criticism: multiple weak chains can collectively elevate a narration. The author then cites Ibn Hibban and Ibn Abd al-Barr to show that despite the weakness of Yazid ibn Abd al-Malik, the hadith is supported by a different chain through Nafi' ibn Abi Nu'aym, who is reliable. The passage then presents two additional corroborating hadiths: one from Aisha with strong wording against those who pray without ablution, and another from Umm Habiba with a direct command. However, the chain of the Umm Habiba hadith is criticized by al-Bukhari due to a break (Makhul not hearing from Anbasa). Overall, the author demonstrates how textual variants and chain analysis impact the strength of a legal proof in Hanafi usul.

Key Terms
حَدِيْث قوي (Hadith qawi): A hadith that has multiple chains of transmission that collectively make it reliable, even if some individual chains are weak.
إسناد صالح (Isnad salih): A chain of transmission that is acceptable, though not necessarily at the highest level of authenticity, often due to the reliability of its narrators.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The narrator Nafi' ibn Abi Nu'aym was weak.
B) The hadith was only known from Yazid ibn Abd al-Malik, who was unanimously considered weak.
C) The hadith had a broken chain (mursal).
D) The text of the hadith was contradictory to the Quran.

Key Takeaway
Multiple weak chains can collectively strengthen a hadith to an acceptable level for legal proof in Hanafi usul, as demonstrated by the hadith on wudu after touching private parts.

Analyzing the Hadith of Touching Private Parts and Wudu
Presentation of a hadith text and its narrators for textual analysis.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the textual features of this hadith (marfu', wording, chain) and apply the Hanafi usul principle that ahad hadith with zanni thubut and dalala can be overridden by other evidences such as istihsan.

Core Idea
A single ahad hadith does not establish a ruling if its chain and meaning are contested; the Hanafi school prioritizes stronger proofs.

This lesson examines the hadith reported by Aisha (ra) concerning wudu after touching private parts. We will parse the text, identify its chain and wording, and then see how the Hanafi school treats such ahad hadith in the presence of conflicting evidence. The passage is a classic example of textual analysis: understanding the literal wording is only the first step; the usul framework determines its legal weight.

Guided Path
1
Identify the source and its transmission
The hadith is attributed to Aisha, marfu'an (raised to the Prophet). Narrated by al-Tahawi, al-Bazzar, al-Daraqutni. Note: the wording is from al-Daraqutni.
Chain is not mutawatir.
2
Parse the key phrases
Identify the operative phrases: يمسون (touch), فروجهم (private parts), يصلون (pray), ولا يتوضئون (do not perform wudu).
3
Classify the hadith in usul
It is ahad (khabar al-wahid) because not mutawatir. Thubut is zanni (chain not mass-transmitted). Dalala is zanni because the imperative form may indicate obligation or threat, and there is ikhtilaf in interpretation.
Ahad hadith with zanni thubut and dalala.
4
Apply Hanafi principle
According to Hanafi usul, ahad hadith with zanni dalala can be overridden by stronger proofs like Qur'an, mutawatir, or istihsan. Here, the school does not take this hadith as obligating wudu; they interpret it as a warning about impurity or a recommendation.
Istihsan is the key override.
5
Contrast with other schools
The Shafi'i school uses this hadith as evidence that touching private parts nullifies wudu. Identify the difference in usul approach: they treat the literal meaning as carrying wujub, while Hanafi consider it overridden.
Resulting in different fiqh rulings.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أم المؤمنين عَائِشَة مرفوعاً: ولفظ حديثها ويل للذين يمسون فروجهم ثُمَّ يصلون ولا يتوضئون». رَوَاهُ الطحاوي والبزار والدارقطني واللفظ لَهُ.
Mother of the Believers Aisha, raised (to the Prophet): The wording of her hadith: 'Woe to those who touch their private parts then pray and do not perform wudu.' Narrated by al-Tahawi, al-Bazzar, and al-Daraqutni, and the wording is his.
Source pages p. 214

Commentary
This passage presents a hadith from Aisha (may Allah be pleased with her) concerning the obligation of wudu after touching the private parts. The wording is 'Woe to those who touch their private parts then pray without performing wudu.' The author cites the narrators: al-Tahawi, al-Bazzar, and al-Daraqutni, noting that the wording is from al-Daraqutni. This hadith is used as evidence by scholars who hold that touching the private parts nullifies wudu. However, the Hanafi school does not consider touching the private parts to break wudu, and they may interpret this hadith as a warning for those who do not wash their hands before prayer or as a recommendation. The passage simply presents the text without commentary, leaving the chain and textual differences to be analyzed.

Key Terms
مرفوعاً (marfu'an): A hadith attributed directly to the Prophet Muhammad.
فروجهم (furujahum): Private parts (plural of farj).
ويل (wayl): Woe, a term of warning and severe displeasure.
يمس (yamassu): He touches (from mass).
يتوضأ (yatawadda'u): He performs wudu (ritual washing).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi usul analysis of Aisha's hadith, why does the school not consider touching private parts to break wudu?
A) The hadith is weak in chain
B) The hadith is overridden by istihsan and other evidences
C) The hadith has a different meaning
D) The hadith is not authentic

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi usul principle that ahad hadith with zanni dalala can be overridden by istihsan leads to a different ruling than the apparent meaning of the text.
